*** FOLLOW-UP — VALIDATION CANDIDATES ENGINE + AUDIT TRUTHFULNESS FIX —
2026-07-08 — RESTART: N/A (additive function + escalation text + audit script),
DEPLOY: N/A, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
CONTEXT: user observed the INVALIDATION CANDIDATES ENGINE gives Chev a polished
"where this thesis dies" list, but nothing symmetric for "where it wins" — the
reward-side math (Opportunity.target_price, structural_rr, reward_profile) was

escalation text only surfaced a half-finished "ZONE ALIGNMENT CHECK." While
verifying, the audit script was found to be self-contradictory (see fix #4).
WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. engines.py — added ValidationCandidate dataclass + compute_validation_candidates()
   + format_validation_candidates_for_chev(): the exact reward-side MIRROR of the
   invalidation engine (compute_invalidation_candidates / format_...). Three priced
   candidates: THESIS-TARGET (Opportunity.target_price — the measured-move target
   where the thesis completes), STRUCTURAL EXTREME (the structural extreme this move
   targets, derived from reward_profile: balance extreme / mid / fib extension),
   R:R FLOOR (entry ± 1.0×risk_distance — the minimum target that satisfies 1:1
   reward/risk, labeled "below this, not worth taking"). Pure function, no I/O, never
   modifies other engines. Verdict OK/THIN vs the 1:1 R:R floor (mirrors invalidation's
   PASS/FAIL vs noise floor). WHY: symmetry — Chev's skip discipline already required
   naming invalidation; the validation half is the other side of the same coin.
2. dexter.py — wired validation_block into the escalation message immediately after
   invalidation_block (ask_chev_to_judge, ~8226), reusing the same _near_sup/_near_res
   long/short/both logic so the two blocks always agree. Pulls target_price /
   structural_rr / reward_profile / expected_trigger / invalidation_price from
   _survey.opportunity and the structural extreme from _survey.auction (per
   reward_profile). WHY: now Chev reads named "where he wins" levels, not just "where
   he dies."
3. test_validation_candidates.py — standalone (no dexter import), 7 scenarios incl.
   direction-awareness, THIN-reward (rr<1.0), empty/"none found", dedupe of an extreme
   identical to the target, and no-stop-distance (R:R FLOOR skipped). ALL TESTS PASSED.
4. audit_context.py — FIXED a PRE-EXISTING self-contradiction: section 1 still used the
   PRE-CUT 15-25K docstring brief estimate and printed a false "OVER budget" verdict,
   while section 2 correctly reproduced the post-cut brief at 4,283 and printed "under
   14k." ALSO the audit's msg copy omitted the new validation_block, understating
   esc_tok. Fixes: removed the stale docstring total + false OVER verdict (section 1
   now defers to section 2's authoritative COMBINED TOTAL); added a validation_block
   sample, inserted it into the audit msg, and added it to the per-section inventory;
   updated the module docstring + the EXCLUDED comment that falsely claimed the brief
   "is not reproduced"; removed the stale "Bollinger Band rules still present" note
   (Bollinger was deleted from the wrapper in Task 3). WHY: a verification tool that
   prints a false OVER must not be trusted — it now tells the truth.
BENEFIT: Chev gets symmetric named validation levels (THESIS-TARGET / STRUCTURAL
EXTREME / R:R FLOOR) next to his invalidation list; the audit is internally
consistent and the budget gates are honestly proven.
VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile engines.py dexter.py audit_context.py` exit 0.
Both test suites ALL TESTS PASSED. audit_context.py now prints COMBINED TOTAL =
system_prompt 1,679 + wrapper 3,903 + brief 4,283 = 9,864 tokens (≤14,000, under by

*** FOLLOW-UP #2 — "CAN'T REACH FIREBASE" TRADES-PANEL FLAPPING FIXED —
2026-07-08 — RESTART: NO (frontend only), DEPLOY REQUIRED ***
Root cause found after ruling out everything else first: (1) fetched the live
monitor.json data directly from Firebase and ran dexter's ACTUAL
renderTradingLogs()/_updatePerfSection() against it in a sandboxed Node test —
zero exceptions, proving the rendering code itself is correct against real
data; (2) confirmed via curl the endpoint returns 200 consistently, fast, with
correct CORS headers, no rate-limiting observed externally; (3) Kev's own
screenshot was the actual smoking gun: the "LIVE (1)" badge showed the correct
open-trade count while the row content underneath showed "Can't reach
Firebase" — those two are set by the same function, meaning a recent poll had
already succeeded (that's how the badge got the right number) and a LATER,
separate 5-second poll failed and overwrote only the row content. Genuinely
intermittent, not a permanent bug — Incognito ruled out extensions.
FIX (webapp/index.html, `refreshTradingLogs()`, ~line 4167): a single failed
poll no longer blanks the display. Added `_tradingLogsFailCount`, incremented
on failure and reset on success; the "Can't reach Firebase" message now only
shows after 3 CONSECUTIVE failures (15 seconds of no data) instead of one
transient blip. Whatever is causing the occasional individual fetch to fail
(likely ordinary network jitter between the browser and Firebase, not
something in our control) is unchanged — this stops it from being visually
alarming and misleading ("is Dexter online?" when Dexter never stopped
pushing data) for a single missed cycle.
ALSO FIXED THIS SESSION (see FOLLOW-UP #1 above): the Firebase drawings-stream
`timeout=600000` → `timeout=600s` bug, which was independently confirmed fixed
(forex prices started working again after it, per Kev's own test).
VERIFICATION: `node -e` syntax check clean, `<div>` balance unchanged
(581/581). A dedicated extract-and-exec test against the real
`refreshTradingLogs()` source — 7/7 assertions: 1 and 2 consecutive failures
don't show the error, 3 consecutive failures do, and a success after failures
both resets the counter and renders the real data (not just suppresses the
error).
RESTART: NO (webapp/index.html only). DEPLOY: YES (push_dashboard.py as usual;
if viewing directly at the Cloudflare tunnel URL rather than the GitHub Pages
site, this fix is already live there without any deploy step, since Dexter
serves that file straight from disk on every request).

*** FOLLOW-UP — CONFIRMATION-RULE REVERT, STRUCTURAL READ FIELD, FIREBASE
DRAWINGS-STREAM FIX — 2026-07-08 — RESTART REQUIRED, DEPLOY REQUIRED, RE-PASTE
CHEV PROMPT: NO (net change from the forensic remediation above is zero) ***
1. REVERTED the forensic remediation's Root Cause 1/2 prompt edits in full —
   Kev has direct, lived history with this exact change (documented above at
   "THE ACTUAL ROOT CAUSE — HARDCODED CONFIRMATION FIELD," 2026-07-05): a
   confirmation-candle requirement was tried once, produced 0 POSTs across 93
   decisions in 4.5 hours (72% of skips citing "lacks confirmation"), and was
   deliberately removed rather than softened. Re-introducing any form of it —
   even the "only if you can name a concrete signal" framing this remediation
   used — repeats a mistake Kev already paid for. dexter.py's escalation
   prompt and "Chev Prompt"'s three playbooks are now byte-identical to
   before the forensic remediation touched them (verified via `git diff`).
   The two unrelated fixes from that remediation pass (the `chev_conversation`
   audit trail, and the `opened_at`/`open_ts` duration-fallback bug) were kept
   — Kev's objection was specifically to the confirmation-timing change, not
   these.
2. NEW — STRUCTURAL READ field: separate from the reverted item above, and
   deliberately NOT a timing/confirmation rule. Real, data-backed finding:
   only 14/89 real trades' reasoning mentions anything from Elliot's
   structural engine (trendline/geometry/auction/conviction vocabulary) at
   all, vs. 28/89 mentioning Dexter's indicator vocabulary — most reasoning
   is as generic as "Confluence at 0.14330 aligns trend and indicators, setup
   valid." Elliot's Opportunity output was already being computed and shown
   to Chev (the ZONE ALIGNMENT CHECK), just silently skippable. Fix: a new
   required field, STRUCTURAL READ, added to both prompt templates (dexter.py
   ~8106, ~8261) and parsed (`parse_chev_reply`, new tuple
   `("STRUCTURAL READ:", "structural_read")`), persisted to `new_trade` and
   the journal entry alongside structure_4h/invalidation/confirmation.
   Deliberately neutral wording, caught and fixed mid-design after Kev's own
   pushback: it does NOT ask Chev to justify disagreeing with Elliot (that
   would bias him toward false agreement to avoid scrutiny) — it only
   requires he state Elliot's entry zone/hypothesis/conviction as fact and
   say whether his own entry matches, differs, or wasn't influenced by it,
   with explicitly no "right" answer. No hard validation added — same
   opportunistic-parse-with-no-rejection behavior as the existing three
   fields, so a missing field doesn't break anything, same as today.
3. FIXED — Firebase drawings live-sync 400 Bad Request (webapp/index.html
   `_subscribeDrawings`, ~line 6384): the SSE stream URL had
   `timeout=600000` (bare milliseconds) instead of a valid Firebase duration
   string. Firebase's own error confirmed it exactly:
   `"timeout must contain length and unit (s/seconds/min/minutes)"`. Changed
   to `timeout=600s` (same 600-second/10-minute intent). Verified directly
   against the live Firebase REST endpoint via curl — 400 before, 200 after.
   This was firing on every symbol switch, for every visitor, the whole time.
4. IN PROGRESS — the "Can't reach Firebase" message on the live trades panel:
   confirmed the underlying `monitor.json` fetch itself returns 200 (checked
   directly by Kev in browser dev tools), so the failure is in parsing the
   response or in `renderTradingLogs()` throwing on it, not connectivity —
   the error message is misleading (the same catch block covers both the
   fetch AND the render call). Likely related: `refreshForexPrices()`'s
   primary source is `_latestFbData`, which only gets populated when this
   same fetch succeeds end-to-end — so the forex-price CORS/522 errors Kev
   also saw are probably a downstream symptom of this one root issue, not a
   separate problem (freeforexapi.com, the fallback source, also appears to
   be down independently right now per a direct curl test — real, but not
   ours to fix). Waiting on the actual browser console error at the moment
   the trades panel fails to identify the exact line.
RESTART: YES (dexter.py's escalation prompt/parser/journal fields changed).
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO — net change versus what's already pasted is zero,
since the confirmation-rule edit was fully reverted; the file is back to
byte-identical. DEPLOY SITE: YES (webapp/index.html's drawings-stream fix and
new push_dashboard.py-independent from Chev Prompt).

*** FORENSIC INVESTIGATION REMEDIATION — 2026-07-08 — RESTART REQUIRED, DEPLOY
NOT REQUIRED (no frontend changes), RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: YES ***
Directly implements Root Causes 1 and 2 plus two of the three suggested code
changes from the forensic investigation artifact ("Why Dexter/Chev Keeps Making
the Same Bad Entries"). Root Cause 3 ("stops too tight") was explicitly dropped
per Kev's own call — the data refuted it, so there was no real fix to make.
This crosses the standing "no phase talks to Chev" boundary deliberately and
with Kev's direct request — he asked for exactly this file, not a UI/backend
change that drifted into it.
WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. ROOT CAUSE 1 (entries sit on S/R with no confirmation, by design) — dexter.py's
   live escalation prompt (the BANNED SKIP LANGUAGE / ENTRY MODES block, ~8172-
   8213) and three of "Chev Prompt"'s four playbook sections (PULLBACK,
   BREAKOUT, RANGE/BALANCE) no longer flatly forbid waiting for confirmation.
   The original vague-language ban stays intact word-for-word ("lacks
   confirmation," "needs confirmation," "too early" are still banned) — what
   changed is that Chev can now SKIP or use a MODE B pending order specifically
   because he's waiting for one NAMED, checkable signal (e.g. "a 15m close back
   above 1.0490," "a rejection wick off a level with only 1 prior touch"),
   stated in REASONING with the exact price/level. An unnamed "wants more
   confirmation" is still banned exactly as before — the fix targets the gap
   between "vague stalling" and "a real, checkable reason to wait," not the
   anti-stalling intent itself.
2. ROOT CAUSE 2 (the learning loop was explicitly forbidden from ever writing
   the one rule that would fix Root Cause 1) — dexter.py's `_run_learning_session()`
   had two HARD RULE blocks (the main playbook rewrite prompt, and the loss-
   pattern-analysis prompt) that explicitly banned writing any advice to wait
   for a confirmation candle. Both replaced with a rule that allows writing a
   confirmation-related lesson ONLY if it names a specific, checkable signal
   that the actual losing trades in that batch demonstrably needed — still
   bans vague "wait for confirmation" advice with nothing to check. This means
   the playbook-rewrite mechanism (already confirmed working, not write-only)
   can now actually learn this lesson instead of being blocked from ever
   writing it down. The 4 playbook .txt files themselves were NOT hand-edited —
   they're auto-regenerated by this same function every 10 closed trades, so
   editing their current snapshot text would just get overwritten; the fix had
   to be in the code that generates them.
3. SUGGESTION — forensic audit trail — every trade's journal entry now carries
   `chev_conversation`: the complete back-and-forth that produced it (the
   assembled prompt, every hallucination/geometry/gauntlet correction sent, and
   Chev's reply at each step, ending with the final accepted reply), built from
   `_chev_messages` (which the hallucination/geometry/gauntlet-fixable-reject
   blocks already append to) plus the final `chev_response`. KNOWN LIMITATION:
   this lives only on the in-memory trade dict, not in a Sheet column (a full
   conversation can be several KB — not a sane thing to cram into a spreadsheet
   cell) — so it will NOT survive a Dexter restart while the trade is still
   open, same class of gap as the duration bug below, just not worth fixing the
   same way given the size. Still a real improvement: any trade that opens and
   closes without a restart in between (the common case for scalp/day trades)
   now has a full record.
4. EVIDENCE GAP FIX — duration computation bug (not just historical data, a live
   bug): `opened_at` is set in-memory when a trade opens but was never restored
   when trades reload from the Sheet after a restart — unlike `open_ts`, which
   IS persisted to and restored from the Sheet (same literal timestamp, just
   under a different dict key depending on code path). This is almost
   certainly why 66/88 real journal entries show `duration: "unknown"` — most
   of them likely outlived at least one restart. Fixed in both
   `_trade_duration_str()` and `_do_postmortem()` by falling back to `open_ts`
   when `opened_at` is absent, mirroring the same fallback pattern already used
   elsewhere in the file (`t.get("open_ts") or t.get("ts")`). This does NOT fix
   the 66 already-written journal entries (that data is genuinely gone) — it
   stops the bug from continuing to happen to future trades.
NOT CHANGED: Root Cause 3 (dropped per Kev — data refuted it, nothing to fix).
The two historical evidence gaps that are genuinely unrecoverable (only 5/88
trades joinable to ATR/distance shadow data; 41/88 missing `open_ts` entirely)
were left alone — both predate fields that already exist in the current code
and will keep improving on their own as new trades accumulate; there's no
retroactive fix for data that was never recorded.
VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. Source-text checks (12
assertions) confirm every old banned/hard-rule phrase is gone and every new
phrase is present, in both dexter.py and "Chev Prompt," including confirming
the original vague-language ban survived word-for-word. A dedicated
extract-and-exec test (4/4 assertions) against the real `_trade_duration_str()`
function proves the `open_ts` fallback works, preserves `opened_at` priority
when both exist, and doesn't change behavior when neither exists.
RESTART: YES (dexter.py changed — prompt text, learning-session rules, journal
audit trail, and the duration fix all only take effect on restart). RE-PASTE
CHEV PROMPT: YES (the three playbook sections changed — this is the one time
this session that's actually required, since the file itself changed). DEPLOY
SITE: NO (no frontend files touched).

*** FOLLOW-UP — PERSISTENT LEARN TAB HIGHLIGHT — 2026-07-08 — RESTART: NO,
DEPLOY REQUIRED ***
Ad-hoc fix requested directly by Kev (not a formal phase paste) after using
Phase 27's Story Time toggle: the (i) icon's deep-link highlight
(`.justJumped`, a 1.8s CSS fade) was disappearing too fast, and switching to
Story Time lost it entirely, since `_renderLearnContent()` rebuilds
`#stratLearnSections`' HTML from scratch on every mode toggle, wiping any class
on the old DOM nodes.
FIX: `.justJumped` + its `@keyframes learnJumpFlash` replaced with a persistent
`.learnPinned` class (same violet tint, no animation, no auto-removal). A new
`_pinnedLearnKey` module-level variable tracks which section is pinned, and
`_renderLearnContent()` re-applies `.learnPinned` to the matching entry on every
render (Sections list only — Concept/Tag Glossary entries aren't (i) deep-link
targets), which is what makes it survive a Definition/Story Time toggle. The
(i)-icon click handler now sets `_pinnedLearnKey` and moves the highlight
instead of flashing it; clicking the currently-pinned entry itself clears the
highlight and resets `_pinnedLearnKey` to null so a later re-render doesn't
resurrect it. Clicking a different (i) icon moves the pin (old entry unpinned,
new one pinned) rather than stacking highlights.
VERIFICATION: `node -e` syntax check clean, `<div>` balance unchanged at
581/581 (no markup added, only class-list logic changed). Dedicated JS test
against a minimal fake-DOM — 11/11 assertions: pinning on (i) click, survival
across a simulated full re-render (the exact bug being fixed), click-to-clear,
clearing correctly prevents a later re-render from resurrecting the pin, moving
the pin between two different entries un-pins the old one, and confirmed the
old `.justJumped`/`learnJumpFlash` CSS is fully gone with no leftover
references anywhere in the file.
RESTART: NO (frontend only). DEPLOY: YES (webapp/index.html changed).

*** PHASE 27 COMPLETE — STORY TIME (LEARN TAB TOGGLE) + CHARACTER RENAMES —
2026-07-08 — RESTART: NO, DEPLOY REQUIRED ***
RESTART DEXTER: NO — dexter.py was not touched at all this phase (see discovery
note below for why). DEPLOY SITE: YES (webapp/index.html changed).
DISCOVERY (STOP-CHECKED with Kev before implementing): grepped the entire site
for "Marc" and "The Guards" — zero matches anywhere (webapp/index.html,
monitor.html, dexter.py). The "Assembly Line" character-card feature these two
belong to was discovery-only in an earlier phase and was never actually built,
confirmed again here. Found `Chev Story.txt` in the repo root — a personal
narrative reference document (not part of the deployed site) that defines Marc
(the honest one — real-candle exit verification + the -3R circuit breaker) but
has no character called "The Guards" at all; that name only ever existed in an
older, unbuilt Assembly Line sketch and doesn't match this apparently-current
story's cast. "The Examiner," by contrast, IS real — it appears in actual
user-visible text today: two "(no Examiner record)" labels on the Gate
Scoreboard, plus prose inside several Learn tab tooltip/CONCEPT_GLOSSARY entries,
PLUS (importantly) inside several TAG_REGISTRY tag definitions that dexter.py
serves to the frontend. STOP-CHECK asked Kev how to handle Marc/Guards having
nothing to rename; answer: rename Examiner only this phase, skip Jax/Messi
entirely rather than inventing new display text for characters that were never
shown anywhere — Marc/Guards renames wait for a future phase if an Assembly Line
feature ever actually gets built.
IMPLEMENTATION:
1. CHARACTER_DISPLAY = { Examiner: "Mike Ross" } (webapp/index.html) — a single
   dict, easy to extend later. A new `_applyCharacterNames(text)` helper does the
   actual regex-based rewrite ("the Examiner"/"Examiner's"/bare "Examiner" — all
   forms) and is applied at RENDER TIME to every piece of Learn tab text: Section
   tooltips, Concept Glossary def/how, and — critically — the Tag Glossary's
   `definition`/`how` fields, which are fetched live from dexter.py's
   /api/tag_registry. Applying the rewrite client-side at render time (rather
   than editing the backend TAG_REGISTRY strings themselves) means the several
   "Examiner"-mentioning tag definitions in dexter.py never needed to change and
   no restart is required — this is the "registry text served from backend"
   case the phase spec flagged, resolved without touching the backend at all.
   The two literal "(no Examiner record)" Gate Scoreboard labels also route
   through CHARACTER_DISPLAY.Examiner directly. No backend identifiers, file
   names, functions, or log fields were renamed — Marc/Examiner/Guards remain
   the internal names everywhere in code; Mike Ross is a display-only rename.
2. Definition / Story Time toggle — two buttons reusing the existing `.pill`/
   `.pill.active` component (same class already used for the chart timeframe
   selector), added at the top of the Learn tab. Default Definition; the choice
   is remembered in localStorage (`chevLearnMode`) per device. Toggling re-runs
   a new `_renderLearnContent()` (extracted from the old `_ensureLearnRendered`)
   which picks Definition or Story Time text for every entry and reapplies
   `_applyCharacterNames()` either way; the tag registry fetch is cached after
   first load so toggling never re-fetches it.
3. Story Time content — original text only, no dialogue/quotes/scenes from any
   show, following the persona voice guide and Kev's own Chev Story.txt:
   - `SECTION_STORY` — all 16 section keys retold in-character (Jax for the
     real P&L/ledger sections, Mike Ross for every shadow/hypothetical section,
     Dexter for scanning/funnel/grading sections, George for the R:R/rules-over-
     time sections).
   - Each of the 6 `CONCEPT_GLOSSARY` entries gained a `story` field.
   - The 123-tag glossary got a LIGHT-TOUCH treatment per the spec's own
     instruction, not 123 bespoke paragraphs: a new `_tagStoryText(name)`
     categorizes every tag by keyword into either Dexter's voice (indicators —
     S/R, Fibonacci, RSI, EMA, Bollinger, volume/VWAP, candles, funding/OI,
     session anchors) or Elliot's voice (patterns/structure — triangles,
     wedges, flags, pennants, channels, double/triple tops, market structure),

IMPLEMENTATION:
1. dexter.py — new `SECRETS_FILE = C:\ChevTools\secrets.local` (plain key=value
   lines, gitignored, created by Kev by hand, never by code). `_load_secrets()`
   reads it once at import time; `DASHBOARD_KEY = _SECRETS.get("DASHBOARD_KEY")`.
   Missing file or missing key -> DASHBOARD_KEY is None, a loud console warning
   prints, and `require_key`-wrapped routes return 503 ("auth not configured") —
   never silently falls back to open access. `require_key(fn)` decorator compares
   the request's `X-Chev-Key` header against DASHBOARD_KEY via `hmac.compare_digest`
   (constant-time). Applied to all six mutating routes, no others touched — every
   read-only route (vitals, strategy/*, counterfactual, tag_registry, etc.) stays
   open exactly as today, per the spec's own explicit decision.
2. push_dashboard.py — GITHUB_TOKEN now read from the `GITHUB_TOKEN` env var first,
   falling back to a `GITHUB_TOKEN=` line in secrets.local; the old hardcoded
   token string is deleted from the file entirely. Missing token -> prints a clear
   message and exits without attempting the push (no crash, no silent failure).
3. .gitignore — added `secrets.local` under the CREDENTIALS section.
4. webapp/index.html — new `getDashboardKey()` (reads localStorage key
   `chevDashboardKey`; prompts once via `window.prompt` if absent, caches it).
   `_apiFetch()` now attaches `X-Chev-Key` on every call (harmless on read-only
   routes, required on the six mutating ones) and, on a 401/403 response, clears
   the stored key and calls `showNotification(...)` with a visible "key rejected"
   note before returning the response to the caller — never a silent failure.
   chev_chat's raw `fetch()` (the one caller that doesn't use `_apiFetch`) got the
   same header added directly, plus its own inline 401/403 handling that clears
   the key and pushes a chat-bubble message rather than letting `data.choices[0]`
   throw into the generic "Connection error" catch-all.
5. webapp/monitor.html — same `getDashboardKey()` helper added standalone (same
   `chevDashboardKey` localStorage key as index.html — both are served from the
   same origin by Dexter locally, so one prompt covers both pages on a given
   device). Its `forceCloseTrade()` now sends the header and, on 401/403, clears
   the key and sets the button to "Wrong key — click to retry" rather than
   reporting a generic failure.

*** PHASE 25 COMPLETE — 4-HOUR X-AXIS FOR THE TIME CHARTS — 2026-07-07 —
RESTART REQUIRED, DEPLOY REQUIRED ***
RESTART DEXTER: YES (three dexter.py routes changed). RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO. DEPLOY
SITE: YES.
DISCOVERY (STOP-CHECKED with Kev before implementing): this was bigger than "change the
aggregation" — `/api/strategy/timeseries` and the Equity Curve both fed LightweightCharts
date-only strings ("YYYY-MM-DD", the library's "business day" mode, which can only
represent a whole calendar day). Sub-day granularity requires switching every affected
series to real UNIX-timestamp time values (the library's numeric mode) plus
`timeVisible: true`. The heatmap has no charting library involved (hand-rolled divs) — its
hour math lives entirely in one place, `/api/strategy/heatmap`'s `grid[dow][hour] += 1`,
regrouped to `hour // 4` in that same single spot. Point-volume check: 30 days × 6
buckets/day = 180 — confirmed sane, no need to shrink the default window.
IMPLEMENTATION:
1. `/api/strategy/timeseries` — new `bucket_hours` param (4 default, or 24 for the old
   daily behavior; anything else falls back to 4, never crashes). Bucket key is now the
   bucket's start EPOCH (int, UTC-aligned via floor-division on the hour — both allowed
   values divide 24 evenly, so this always lands on a clean boundary: 00/04/08/12/16/20 for
   4h, just 00 for 24h) instead of a day-string; each row carries both `t` (epoch, for
   charting) and `label` (human string, for tooltips) — nothing that used to read a date
   string loses information. `threshold`/`annotations` stay event-precise (their own exact
   timestamp, never bucket-aligned) with a new `t` epoch field added alongside the existing
   `ts` string. Cache keyed on `days` AND `bucket_hours` now.
2. `/api/strategy/performance`'s `equity_curve` — switched from one point per closed trade
   to **one point per 4h bucket boundary across the account's full history** (unchanged
   scope — no new window/cap introduced, just like today's unwindowed curve). Value is the
   running balance AS OF that boundary; a bucket with no new close simply repeats the last
   known balance — this is what produces the flat segments between trades honestly, as
   real data points, with no special step-interpolation rendering mode needed on the
   frontend.
3. `/api/strategy/heatmap` — grid is now `[7][6]` (six 4-hour blocks) instead of `[7][24]`,
   via `hour_utc // 4`; response gained `block_hours: 4`. Unconditional switch, no
   parameterization (not asked for, unlike the timeseries route).
4. Frontend: all 4 affected LightweightCharts series (Equity Curve + the 3 System Over
   Time charts) switched to numeric epoch time; the System Over Time charts' shared
   `_tsBaseChartOpts()` gained `timeVisible: true` (relying on LightweightCharts' own
   adaptive tick formatter — no custom `tickMarkFormatter` written; flagged as something to
   revisit if Kev's verification finds the default labeling unclear). `_tsMarkersFor()`
   (annotation-to-chart matching) changed from exact date-string equality to
   floor-to-bucket-boundary epoch matching, parameterized by `bucketSecs` so it works for
   either bucket size. Heatmap frontend: 24 hour-label columns → 6 block-label columns
   ("00–04" … "20–24", generated from the response's own `block_hours` rather than
   hardcoded), grid CSS `repeat(24,1fr)` → `repeat(6,1fr)`.
VERIFICATION: extract-and-exec (no `import dexter`) — 20 assertions across all three
routes: bucket_hours default/24/invalid-fallback, epoch alignment (4h and 24h boundaries),
equity_curve's flat-carry-forward behavior verified with a 2-trade fixture 20h apart
(intermediate buckets correctly stay flat at the first trade's balance, never interpolate
toward the second), heatmap's `hour//4` grouping and `block_hours` field. Plus the exact
spot-check Kev's own verification step asks for: a 9-decision fixture scattered across one
calendar day produces IDENTICAL totals whether summed across six 4h buckets or read from
one 24h bucket (9 == 9) — proves no data lost or double-counted in the regroup. Frontend:
the new `_tsMarkersFor()` floor-matching logic extracted and unit-tested in isolation — 4/4
assertions (exact-boundary match, mid-bucket floor match, no-match-drops-silently,
mixed-batch ordering). `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. `node -e` syntax check clean
on both inline `<script>` blocks; `<div>` balance 580/580 (unchanged — no new markup, only
existing render logic and one CSS grid rule changed).
See 4-HOUR X-AXIS FOR THE TIME CHARTS (PHASE 25) section, right after this banner, for the
Kev verification checklist.

*** PHASE 23 COMPLETE — DATA FIXES: EMPTY SCOREBOARD + GATE SCOREBOARD N/A PILLS —
2026-07-07 — RESTART REQUIRED, DEPLOY REQUIRED ***
RESTART DEXTER: YES (new dexter.py shadow-tracking call + counterfactual_report.py join
fix). RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO. DEPLOY SITE: YES.
DIAGNOSIS (STOP-CHECKED with Kev before fixing — one hypothesis confirmed, one refuted):

*** BUG (a) — Indicator Scoreboard renders zero rows ***
Root cause is NOT a data/join bug. Ran the real `/api/tag_registry`, `/api/strategy/
performance`, and `/api/strategy/tag_trends` route bodies against the actual production
chev_journal.json (extract-and-exec) — all three work correctly and join cleanly (123
registry tags, 45 real tag_stats keys all present in the registry, 24 trend-tag keys all
present). The real bug: `loadScoreboard()` wrapped all FOUR sources (registry, performance,
counterfactual, tag_trends) in ONE shared try/catch — if any single one failed (e.g. a
not-yet-restarted Dexter still missing `/api/strategy/tag_trends` — 404 → non-JSON body →
`.json()` throws), the exception was caught at the top and `_scoreboardRows` never got
populated at all, so the ENTIRE table rendered zero rows instead of just one missing
column. Fixed: `loadScoreboard()` now uses `Promise.allSettled` and handles each of the 4
sources independently — Points/Indicator always render from the registry alone; Real WR/
Shadow WR/Trend individually degrade to "—" (with an explanatory `title`, e.g. "No closed
trades this era yet") only for whichever specific source actually failed. Only a
genuinely-failed registry fetch now produces a real empty state, with an explicit message
("Indicator registry unavailable") instead of a silently blank table.

*** BUG (b) — Gate Scoreboard "n/a" pills despite n>0 ***
The phase's own hypothesis ("the labeller stamps those labels with chev_decision POST...
if the join requires REJECT, it matches nothing") does NOT hold — verified empirically,
not just by reading code. Searched labels_open.jsonl + labels_closed.jsonl for ANY record
matching a gate-killed decision (GATE_REJECT/STRUCT_REJECT/MTF_TAX_REJECT/GEOMETRY_REJECT/
REJECT) by symbol+tf, at tolerances from 5 to 60 minutes: 5min → 0/215 matches; wider
windows do surface labels, but their chev_decision is ALWAYS NOT_ESCALATED or SKIP — never
POST, at any tolerance (almost certainly unrelated later scan cycles of the same
symbol/tf, not the killed instance itself). Code-confirmed: `labeller.record_setup(...,
"POST", ...)` was called at exactly ONE place in dexter.py — right after "Trade locked,"
i.e. only once a trade survives every gate and actually opens. A gate-killed proposal
never reached that call. Gate-kills had NO Examiner label at all, not a mislabeled one —
the existing hardcoded resolved=0/shadow_wr=None was accurate given the data, matching
that file's own passing self-test.
*** SCOPE NOTE: the real fix requires a new labeller.record_setup() call in dexter.py —
touching labeller call sites, which is on this phase's own do-not-touch list. Kev
explicitly authorized this one, narrow, well-justified exception before it was written. ***
Fixed in two places:
1. dexter.py: new `labeller.record_setup(result, asset_type, "POST", ...)` call added
   immediately after `_trade_originally_parsed` is computed — i.e. the MOMENT Chev's reply
   first parses as a valid trade, BEFORE any downstream gate (hallucination/score/struct/
   mtf-tax/geometry/gauntlet) can kill it. Uses the literal string "POST" (not a new
   decision value) because `record_setup()`'s own `is_post` check requires exactly that to
   use Chev's real entry/direction rather than the generic zone-proxy (confirmed by reading
   labeller.py — do-not-touch, read-only). record_setup()'s existing symbol+tf+entry_ref
   dedup collapses this into a no-op for the common case where the same trade later locks
   in for real (same entry price → same dedup zone → second call skipped) — nothing is
   double-counted.
2. counterfactual_report.py's `build_counterfactual()` (the shared bucketing function —
   the ONLY place this fix belongs, per the phase's own instruction): the downstream
   gate-kill block now matches each gate-killed decision to the closest "POST" label by
   symbol+tf+timestamp proximity ONLY (900s/15min window — covers deliberation + retries),
   NEVER by chev_decision (that restriction was the actual bug). Matched-and-resolved
   labels flow through the exact same `bucket_stats()`/`_add_bucket()` machinery every
   other bucket already uses (small, backward-compatible extension: `_add_bucket()` gained
   an optional `key_override` param so the bucket's public "GATE-COST_GATE"-style key can
   differ from the bare code passed to `_bucket_label()`). A decision matched to a
   still-open label, or matched to nothing at all (all historical gate-kills from before
   this fix existed), still counts as "pending" — exactly the same honest treatment this
   bucket has always given unresolved/absent data.
VERIFICATION: `counterfactual_report.py --selftest` extended with a new fixture
reproducing exactly the case the phase asked for (decision REJECT + label chev_decision
POST, matched by symbol+tf+timestamp) — proves the join now resolves real numbers
(GATE-COST_GATE: n=2, resolved=1, shadow_wr=100%, avg_r/total_r=+0.80, verdict_split
right=0/wrong=1/pending=1) while a gate-kill bucket with no matching label anywhere
(GATE-MTF_TAX) still correctly shows resolved=0/shadow_wr=None — same treatment as
always. Every existing assertion recalculated and updated where the new fixture data
shifted a total (coverage.total 7→11, coverage.resolved 6→7, headline.forfeited_r
2.00→2.80) — 51/51 self-test cases passing (up from 45). `python -m py_compile dexter.py
counterfactual_report.py risk_gauntlet.py` clean. Frontend: a standalone Node simulation

DISCOVERY (STOP-CHECKED with Kev before writing any names): tag codes turn out to come
from THREE separate vocabularies, not one — (1) `CONFLUENCE_SCORES` (dexter.py, 77 keys,
the real weights table), (2) Chev's own free-typed `tags=` field on POSTed trades (44
distinct codes observed in chev_journal.json, a superset of #1 plus 8 codes with no
weights-table match at all — spelling drift or shorthand Chev has typed that was never
formally scored), and (3) labeller.py's `normalize_reasons()` tokens (42 distinct, used
only by the PHASE 7B-3 Shadow Tag/Combo leaderboards — a differently-named vocabulary,
percentage-based Fib levels and no-underscore EMA periods instead of timeframe-based,
mostly NOT string-matching the weights table; only gp/rsi_ob/rsi_os match exactly).
Union across all three: 123 unique codes — the registry covers every one, verified by
exact set comparison against a fresh read of chev_journal.json (no code guessed that
doesn't exist). Kev confirmed the handling for the ambiguous cases: `points: null` for any
code without an exact `CONFLUENCE_SCORES` match (no aliasing between differently-spelled
versions of the same concept, e.g. `ema55` vs `ema_55` — simplest, safest, zero hand-
maintained alias table to keep in sync), and the `hd`/`rd` journal shorthand is flagged in
its own tooltip as an inferred (not confirmed) reading of "Hidden/Regular Divergence,"
since labeller.py makes that exact distinction elsewhere but Chev's two-letter codes are
never defined anywhere in code.
IMPLEMENTATION: new `TAG_REGISTRY` dict in dexter.py (ANCHOR: right after `CONFLUENCE_
SCORES`'s closing brace) — one entry per code with `name`/`tooltip`/`definition`/`how`,
written from reading the actual computing code wherever mechanics were non-obvious (e.g.
Golden Pocket is the REAL code's 50%-61.8% Fib band, not the CONFLUENCE_SCORES comment's
slightly different "0.618-0.65" phrasing; a liquidity sweep is a wick through a cluster of
equal highs/lows within ~40 candles that closes back inside; sr_multi/sr_single is a 3+-
touch threshold read straight from labeller.py's own regex). Deliberately NO `points` field
stored on the dict itself — new `GET /api/tag_registry` (300s cache; tag meanings only
change when this file is edited, never at runtime, so a long cache is safe) looks up
`points` fresh from `CONFLUENCE_SCORES` on every serve, so retuning a weight in code is
automatically reflected on the site with nothing to keep in sync by hand.
Frontend (webapp/index.html): shared `friendlyTag(code)`/`friendlyCombo(comboKey)`
helpers (comma-joined combo keys split, each piece mapped, joined with " + ") — fetch
`/api/tag_registry` once per page load via `_loadTagRegistry()` (module-level cache,
kicked off in the same init block as `loadVitals()`), unknown codes fall back to a plain
prettifier (underscores → spaces, capitalized) so a brand-new tag can never break the
page. Applied at all three Strategy-section render sites found in discovery: the Tag
Leaderboard (`#stratTagBars`), the Combo Leaderboard (`#stratComboBars`), and the single
shared `renderShadowLeaderboard()` that serves BOTH Shadow Tag and Shadow Combo boards
(PHASE 7B-3). Every row's visible label is now the friendly name; the raw code stays in
that row's `title` attribute unchanged, for cross-referencing logs. Two other tag-code
render sites were found (Chev's Corner ideas panel tag chips, the hypothetical-trade-card
component) but are OUTSIDE the Strategy section per this phase's own scope — left
untouched, flagged here for a future phase if Kev wants them covered too.

*** PHASE 14 COMPLETE — TUNABLES.JSON HOT-RELOAD — 2026-07-07 —
RESTART REQUIRED (ONCE), NO DEPLOY ***
RESTART DEXTER: YES, ONE LAST TIME for this whitelist — after this restart, every
whitelisted key below can be changed by editing `C:\ChevTools\tunables.json` and waiting
for the next scan cycle. RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO. DEPLOY SITE: NO (backend only, no
frontend this phase — that's PHASE 15).
DISCOVERY (STOP-CHECKED with Kev before implementing): all four proposed groups
(escalation thresholds — both normal AND exploration variants, `ESCALATION_TF_FLOOR`,
`HALLUCINATION_MAX_ENTRY_DIST`, exploration-profile `MIN_NET_RR`/`MAX_COST_R`/
`CONCURRENCY_CAP`) are read fresh per-cycle/per-call everywhere in the codebase — nothing
is baked into a module-level structure at import time, so nothing needed a refactor or
exclusion this phase. `_NORMAL` (risk_gauntlet.py) is deliberately, permanently
untouchable from tunables.json — Kev's own reasoning, on record: it's the "return to
discipline" baseline, and it only means something as a fixed reference point; if the
baseline itself could drift from a phone tap, "restore defaults" becomes circular. Same
reasoning excluded `ABS_MIN_RR` (hard safety backstop), `MAX_TOTAL_HEAT`/`MAX_CORR_SAME_DIR`
(account-protection gates, already on the global do-not-touch list), and `ATR_FLOOR` (feeds
the EXECUTABLE GEOMETRY coaching block, more coupling than a first-round tunable should
carry) — all live, all real, all deliberately NOT in this whitelist. Small first, expand
one key at a time later only if actually needed.
WHITELIST + BOUNDS (full comment block also lives directly above `TUNABLES_BOUNDS` in
dexter.py): `escalation_thresholds.{normal,exploration}.score.{crypto,forex,stock}` →
(1, 20); `escalation_thresholds.{normal,exploration}.max_dist_pct` → (0.1, 5.0);
`escalation_tf_floor.{crypto,forex,stock}` → must be a key in `TF_SECONDS`
(5m/15m/30m/1h/4h); `hallucination_max_entry_dist` → (0.005, 0.10);
`exploration_profile.min_net_rr.{scalp,day,swing}` → (0.5, 5.0);
`exploration_profile.max_cost_r.{scalp,day,swing}` → (0.05, 0.60);
`exploration_profile.concurrency_cap.{scalp,day,swing}` → (1, 5). `EXPLORATION_MODE`
itself stays out — it already has its own toggle path.
IMPLEMENTATION: new `load_tunables()` (dexter.py, called once per cycle at the very top of
`while True:`) reads `tunables.json`, validates every present key against
`TUNABLES_BOUNDS` (or the `TF_SECONDS` allowed-set for the TF-floor keys), applies only
in-bounds AND actually-changed values, and records every applied diff to the flight
recorder (`record_system_state("tunables_applied", "file", changed={...})`) — old/new
pairs, keyed by dotted path. File missing → silent no-op (the normal pre-tuning state).
File corrupt/unreadable, or any single value out of bounds/malformed/unknown → warned
once (not spammed every cycle) and that value's last-good (previous-cycle or hardcoded-
default) stays in force; a bad value never blocks its unrelated siblings from applying.
The three exploration-profile keys are applied through a NEW public
`risk_gauntlet.apply_exploration_overrides(updates)` — the ONLY sanctioned way to mutate
the live `_EXPLORATION` dict from outside risk_gauntlet.py, mutating in place (every
`get_active_profile()` caller holds a reference to this same object, so in-place mutation
is what makes a change visible everywhere on the very next call). Per Kev's three
conditions: (1) refuses any key outside `EXPLORATION_TUNABLE_KEYS = {MIN_NET_RR,
MAX_COST_R, CONCURRENCY_CAP}`, a second independent lock behind dexter.py's own bounds
check ("two doors, both locked"); (2) physically cannot touch `_NORMAL` — there is no
mode parameter, the function only ever references `_EXPLORATION` by name; (3) has its own
5 new cases (27–31) in risk_gauntlet.py's self-test suite (33/33 passing total, up from 26).
Initial `C:\ChevTools\tunables.json` shipped containing exactly today's hardcoded live
values (no immediate diff on first read — see behavior note below for why that's correct).
*** BEHAVIOR NOTE, on record so it isn't mistaken for a bug in a month (Kev's own words):
the mutation this file drives is IN-MEMORY ONLY. Every restart resets every value to its
hardcoded default, and the very first scan cycle after that restart reapplies
tunables.json on top. So once tunables.json's values actually differ from the hardcoded
defaults, a restart will correctly show a "startup" flight-recorder snapshot with
defaults, followed immediately by a "file" change record showing tunables.json being
reapplied — that's the system working as designed, not a double-toggle bug. ***
VERIFICATION: extract-and-exec (no `import dexter`) against a `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()`
fixture, using the REAL risk_gauntlet module — 20/20 assertions passed: missing file
(silent no-op), a valid multi-key change (dexter-level scalar + TF floor + exploration-
profile dial, all applied, exactly one flight-recorder record with correct old/new diff),
out-of-bounds values (rejected, hardcoded default kept, nothing recorded), malformed JSON
(no crash, last-good kept, warned exactly once), unknown top-level key AND unknown
trade_type inside a whitelisted group (both ignored with a warning, valid sibling keys
still applied), and a true no-op (value equal to current — not reported as a change).
`python -m py_compile dexter.py risk_gauntlet.py` clean. `python -X utf8 risk_gauntlet.py`
— 33/33 self-test cases passing.

*** HOTFIX — FILL-TIME RE-CHECK CRASH (risk_gauntlet.ATR_FLOOR AttributeError) —
2026-07-07 — RESTART REQUIRED ***
RESTART DEXTER: YES. RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO. Kev restarted Dexter after PHASE 7B-4 and
it crashed the whole process within ~30 seconds: `AttributeError: module 'risk_gauntlet'
has no attribute 'ATR_FLOOR'`, raised from check_and_update_open_trades()'s fill-time
re-validation block (dexter.py, PENDING->OPEN fill path) the moment a PENDING order with
a fetchable fresh ATR was processed. This is the exact latent bug flagged (but left
untouched, "out of scope") during PHASE 2's discovery this session — dexter.py referenced
`risk_gauntlet.ATR_FLOOR` / `.MAX_COST_R` / `.MIN_NET_RR` as flat module-level dicts, but
they only ever existed nested inside risk_gauntlet's `_NORMAL`/`_EXPLORATION` profiles,
accessed everywhere else via `risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile(EXPLORATION_MODE)`. The
ATR-floor reference wasn't wrapped in its own try/except, so it took the whole process
down; the cost/R:R reference right below it WAS wrapped, so it had been silently no-op'ing
(always hitting `except Exception` and printing "proceeding on original gauntlet pass")
instead of crashing -- fixed both in the same pass since they're the same root cause.
FIX: added `_fill_prof = risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile(EXPLORATION_MODE)` once at the
top of the fill-time re-validation block, replaced all 5 broken references with
`_fill_prof["ATR_FLOOR"]` / `_fill_prof["MAX_COST_R"]` / `_fill_prof["MIN_NET_RR"]`.
Verified: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean; extracted the exact fixed block and
exec'd it standalone (never imported dexter.py) against 3 stubbed cases -- a healthy fill
(no cancel), an ATR-floor violation at fill (cancels, as designed), and a cost-gate
violation at fill (cancels -- this path was previously unreachable due to the silent
no-op, so this is now genuinely enforcing for the first time) -- all 3 passed, no
AttributeError anywhere. Grepped the rest of dexter.py for the same pattern: every other
`risk_gauntlet.<CONSTANT>` reference (`FEE_SIDE`, `SLIPPAGE_SIDE`, `FUNDING_EST_SWING`,
`TAG_WINRATE_WINDOW_TRADES`, `TAG_WINRATE_SMOOTHING_K`) is a genuine flat, mode-independent
module constant -- confirmed no other instances of this bug exist.

malfunction — those are exactly the trades this phase exists to force a decision on. ***

only ever loaded `expiry_at` for PENDING-status rows — an OPEN trade reloaded after a
restart had NO expiry_at in memory at all, which would have silently made this whole phase
inert for exactly the trades it's meant to catch. Fixed by loading the same sheet column
for both statuses (the value doesn't change between PENDING and OPEN — it's written once
at proposal time and never rewritten at fill).

*** BASELINE — Dexter restarted + "Chev Prompt" re-pasted into Open WebUI: 2026-07-06 04:26 ***
Supersedes the 2026-07-06 03:38 baseline below (that one is now just history: Opportunity
Engine rework only, before the reasoning-specificity fix existed). Everything in the
OPPORTUNITY ENGINE REWORK section AND the REASONING SPECIFICITY FIX section (both
engines.py/dexter.py changes, live automatically on restart) plus the matching "Chev
Prompt" rewrites (manually re-pasted into Open WebUI at this same 04:26 restart) took
effect from this timestamp forward. Any chev_decisions.jsonl entries or console
escalations from BEFORE 04:26 reflect OLD behavior — don't diagnose against those.

HOW TO ACTUALLY FIND THE ANNOYING RULE NOW: every decision from 04:26 onward carries a
`detail` field (Chev's full reasoning + what was missing, required to cite a real number
now — see REASONING SPECIFICITY FIX) and a `specific` boolean (false = still vague despite
the new rule, itself worth flagging). First split by `decision` type — that alone answers
"is it Chev or Dexter":
  SKIP                                    → Chev's own judgment call. Read `detail` — it
                                             now has to name a real number, so the actual
                                             blocking condition should be visible directly.
  GATE_REJECT / STRUCT_REJECT /
  MTF_TAX_REJECT / REJECT (gauntlet)      → Dexter's own deterministic gates, not Chev —
                                             these already state real numbers by nature
                                             (e.g. "score=9.5 < threshold=10", "Net R:R
                                             after costs = 2.4 < required 3.8"). If ONE of
                                             these fires far more often than the others,
                                             or the SAME specific number/threshold shows up
                                             across many entries, that repeated one is the
                                             annoying rule to target next — not a vague
                                             feeling, a literal grep-able pattern in
                                             chev_decisions.jsonl or the Strategy
                                             Dashboard's raw log tab (now filterable/visible
                                             with the `detail` column added this pass).
If it's still mostly SKIP with `specific: false` details even after this fix, the "Chev
Prompt" re-paste likely didn't take — re-check that first, same as always.

*** EXPLORATION_MODE = True RIGHT NOW — READ THIS FIRST ***
Dexter is running live with a lowered, temporary paper-trading entry bar (confirmed live
via direct terminal read 2026-07-05 — this is not a "restart pending" state, the code
changes described in this document are actually running right now). Flipping this one
flag to False reverts score thresholds, Chev's own subjective skip conditions, AND every
setup-quality number in risk_gauntlet + GEOMETRY REVIEW at once. Full detail in THE BIG
PICTURE section (just below FILE LOCATIONS) and the dedicated EXPLORATION MODE section.

*** "Chev Prompt" STILL REQUIRES A MANUAL PASTE INTO OPEN WEBUI ***
This is the one piece of this document that is NOT automatically live just because the
file on disk is correct — Open WebUI's model system prompt field must be updated by hand
each time this file changes. Everything else described in this document (dexter.py,
risk_gauntlet.py, the playbook files) takes effect the moment Dexter restarts or, in most
cases, on the very next scan cycle. Re-pasted as of the 2026-07-06 04:26 baseline above —
if the file changes again after that, it needs re-pasting again; git diff on "Chev Prompt"
is the fast way to check whether it's drifted from what's actually live in Open WebUI.

## EVERY STANDARD LOOSENED SO CHEV ACTUALLY TAKES TRADES — CONSOLIDATED LIST (as of 2026-07-06)

This pulls every "make it easier for Chev to post" change into one place — each one lives
in its own section elsewhere in this doc with full detail; this is the map so nothing has
to be pieced together from three different sections again. If trades are still not posting
after the 2026-07-06 03:38 baseline, this is the full list of levers already pulled —
diagnosing "what haven't we loosened yet" starts here.

1. EXPLORATION_MODE (added 2026-07-04) — the master flag. One boolean in dexter.py flips
   ALL of the following at once, no partial states possible:
     - Dexter's own score threshold: crypto 10→7, forex 8→6, stock 8→6.
     - Max escalation distance from a confluence level: 0.75%→1.5%.
     - Weekend crypto threshold bump (+2): disabled entirely during exploration.
     - risk_gauntlet.py profile (NORMAL → EXPLORATION), same flag drives every number below:
         ATR_FLOOR (SL distance vs ATR):    {1.0, 1.2, 1.5} → {0.6, 0.7, 1.0}  (scalp/day/swing)
         MAX_COST_R (cost ceiling):         {0.20, 0.25, 0.30} → {0.35, 0.40, 0.45}
         MIN_NET_RR (flat R:R floor):       {2.0, 1.8, 2.5} → {1.3, 1.2, 1.6}
         ABS_MIN_RR (hard floor):           {1.1, 1.1, 1.3} → {0.8, 0.8, 1.0}
         MAX_TOTAL_HEAT (portfolio heat):   8.0 → 25.0
         MAX_CORR_SAME_DIR (correlation):   2 → 3
         CONCURRENCY_CAP:                  {1, 2, 2} → {2, 3, 3}
     - Chev's escalation prompt gains a paragraph: paper account, DEFAULT is POST if there's
       a nameable entry/stop/target, SKIP must name one concrete broken element.
     - Chev Prompt's own EXPLORATION PHASE paragraph: the four Operating-System hard-skip
       conditions (auction maturity >85%, participation <25, direction-score contradiction
       >50pts, TRANSITIONING state) become sizing/conviction inputs, not vetoes, on Dexter
       escalations only.
   Deliberately NOT loosened by this flag: STRUCT/CONFLICT pre-gates, SL-direction hard-
   rejects, stale-price/ATR-staleness checks, _setup_grade() (always grades against the FULL
   normal threshold regardless of mode — the real risk control of the whole phase).
   See: EXPLORATION MODE section.

2. Chev Prompt TRIGGER-removal rewrite (2026-07-05). Every playbook (PULLBACK, BREAKOUT,
   RANGE/BALANCE) previously required waiting for an exact "TRIGGER" — a specific candle
   close, rejection wick, or confirmation bar — before entry. Rewritten throughout to "once
   the [named structural conditions] are named and hold up — commit," removing the
   candle-by-candle waiting requirement entirely. Also removed the standalone rule "Never
   enter on a NEXT condition," and changed the B-quality Opportunity guidance from
   "demand the TRIGGER fires cleanly" to "don't wait for the TRIGGER to fire first." Applies
   to Kev's normal chat requests AND Dexter escalations (this one wasn't scoped to
   exploration only — it's a permanent persona change, not a temporary phase).

3. Opportunity Engine rework (2026-07-06 03:38 baseline — this session). Three separate
   fixes to a gate that EXPLORATION_MODE never touched at all:
     - ATR-tolerant trendline fit: ordinary wicks/fakeouts (within 0.3× ATR, capped at 30%
       of current channel width) no longer penalize pattern-fit quality.
     - Confidence formula: catastrophic floor (0.15) still disqualifies outright, but above
       that, four sub-scores blend as a weighted average instead of a strict minimum.
     - A+/A/B/C quality ladder decoupled from decision-making entirely — it's now cosmetic
       display only; Chev sizes continuously off the 0-100 confluence_score instead, and his
       prompt was rewritten to never skip solely for moderate (vs. high) conviction.
     - Added: a stated SR/Fib-vs-entry-zone proximity fact (SAME ZONE/NEARBY/DIFFERENT) so
       Chev doesn't have to re-judge alignment himself with no defined tolerance.
   See: OPPORTUNITY ENGINE REWORK section (immediately below the EXPLORATION MODE section).

NOT YET DONE (surfaced but out of scope so far): chart_drawer.py has its own independent,
un-touched copy of the same A+/A/B/C ladder for Kev's manual get_market_survey chat calls —
not part of any pass above, since it doesn't affect Dexter escalations at all.

## WHAT THIS PROJECT IS

A fully local, private AI trading terminal built for one user (Kev). Three parts:

1. CHEV CHELIOS — AI trading partner running in Open WebUI (local, private)
   Model: qwen3-vl:30b via Ollama. Personality: witty Londoner, Chelsea fan, Seinfeld
   references. Has chart analysis tools. Makes trade recommendations, NEVER executes.

2. DEXTER — Python trading bot at C:\ChevTools\dexter.py (5000+ lines, runs 24/7)
   Scans watchlist for technical confluences, escalates to Chev via Open WebUI API,
   logs trades to Google Sheets, monitors/closes positions. Also hosts the web terminal
   as a Flask server on port 8080.

3. WEB TERMINAL — C:\ChevTools\webapp\index.html
   Dark TradingView-style chart terminal. Live candles, watchlist, trade logs, Chev's
   Corner (On Radar ideas), multi-conversation Chev chat panel, drawing tools.

4. MOBILE APP — C:\ChevMonitorApp\ (React Native / Expo SDK 57)
   Android-first native app. Firebase real-time data. Tabs: Home, Trades, Jane, History.
   NOT yet installed on device — EAS Build path chosen (Expo Go incompatible with SDK 57).
   Alejandro (new collaborator) will help build this out.

================================================================================
## THE BIG PICTURE — WHAT EACH MOVING PART DOES AND WHY (added 2026-07-05)
================================================================================

Read this section first if you've lost track of how any given rule fits into the whole
system — that's exactly why it exists. It's a map, not the territory: full technical
detail on each item already lives in its own section elsewhere in this document; this is
the one-page version so you don't have to re-derive the whole pipeline from memory every
time. Written after Kev said plainly: "we have too many moving parts now that I can't
keep up" — that sentence is the reason this section exists at all.

--- THREE SEPARATE TEXTS REACH CHEV, AND THEY BEHAVE DIFFERENTLY ---

1. "Chev Prompt" (C:\ChevTools\Chev Prompt) — Chev's permanent personality + rulebook.
   Only changes Chev's real behavior once you manually copy-paste it into Open WebUI's
   model system prompt editor. Editing the FILE does nothing by itself — this has bitten
   us before (a whole rewrite sat unused for hours because this step was assumed done).

2. The escalation message (built fresh by ask_chev_to_judge() in dexter.py, every single
   time Dexter has a setup to show Chev) — the actual numbers for THIS setup: candles,
   score, SR/Fib/VP levels, the EXPLORATION note if active, the required output format.
   This is a stateless, one-shot message (confirmed 2026-07-05 — no persistent conversation
   history across escalations), so nothing said in a PAST escalation carries into this one.

3. The playbook (chev_playbook_{crypto,forex,stocks}.txt) — an auto-regenerated "lessons
   learned" file, rewritten by a background job every 10 closed trades, then PREPENDED to
   EVERY escalation message in #2 as "=== YOUR TRADING PLAYBOOK ===". This is the one most
   people forget exists — it's not something you edit directly day-to-day, it writes
   itself from Chev's own past trades, and it silently re-enters every future decision.
   (This is exactly where the "confirmation candle" language kept surviving prompt fixes
   from — see NET_RR/CONFIRMATION history in RISK GAUNTLET and the STRUCTURED REASONING
   sections. Fixed 2026-07-05, but worth remembering this file exists and self-writes.)

--- STAGE 1: DOES DEXTER EVEN BRING THIS SETUP TO CHEV? (before Chev sees anything) ---

- Confluence score — a plain number Dexter computes from SR/Fib/RSI/EMA/BB/patterns/etc.
  Nothing subjective here; it's arithmetic over engines.py's outputs.
- TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE — score must clear a threshold, set via _active_thresholds()
  (EXPLORATION_MODE-aware: crypto 10→7, forex/stock 8→6 during exploration).
- STRUCT PRE-GATE — must have a real structural anchor (SR or VP score ≥2, or a fast
  intraday anchor like prior-day H/L or opening range). NOT exploration-aware — this is
  a "don't trade thin air" hygiene check, not a setup-quality dial.
- DISTANCE gate — price can't be too far from the confluence zone. Max distance is also
  EXPLORATION-aware (0.75%→1.5%) via the same _active_thresholds() call.
- CONFLICT gate — rejects setups where bull and bear signals both fire without one
  clearly dominating. NOT exploration-aware — contradictory signals are contradictory
  regardless of how much data you're trying to collect.
- Cooldowns (skip/post cooldown per timeframe) — pure time-spacing, prevents re-escalating
  the same symbol/TF every scan cycle. Not exploration-aware, not about setup quality.

--- STAGE 2: CHEV'S OWN JUDGMENT ---

- Chev reads the escalation message (see #2 above) and decides POST or SKIP.
- Chev's Operating System skip conditions (auction maturity >85%, participation <25,
  direction-score contradiction, TRANSITIONING state) — during EXPLORATION_MODE these
  become sizing/conviction inputs, not automatic vetoes (the escalation note tells him
  this explicitly). This is the ONE place exploration mode touches Chev's own subjective
  read, as opposed to the deterministic math gates below.

--- STAGE 3: AFTER CHEV SAYS POST, BEFORE IT'S REAL ---

- SCORE GATE — re-verifies Dexter's own mechanically-computed score against the same
  threshold, so Chev can't inflate eligibility by adding unverified tags. EXPLORATION-aware
  (same _active_thresholds() call).
- STRUCT GATE — same structural-anchor check as the pre-gate, re-run after Chev's reply
  in case his proposal moved the level. NOT exploration-aware.
- MTF TAX — counter-trend trades (long vs 4H downtrend, short vs 4H uptrend) need a higher
  score bar (1.5× normal) AND a confirmed (not forming) divergence. Indirectly
  exploration-aware since the bar is 1.5× whatever _active_thresholds() currently returns.
- GEOMETRY REVIEW — an early sanity pass on Chev's actual entry/SL/TP numbers (ATR-relative
  SL distance, minimum R:R, position size vs grade cap) with ONE retry if it fails.
  UNTIL 2026-07-05 this had its OWN separate hardcoded numbers (a flat 2.0:1 R:R, its own
  ATR multiplier table) — completely disconnected from risk_gauntlet and from
  EXPLORATION_MODE. This was a real, undocumented fourth source of the "2.0:1" belief Chev
  kept citing. FIXED same day: it now calls risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile(
  EXPLORATION_MODE) and uses the EXACT same ATR floor / R:R numbers as the gauntlet below
  — one source of truth instead of two that could silently disagree.
- RISK GAUNTLET (risk_gauntlet.py, 14 gates, full detail in its own section below) — the
  real deterministic gate: equity floor, side sanity, data quality, stale price, ATR floor,
  risk-band clamp, cost model, EV-aware net R:R, sizing, leverage derivation, liquidation
  safety, heat cap, correlation cap, concurrency cap. As of 2026-07-05, the setup-QUALITY
  gates here (ATR floor, cost gate, R:R, heat/correlation/concurrency caps) read from one
  of two named profiles — NORMAL or EXPLORATION — selected by the SAME EXPLORATION_MODE
  flag. Account-SAFETY gates (equity floor, liquidation, leverage caps) never change.
- FILL-TIME PENDING RE-VALIDATION — a pending order can sit for hours before it fills;
  this re-checks fresh ATR floor and fresh cost/R:R using the ACTUAL fill price (not the
  originally quoted one) at the moment it fills, before flipping PENDING → OPEN.

--- STAGE 4: LEARNING LOOPS (feed back into the system over time, not per-trade) ---

- THE EXAMINER (labeller.py) — a shadow triple-barrier labelling system that records
  EVERY setup Dexter ever sees (POST, SKIP, NOT_ESCALATED, REJECT) and objectively labels
  the outcome, whether or not Chev ever acted on it. Exists to measure whether Chev's
  judgment adds real alpha above Dexter's raw score, independent of what Chev thinks of
  himself. Lives in labels_open.jsonl / labels_closed.jsonl / labels_discovery.json.
- PLAYBOOK LEARNING SESSIONS (_run_learning_session(), dexter.py) — runs automatically
  every 10 closed trades, for all 3 asset types. Rewrites the playbook file described in
  #3 above from real trade statistics (confluence combo win rates, management patterns,
  reasoning quality). This is where Chev is literally asked to analyze its own past
  trades and write advice back to its future self — powerful, but also exactly the
  mechanism that re-injected "wait for confirmation" language after we thought we'd
  removed it. Now has an explicit hard rule banning that framing (see RISK GAUNTLET /
  ROOT CAUSE sections) but it's worth remembering this loop exists and self-writes.
- TAG WIN-RATE / EV SYSTEM (compute_tag_win_rates(), risk_gauntlet.py) — computed fresh
  from chev_journal.json at gauntlet time, feeds the EV-aware NET_RR gate so a setup's
  required R:R scales with how well THAT SPECIFIC confluence tag has actually performed,
  instead of one flat number for every setup regardless of quality.
- CROSS-ANALYSIS / ADVISORY ACCURACY — tracks how often Chev's own POST/SKIP verdict
  would have matched what actually happened to Jane's (the human trader's) real trades,
  runs every CROSS_ANALYSIS_EVERY=20 combined closes.

--- SEEING ALL OF THIS LIVE: THE STRATEGY DASHBOARD (added 2026-07-05) ---

Everything described above — the feed, the funnel, the tag/combo win rates, the mode —
used to only be visible by reading raw log files (which is what most of this session was
spent doing by hand). It's now a real page: click the 🔥 icon in the webapp's top bar.
Full detail in the dedicated STRATEGY DASHBOARD section further down this document.

--- EXPLORATION_MODE — THE MASTER SWITCH, EVERYTHING IT CURRENTLY TOUCHES ---

One boolean (dexter.py, EXPLORATION_MODE = True right now). Why it exists: a paper-trading
data-collection phase needs enough trade VOLUME to actually learn something — a bar tuned
for real money produces too few trades to build the statistics (tag win rates, playbook
patterns, Examiner labels) that make every other part of this system smarter over time.
Flipping it to False is meant to restore every real-money-appropriate number in one motion
— that guarantee is only as good as this list, so if you add a new gate anywhere, ask
whether it should read from this flag too.

What it currently controls:
  1. Escalation score threshold + max distance (_active_thresholds()) — lower bar, wider
     distance tolerance, so more setups get shown to Chev at all.
  2. Chev's own OS-level skip conditions (auction maturity, participation, direction-score,
     TRANSITIONING) — demoted from hard vetoes to sizing/conviction inputs.
  3. GEOMETRY REVIEW's ATR floor + R:R pre-check — via risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile().
  4. risk_gauntlet.run_gauntlet()'s setup-quality gates — ATR floor, cost gate, R:R floor,
     heat cap, correlation cap, concurrency cap — via the same NORMAL/EXPLORATION profiles.

What it deliberately never touches, in any mode: STRUCT PRE-GATE, CONFLICT gate, equity
floor, liquidation safety, leverage caps, MIN_SAMPLES_FOR_EV, EV_SAFETY_MARGIN, RISK_BANDS.
These are either hygiene checks (garbage setups are garbage regardless of data-collection
goals) or account-survival math (a paper account can afford worse setups; it can't afford
pretending liquidation risk doesn't exist).
