================================================================================
## HOW DEXTER WORKS
================================================================================

Every 2 minutes Dexter scans all pairs across timeframes:
- Crypto: 5m/15m/30m/1h/4h (full Tier A/B SR model, Binance free)
- Forex/Stocks: 15m/30m/1h/4h (Tier B only — protects Twelve Data API budget)

When 3+ confluences align on a pair/TF, Dexter calls Chev via Open WebUI API:
  POST http://localhost:3000/api/chat/completions
  model: "chev-chelios"
  message: [full market brief + candle data + SR levels + Chev's playbook + journal]

Chev replies in strict format:
  POST: <15-word max summary>
  TRADE: direction=long, entry=X, sl=Y, tp=Z, risk_pct=N, leverage=N,
         position_size_usd=N, tags=sr_4h,fib_1h,rsi, trade_type=day,
         sr_level=X, fib_high=X, fib_low=X, vp_start=YYYY-MM-DD,
         rsi_div_t1=YYYY-MM-DD, rsi_div_t2=YYYY-MM-DD
  REASONING: <full analysis, no word limit>
     Must include: 4H STRUCTURE / INVALIDATION / ENTRY BASIS blocks (renamed from
     CONFIRMATION 2026-07-05 — see THE ACTUAL ROOT CAUSE section below)

  OR: SKIP: <one sentence why — must state what was missing>

Dexter parses the TRADE: line, validates confluence score, checks SL direction,
logs to Google Sheets, and monitors until TP/SL/expiry.

Gate order (2026-07-04 — a whole pre-Chev stage was added; see CONFLUENCE SCORING
SYSTEM → TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE for full detail):
  0. TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE (BEFORE Chev is asked): trade threshold, struct pre-gate,
     distance-from-level, directional-conflict — all shadow-logged, all skip Chev
     entirely if failed
  1. Format check (POST:/SKIP: present) — retry once if missing
  2. Post-Chev hard score gate (Dexter's own score vs _active_thresholds(), independent
     of anything Chev tagged — rejects if Chev somehow posts on a setup that shouldn't
     have reached him)
  3. STRUCT_REJECT gate (sr_score ≥ 2 OR vp_score ≥ 2 required) — legacy, redundant with
     the pre-gate's struct check on purpose, both measured
  4. risk_gauntlet validation (ATR SL sanity, R:R ≥ 2.0, position size cap)
  5. Google Sheets log + monitoring loop

================================================================================
## CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM (recalibrated 2026-07-03, thresholds reworked 2026-07-04)
================================================================================

NORMAL minimum score to open a trade: crypto=10, forex=8, stock=8
EXPLORATION minimum (currently ACTIVE — see EXPLORATION MODE section): crypto=7, forex=6, stock=6

Both sets of numbers live as constants near the top of dexter.py
(CONFLUENCE_THRESHOLD_CRYPTO/FOREX/STOCK and EXPLORATION_THRESHOLD_CRYPTO/FOREX/STOCK).
EVERY gate that checks "is this score/distance good enough" MUST read them through the
single helper _active_thresholds(asset_type) — never the raw constants directly — so
exploration mode can never be half-applied across gates. Three call sites currently use
it: the TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE, the post-Chev hard score gate, and the "Score X vs
threshold Y" line shown to Chev in ask_chev_to_judge. _setup_grade() deliberately does
NOT use the helper — grading always uses the FULL normal threshold regardless of
exploration mode, because the grade (and its suggested risk %) is the real risk control
during the exploration phase. See EXPLORATION MODE section for why this matters.

Score = raw_score × TF_multiplier. TF multipliers:
  4H × 1.2   |   1H × 1.0   |   30M × 0.9   |   15M × 0.8

IMPORTANT, CLARIFIED 2026-07-05: these point values are STATIC. There is no live
mechanism where a signal's real win rate feeds back into its own point value — Kev's
own reasonable assumption ("if SR is winning, its points should go up") is NOT how this
works today, and he asked to be corrected if wrong, so: corrected. The only place real
win-rate data touches anything live is downstream, in risk_gauntlet's EV-aware NET_RR gate
(compute_tag_win_rates/compute_combo_win_rates — see RISK GAUNTLET section) — that affects
whether a PROPOSED TRADE's reward justifies its risk, never the upfront confluence score
itself. If auto-tuning these point values from real performance is ever built (raised as
brainstorm item 6 in the Strategy Dashboard planning conversation), it needs real
guardrails against a runaway feedback loop — a well-performing tag getting weighted
higher, getting used more, looking even better partly from the extra weight itself, and
eventually swallowing the whole score on its own: a hard ceiling per tag's point value, a
minimum sample size before any adjustment is trusted, and a human approving the change
rather than a silent overnight drift. This is the same shape of bug as the playbook
self-reinforcement loop found and fixed earlier this session (see THE ACTUAL ROOT CAUSE
section) — a system that grades its own homework and rewards itself for it. NOT BUILT,
deliberately, until (if ever) those guardrails exist.

Raw scores by signal type:
  SR (multi-touch, ≥3x):   3pt  — exposed as sr_score
  SR (single/double, 1-2x): 2pt
    NOTE (2026-07-04): if BOTH a resistance and support zone are within the 1.5% window,
    only the NEARER one scores — price sandwiched mid-range no longer collects points
    for both sides (that was chop, not confluence).
  Golden Pocket (GP):       3pt
  Volume Profile (VP POC/VAH/VAL): 3pt — exposed as vp_score
    NOTE (2026-07-04): VP now respects the underlying auction anchor's own validation
    stamps (from _validate_anchor). If the anchor is no longer "active" (price broke back
    through it), that timeframe's VP is skipped entirely. If active but NOT "confirmed"
    (no follow-through yet), the VP still scores but at HALF points, and the reason string
    gets an "unconfirmed-anchor," note — e.g. "VP POC 4h (0.12% away ≤0.40% prox,
    unconfirmed-anchor, 1.5pt)".
  RSI divergence confirmed: 3pt (4pt if both regular + hidden)
    NOTE (2026-07-04): only the two HIGHEST-scoring divergences that share the SAME bias
    (bull or bear) can both score — a Regular Bullish and a Hidden Bearish no longer both
    add points to one setup (that was contradiction counted as confluence; caught live on
    USD/CAD 15m). The dominant-bias divergence always scores; a second one only scores if
    its bias matches.
  EMA (55/21/13 support/resist): 2pt / 1pt / 0.5pt respectively; total EMA capped 3pt
  Bollinger Band (BURST/near/mid): 2pt / 0.5pt / 1pt
    SQUEEZE — NO LONGER SCORED (2026-07-04): demoted to 0pt context, same treatment as
    RSI 50-cross. Every playbook and Chev's prompt said "do NOT enter during a squeeze"
    while the score argued FOR entry — contradiction resolved by making it context-only.
    Reason string still appears (`BB squeeze (width X%, context, 0pt)`) so Chev/Examiner
    still see it, it just can't push a setup over threshold.
  Derivatives — funding + OI trend (crypto only, via derivs.py): 0–4.5pt combined
    "Funding extreme" (contrarian — crowded side is squeeze fuel): 2pt notable / 3pt extreme
    "OI divergence" (price up + OI down = weak rally; price down + OI down = short
      covering): 1.5pt.  "OI confirmation" (price and OI agree — real participation): 1pt.
    See DERIVATIVES LAYER section below.
  Chart pattern (high/mid conf): 2pt / 1pt
  Sweep (liquidity sweep):  3pt
  Fib retracement level:    1.5pt
  RSI OB/OS:                0.5pt
  RSI 50-cross:             context only (0pt — shown in brief, not scored)
  [WATCH — forming div]:    context only (0pt — never scored, shown as amber watch)

TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE (added 2026-07-04, runs BEFORE Chev is ever asked):
  Fires inside scan_pair_tf's caller, in this order, each shadow-logged to the Examiner
  under a distinct NOT_ESCALATED reason so skip_reason_audit() can measure each gate:
    1. Score < _active_thresholds() trade threshold → "below_trade_threshold"
    2. sr_score < 2 AND vp_score < 2 AND no fast_anchor_pass (no structural anchor) →
       "struct_pregate" — widened 2026-07-05 to also accept prior-day H/L or opening
       range as a qualifying anchor; see FAST INTRADAY STRUCTURAL ANCHORS below.
    3. dist_from_level > _active_thresholds() max distance, UNLESS vp_score ≥ 2
       (a VP anchor IS its own location — SR/Fib distance is irrelevant to it).
       Fast anchors do NOT get this exemption — their prices are folded directly into
       the same candidate list dist_from_level is computed from instead.
       → "too_far_from_level"
    4. Conflicting directional signals: _directional_split(reasons) splits bull vs bear
       points; if the minor side ≥ 2.0 pts AND the dominant side < 2.0× the minor side →
       "conflicting_signals" (contradictory setup, not scored as confluence)
  Weekend crypto bump (+2 to the trade threshold on Sat/Sun UTC) is DISABLED entirely as
  of 2026-07-04 (commented out in place, not deleted) — this is a paper account, so thin
  weekend books / sweep risk don't cost anything real yet. A REMINDER comment sits right
  above the commented-out block in dexter.py: restore it once a live Binance API key +
  real funds are wired in and weekend slippage/sweeps actually matter. This is
  independent of EXPLORATION_MODE now — previously it was gated to `not EXPLORATION_MODE`,
  but is off regardless of that switch as of this change.

This pre-gate is separate from, and runs in addition to, the OLD structural gate
(STRUCT_REJECT, described below) which still fires after Chev replies — CORRECTION:
this is NOT part of risk_gauntlet.py (a prior version of this doc implied that); it's a
separate check inside dexter.py's own main escalation loop, distinct from and running
BEFORE risk_gauntlet.run_gauntlet() is ever called. The two structural gates (pre-gate
and STRUCT_REJECT) are redundant on purpose right now (measuring both).

Structural prerequisite gate (STRUCT_REJECT, legacy, still present post-Chev):
  sr_score ≥ 2 OR vp_score ≥ 2 OR fast_anchor_pass must be true before any trade passes
  (identical widened condition to the pre-gate's struct_pregate check as of 2026-07-05 —
  the two must always move together, see FAST INTRADAY STRUCTURAL ANCHORS below).
  Purpose: kills mid-range EMA/fib-only setups with no structural anchor.
  If gate fails: reason_code = "STRUCT_REJECT", NOT_ESCALATED hook fires.

MTF confidence tax (counter-trend trades only):
  A trade against the 4H regime (e.g. long in TRENDING_DOWN) requires:
    1. Score ≥ 1.5× the NORMAL threshold (crypto ≥ 15, forex ≥ 12, stocks ≥ 12) — this is
       always the full normal threshold, never the exploration one, even during exploration
    2. Confirmed RSI divergence present (not forming)
  If either condition fails: trade blocked before Chev is asked.
  The "Score ≥ 13" literal that used to appear in Chev's prompt AND all three playbooks
  was inconsistent with the actual 1.5× rule — fixed 2026-07-04, now computed live and
  shown as the real per-asset number in both places.

================================================================================
## EXPLORATION MODE — CURRENTLY ACTIVE (added 2026-07-04)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: after the 2026-07-04 scoring recalibration, Dexter's normal threshold
was so tight that Chev received hundreds of escalations over ~10 hours and posted ZERO
trades. With no trades, the learning loops (playbooks, the Examiner's POST-vs-SKIP
comparison) have no data. This is a PAPER account, so a deliberate, time-boxed, fully
reversible exploration phase was built: lower the entry bar, keep every safety/hygiene
gate at full strength, let small graded trades flow, and let the data reveal where the
real threshold belongs.

THE SWITCH — everything hangs off ONE boolean, near the top of dexter.py:
  EXPLORATION_MODE = True     ← flip to False to restore normal thresholds EVERYWHERE
                                 at once. No other code needs to change. Restart Dexter
                                 after flipping.

When EXPLORATION_MODE is True:
  - Trade thresholds: crypto=7, forex=6, stock=6 (vs normal 10/8/8)
  - Max escalation distance from a confluence level: 1.5% (vs normal 0.75%)
  - Weekend crypto threshold bump (+2) is disabled entirely, not just during exploration
    (see CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM section for the reminder-to-restore-on-real-money note)
  - Chev's escalation prompt gets an extra paragraph: this is a paper-trading DATA-
    COLLECTION PHASE, losses are tuition, DEFAULT is POST if there's a nameable entry/
    stop/target, and a SKIP must name ONE concrete broken element (no invalidation level,
    counter-trend without meeting the MTF tax conditions, price nowhere near any zone) —
    never general caution, "not enough confluence", a letter grade alone, or maturity/
    participation figures alone (those are sizing inputs in this phase, not vetoes)
  - Chev's system prompt ("Chev Prompt" file — MUST be manually pasted into Open WebUI
    for this half to actually take effect) carries a matching paragraph right before
    "WHEN DEXTER ESCALATES A SIGNAL": the Operating System's hard skip conditions
    (auction maturity, participation floor, TRANSITIONING state, direction-score
    contradiction) become CONVICTION/SIZING inputs on Dexter escalations ONLY, not vetoes,
    for the duration of the phase. Kev's normal chat requests are completely unaffected.
  - Dexter prints the live regime on startup, right after
    "labeller.start_resolver_daemon(...)" — first screen of the terminal tells you
    whether EXPLORATION MODE is ACTIVE (with its numbers) or OFF (normal thresholds).

DELIBERATELY UNCHANGED BY THE SWITCH (the hygiene stays at full strength — that's the
entire point of this design — none of these read EXPLORATION_MODE at all):
  - STRUCT PRE-GATE and the CONFLICT gate (_directional_split) inside the TRADEABILITY
    PRE-GATE — same sr/vp ≥2 requirement, same bull/bear contradiction check
  - risk_gauntlet.py — ATR SL sanity, R:R ≥ 2.0, position size cap, stale price guard,
    ATR staleness — completely untouched
  - SL-direction hard-rejects
  - _setup_grade() — ALWAYS grades against the FULL normal threshold (10/8/8), regardless
    of exploration mode. This is intentional and is the real risk control of the whole
    phase: a score-7 exploration trade still only grades as a B (or lower), so it gets
    small suggested risk (0.75%) rather than being treated like a full-strength A+ setup.
  - labeller.py, engines.py, honest_sim.py, derivs.py, any jane_* function — all untouched

THE HELPER — _active_thresholds(asset_type) in dexter.py: the single source of truth.
Returns (score_threshold, max_dist_pct) for the given asset type, reading the exploration
constants when EXPLORATION_MODE is True and the normal constants otherwise. Every gate
that checks a score or distance goes through this — never the raw CONFLUENCE_THRESHOLD_*
or ESCALATION_MAX_DIST_PCT constants directly — specifically so the mode can never be
half-applied (e.g. the pre-gate accepting a score-7 setup that the post-Chev hard score
gate then rejects at 10, which is exactly the bug this fixes).

WHAT KEV SHOULD SEE: escalation volume rises within a day of restarting; posted trades
appear, mostly graded B at small suggested risk; Chev's skips each cite one concrete
missing element instead of "score too low" or general caution.

ENDING THE PHASE: once roughly 30–40 trades per asset class have closed, flip
EXPLORATION_MODE to False in dexter.py, restart Dexter, and re-paste the ORIGINAL
(pre-exploration) Chev Prompt paragraph back out if Kev wants the system prompt fully
reverted too — the dexter.py side reverts automatically on the flip, but the Chev Prompt
text file is not touched by the switch and stays as edited until manually changed back.

================================================================================
## OPPORTUNITY ENGINE REWORK (2026-07-06) — why zero trades posted despite EXPLORATION_MODE
================================================================================

*** BASELINE: Dexter restarted + Chev Prompt re-pasted 2026-07-06 03:38 — see top banner ***

WHY THIS EXISTS: EXPLORATION_MODE (above) loosens Dexter's own score gate, but Chev posted
ZERO trades for 53+ hours after it went live. Investigation traced it to engines.py's
Opportunity Engine — a completely separate confidence/R:R grading system (A+/A/B/C),
untouched by EXPLORATION_MODE, that Chev's prompt treated as a near-veto ("B → require
extra confluence, C → minimum size or SKIP"). The setups EXPLORATION_MODE deliberately let
through were getting re-rejected by this second, un-loosened gate downstream. Confirmed via
chev_decisions.jsonl: 1,554 decisions in the drought window, 92.5% Chev's own SKIP (not
Dexter's gates), dominant reason "confluence quality below threshold" — the Opportunity
Engine's letter grade talking, not a Dexter override.

THREE ROOT CAUSES FOUND, ALL FIXED:

1. Trendline fit-quality (engines.py, _fit_trendline) had no noise tolerance — every wick
   or fakeout swing point was penalized identically to a genuine structural break. Fixed:
   swings within 0.3× ATR of the fitted line now count as a clean touch (no penalty), capped
   at 30% of the current channel width so a converging triangle near its apex doesn't get a
   tolerance wider than the whole remaining pattern. New TrendlineFit.within_tolerance_count
   field tracks how many swings were forgiven, surfaced to Chev as a CLEAN/ACCEPTABLE/POOR
   label + one-sentence explanation in the GEOMETRY block of format_survey_for_chev.

2. Hypothesis confidence (engines.py, _score_hypothesis) was a strict min() across 4
   unrelated sub-scores (pattern-match, geometry fit, market state, auction) — one noisy
   ingredient capped the whole hypothesis regardless of the other three. Fixed: a
   catastrophic floor (0.15) still disqualifies outright (e.g. a genuinely dead market), but
   above that floor the four scores blend as a weighted average (pattern-match 40%, the
   other three 20% each) instead of a strict minimum.

3. The A+/A/B/C quality ladder itself (engines.py, run_opportunity_engine) conflated "is
   this a real, tradeable setup" (should be binary) with "how much conviction/size" (should
   be continuous) into one bucketed letter that Chev's prompt used as a soft gate. Fixed:
   the one binary validity gate (real hypothesis, non-neutral bias, auction not FAILED) is
   unchanged; `quality` is still computed but is now cosmetic/display-only — Chev's prompt
   was rewritten (Dexter-escalation section only, ~line 505 in "Chev Prompt") to size
   continuously off the existing `confluence_score` (0-100) field instead, and never skip
   solely for moderate (as opposed to high) conviction.

ALSO ADDED: a ZONE ALIGNMENT CHECK line in dexter.py's ask_chev_to_judge — states the %
distance between Dexter's own SR/Fib confluence zone and the Opportunity Engine's
independently-computed entry_zone (same AT LEVEL/APPROACHING proximity-bucket convention
used elsewhere), so Chev reads a stated fact instead of re-judging "do these line up"
himself with no defined tolerance.

WHAT KEV SHOULD SEE FROM THE 2026-07-06 03:38 BASELINE FORWARD: console escalations
showing a CLEAN/ACCEPTABLE/POOR geometry label and a "Conviction: N/100" line instead of
a bare letter grade; Chev's POSTs (and skips) should no longer cite vague "confluence
quality below threshold" language for setups that already cleared Dexter's score gate.

OUT OF SCOPE, DELIBERATELY NOT TOUCHED: chart_drawer.py has its own INDEPENDENT, duplicate
copy of the same A+/A/B/C ladder (~line 2916), used for Kev's manual get_market_survey
chat-tool calls, not Dexter escalations — not wired to engines.py at all, not part of this
fix. Chev Prompt's normal-chat "Reading the OPPORTUNITY block" section (~line 101) is
separate, already-different guidance, also left untouched.

VERIFICATION DONE: python -m py_compile clean on engines.py + dexter.py. Manual smoke test
against real Binance candle data (BTCUSDT/SOLUSDT/ETHUSDT, no dexter.py import — see the
caution below) confirmed no crashes, sane CLEAN/ACCEPTABLE/POOR labels, and correct zone-
alignment output. No live end-to-end restart verification beyond that was done by Claude —
Kev restarted Dexter and re-pasted the Chev Prompt himself per the baseline above.

CAUTION FOR FUTURE SESSIONS: do not `import dexter` to test anything — its main scan loop
runs at module level (no `if __name__ == "__main__":` guard), so importing it starts a
second live instance of the bot (real trades checked, real Telegram alerts, real Chev
calls). This actually happened once during this rework's verification — caught quickly
(crashed on an unrelated pre-existing Windows console encoding bug, ~1 minute), no lasting
damage, but test engines.py/risk_gauntlet.py/etc. directly instead, never dexter.py itself.

## REASONING SPECIFICITY FIX (2026-07-06 04:26 baseline — see top banner)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: Kev reviewed the Strategy Dashboard's decision feed and couldn't tell why
Chev was actually skipping trades — the feed only ever showed a short one-line summary
("confluence quality below threshold despite strong indicators"), never the fuller
reasoning Chev already writes. Two separate problems, both fixed:

1. THE CODE WAS THROWING AWAY DETAIL THAT ALREADY EXISTED. `parse_chev_reply` (dexter.py)
   only parsed the `REASONING:` field inside the POST branch — for a SKIP, the full
   narrative Chev is required to write was never captured at all, only the one-sentence
   `SKIP:` line and `WHAT WAS MISSING:` survived. For a POST, `_log_chev_decision` was only
   ever given the punchy 15-word Telegram teaser, not the REASONING either (the fuller
   version existed only in the labeller's separate JSONL, never in chev_decisions.jsonl —
   the file the dashboard actually reads). FIXED: REASONING is now parsed unconditionally
   for both POST and SKIP (`result["reasoning"]`, dexter.py's `parse_chev_reply`).

2. `_log_chev_decision` (dexter.py) gained a `detail` param (the full reasoning, plus
   "what was missing" appended for skips) and a free `specific` boolean — true if `detail`
   (or `reason` as fallback) contains at least one digit. No LLM cost, just a cheap
   correctness check: does this explanation actually cite a real number, or is it pure
   qualitative judgment with nothing checkable in it. Both new fields flow straight through
   `/api/strategy/feed` (no endpoint change needed, it already forwards whole JSONL
   records) into the Strategy Dashboard's feed cards and raw log table (webapp/index.html)
   — the raw table gained a `Detail` column, and any entry with `specific: false` gets a
   dim "⚠ vague" tag right on the card, so vagueness is now visible at a glance instead of
   requiring you to go read chev_decisions.jsonl by hand.

3. PROMPT TIGHTENED (both dexter.py's escalation prompt and "Chev Prompt" itself, ~line
   471): REASONING and WHAT WAS MISSING must now cite at least one real number from THAT
   SPECIFIC setup — a price level, ATR multiple, RSI value, %, or named tag — with a
   worked example contrasting vague ("confluence quality below threshold despite strong
   indicators") against specific ("EMA-21/55 cluster at 61,300 vs. the 4H golden pocket at
   61,250-61,420, but no confirmed RSI divergence and the nearest swing low is 2.1% away —
   R:R only 1.1:1 against the 1.3:1 floor"). This is the piece that should actually change
   what Chev writes going forward, not just what the code keeps.

SCOPE: Dexter escalations + the Radar "Ask Chev" hypothetical feature (both run through the
same `ask_chev_to_judge`/`parse_chev_reply` pipeline). Kev's manual chat requests
(chart_drawer.py) untouched, same scoping precedent as the Opportunity Engine rework.

HOW TO USE THIS TO FIND THE ANNOYING RULE: see the "HOW TO ACTUALLY FIND THE ANNOYING RULE
NOW" note under the top banner's 2026-07-06 04:26 baseline — split chev_decisions.jsonl (or
the Strategy Dashboard feed/raw log) by `decision` type first (SKIP = Chev, GATE_REJECT/
STRUCT_REJECT/MTF_TAX_REJECT/REJECT = Dexter's own gates), then read `detail` for whichever
type dominates. A specific number or threshold that keeps recurring across many entries IS
the annoying rule — that's now a literal, grep-able pattern instead of a vague impression.

VERIFICATION DONE: python -m py_compile clean on dexter.py. parse_chev_reply and the
_log_chev_decision entry-building logic both tested in isolation (function source
extracted and exec'd standalone, NOT via `import dexter`) against synthetic SKIP and POST
replies — confirmed `reasoning`/`detail`/`specific` populate correctly for both branches.
node --check + div-balance clean on webapp/index.html. No live end-to-end verification
beyond that was done by Claude — Kev restarted Dexter and re-pasted "Chev Prompt" himself
at the 04:26 baseline.

================================================================================
## NET_RR STALENESS FIX (2026-07-06 — requires restart, see banner; not yet applied as of writing)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: using the reasoning-specificity fix's own new `detail` field, Kev asked for
a pattern check on decisions between the two previous baselines (UTC 02:38-03:26, i.e. local
03:38-04:26). 23 decisions, 20 SKIP, zero POST — drought continued even with both earlier
fixes live. But 7 of the 20 skips explicitly cited "Net R:R after costs" falling short, with
required thresholds of 2.25-3.83 — nowhere near the 1.2 exploration floor. Traced to
`risk_gauntlet.py`'s EV-aware NET_RR gate (added 2026-07-05, a different fix from anything
in the two rounds above): live tag stats pulled from `/api/strategy/performance` matched the
cited numbers almost exactly —

  sr_4h    n=33  win_rate=27%  -> breakeven-derived required R:R = 3.11  (cited: 3.07)
  ema_13   n=13  win_rate=23%  -> breakeven-derived required R:R = 3.85  (cited: 3.83)
  fib_1h   n=34  win_rate=29%  |  dv  n=53  win_rate=34%  |  gp  n=30  win_rate=33%

THE ACTUAL BUG: the gate takes a trade's confluence tags, finds the WORST-performing one
("weakest qualifying tag" — same weakest-link principle as Chev's own confidence
philosophy), and demands a R:R high enough to be profitable at that tag's historical win
rate. Sound idea — except the historical win rate is all-time, and every one of the most
commonly-used tags (sr_4h, fib_1h, dv, gp) has a poor all-time record almost entirely
predating tonight's fixes (EXPLORATION_MODE, the Opportunity Engine rework, the geometry
ATR tolerance). So nearly every new setup inherited a 2.2-3.9:1 required R:R from a report
card that has nothing to do with the system now running. Confirmed as a genuine closed
loop, not "needs more loosening": the only way a tag's win rate could improve is new trades
closing under it — and the stale win rate itself is exactly what was preventing new trades
from closing. Discussed at length with Kev (the credit-score-trap analogy: a bank rejecting
a loan off an old, since-resolved credit problem, denying the applicant the only thing —
a new loan — that could build a fresh history to replace it).

THE FIX — two changes to `compute_tag_win_rates` (risk_gauntlet.py:113), addressing two
separate failure modes Kev identified are NOT the same problem despite looking similar
("wrong era" vs "wrong certainty"):

1. ROLLING WINDOW BY TRADE COUNT, NOT CALENDAR TIME (Kev's own refinement over the first
   calendar-window draft) — new `window_trades` param. Only a tag's most recent N
   occurrences count, however long they took to accumulate — so a good-but-infrequent
   strategy is never penalized just for trading rarely; it's judged on its most recent N
   results whenever they happened, not "did enough calendar days pass."
2. BAYESIAN SHRINKAGE TOWARD THE OVERALL AVERAGE — new `smoothing_k` param. A thin sample
   (even a fresh one, post-window) gets pulled toward the overall win rate across all
   closed trades instead of being trusted as exact truth; a thick sample barely moves.
   Self-correcting as more trades accumulate — no manual re-tuning needed later.

Both params default to off (`window_trades=None, smoothing_k=0`) — calling
`compute_tag_win_rates(closed_trades)` with no extra args is byte-for-byte the original
behavior. TWO CALL SITES, DELIBERATELY TREATED DIFFERENTLY:
  - dexter.py:515 (Strategy Dashboard's tag leaderboard, `api_strategy_performance()`) —
    UNCHANGED, no new params. This is for Kev's own review — it must keep showing the raw,
    full all-time truth, not a smoothed/windowed version. Hiding data from him there would
    be the wrong kind of fix.
  - dexter.py:9821 (right before `risk_gauntlet.run_gauntlet(...)` in the live scan loop) —
    now passes `window_trades=risk_gauntlet.TAG_WINRATE_WINDOW_TRADES` (35) and
    `smoothing_k=risk_gauntlet.TAG_WINRATE_SMOOTHING_K` (10), both new module constants in
    risk_gauntlet.py's CONFIG block, next to MIN_SAMPLES_FOR_EV/EV_SAFETY_MARGIN — this is
    the only call site that should ever change, and gate 8's own logic (risk_gauntlet.py
    345-375) needed ZERO changes — it just reads whatever `tag_stats` dict it's handed.

MIN_SAMPLES_FOR_EV (10) and the "sits on the flat floor until it earns enough sample" gap-
period behavior are UNCHANGED, per Kev's own explicit call — not a flaw, that's the gate
correctly saying "I don't know yet."

HONEST RESULT, NOT OVERSOLD: recomputed against the real 73-entry chev_journal.json —

  sr_4h:   27% -> 29% win rate  |  required R:R  3.07 -> 2.83
  ema_13:  23% -> 28% win rate  |  required R:R  3.83 -> 2.97
  fib_1h:  29% -> 31% win rate  |  required R:R  2.76 -> 2.62
  dv:      n=53->35 (window capped it), 34% -> 36%  |  required R:R  2.24 -> 2.00

Real, measurable, in the right direction — but modest, not dramatic. All 73 existing
journal entries are from roughly the same pre-fix era, so reweighting/windowing existing
data can only do so much; it can't manufacture good new data that doesn't exist yet. The
required R:R is still 2.0-3.0 for the worst-affected tags, well above the 1.2 exploration
floor. The real payoff is structural, not immediate: as NEW trades close under tonight's
improved system, they flow into this same windowed calculation and the numbers should drift
toward reality — which is the whole point, breaking the loop so that CAN happen at all. If
Chev is still skipping heavily on NET_RR after this restart, that may mean the underlying
strategy genuinely needs a better edge on these tags, not just a measurement fix — worth
distinguishing "the gate was lying" (this fix) from "the gate was right" (a strategy
problem) once fresh data comes in.

VERIFICATION DONE: risk_gauntlet.py's self-guarded test suite (`if __name__ == "__main__":`
— safe to run directly, unlike dexter.py) grew from 21 to 23 cases, all passing: one proving
the trade-count window lets recent improvement show through old-era history (60% all-time
vs 86% on the most recent 35), one proving thin samples get pulled toward the overall
average while thick samples barely move. `python -m py_compile` clean on both files. Live
recompute against the real journal (above) done directly, not fabricated.

================================================================================
## EV-NEUTRAL EXPLORATION — PHASE 1 (2026-07-06 14:53 — RESTART REQUIRED, see top banner)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: continuing directly from the NET_RR STALENESS FIX above and the
INVALIDATION-LEVEL BOTTLENECK conversation below it — even after that fix (rolling window +
shrinkage), the EV-based required R:R was still landing at 2.0-3.0:1 for ordinary day
trades, because the win-rate data behind it — while now fresher and smoothed — is still
fundamentally earned by a different, pre-2026-07-06 system. Kev's own framing, confirmed
correct: George is judging today's trades against yesterday's report card, and the
report card can only improve if new trades close, which the report card itself was
blocking. Rather than reweight the old data further, this phase removes the old data's
ENFORCEMENT power entirely while EXPLORATION_MODE is on, without deleting the number —
it's still computed and logged on every decision, just advisory rather than a gate.

THE CHANGE — risk_gauntlet.py, gate 8 only (ANCHOR: "WEAKEST LINK: size the requirement
off the worst-performing qualifying tag"):
  - `eligible`, the weakest tag, `breakeven_rr`, and the EV-derived required R:R are still
    computed exactly as before, every time, regardless of mode.
  - NEW BRANCH: if `exploration_mode` is True AND a qualifying tag exists, the ENFORCED
    requirement becomes the flat `MIN_NET_RR[trade_type]` floor (day=1.2 etc.) instead of
    the EV number — and a note is appended to the trade's `notes` list: "EV advisory (not
    enforced, exploration): weakest tag '<tag>' win_rate=<p>% (n=<n>) would have required
    <X.XX>:1; enforcing flat floor <Y.YY>:1" — visible on every PASS result going forward.
  - If `exploration_mode` is False: behavior is byte-identical to before this phase — the
    EV number is still fully enforced. Nothing changes outside exploration.
  - If no tag qualifies at all (`eligible` empty): unchanged in BOTH modes — already used
    the flat floor before this phase, still does.
  - The `basis` string used inside any NET_RR reject message now states which mode produced
    the enforced number (e.g. "flat floor (exploration — EV advisory only, see notes)"),
    so a rejection is self-explanatory even without reading the notes list.

ERA STAMP — dexter.py: new module constant `SYSTEM_ERA = "explor_v2_2026-07-06"` (placed
right after the EXPLORATION_MODE constants block). Added `"system_era": SYSTEM_ERA` to
every newly-closed Chev-trade journal entry, at BOTH write sites that append to
chev_journal.json: `api_close_trade()` (manual force-close path) and `_do_postmortem()`
(the automatic SL/TP/expiry postmortem path — the main one). Jane's separate journal
(`jane_journal.append`, a different file, a different trader) was deliberately left
untouched — out of scope, not a Chev-trade path. This stamp is PURELY ADDITIVE right now —
nothing reads it yet. It exists so that whenever EV enforcement comes back (Phase 2+, not
yet decided or scheduled), it can be pointed at only trades stamped with the current era,
rather than re-inheriting the same pre-fix bias this phase just neutralized.

VERIFICATION DONE: risk_gauntlet.py's self-test suite grew from 23 to 25 (both new,
passing) — test 24 proves a poisoned tag (20% win rate, n=30, would demand 4.60:1) still
PASSES at net_rr=1.30 under exploration with the advisory note correctly logged; test 25

confirming zero behavior change outside exploration. `python -m py_compile` clean on both

WHAT KEV SHOULD SEE AFTER RESTART: NET_RR should all but disappear from Chev's SKIP
reasons while exploration is on (down from the ~6% it already was after the staleness fix)

## COST GATE — HONEST MESSAGE + RETRY — PHASE 2 (2026-07-06 15:03 — RESTART REQUIRED)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: the cost gate (gate 7 — round-trip trading costs vs. stop distance) was
responsible for 34 of the last 58 downstream kills over 3 days, with zero retries offered —
every other fixable gate (ATR_FLOOR, NET_RR) gives Chev one chance to revise in the same
thread, this one didn't. Its message also asserted "Not fixable by SL adjustment alone,"
which is mathematically wrong: cost-per-R = round-trip-cost ÷ stop-distance, so widening
the stop is the direct, mechanical fix. The gate's underlying economics were never in
question — it was just silent about the cure and needlessly final about it.

THE CHANGE — risk_gauntlet.py, gate 7 only (ANCHOR: "Round-trip cost"):
  - Added `min_stop_pct = cost_rt / prof["MAX_COST_R"][trade_type]` — the exact stop
    distance at which cost-per-R would equal the max allowed, computed from the same
    inputs the gate already had.
  - Reject message rewritten to state that number plainly: ...exceeds max <m>R for <type>.
    For a <type> trade on this asset, the SL must sit at least <min_stop_pct>% from entry.
    Widen the SL to real structure at or beyond that distance, pick a trade_type whose
    ceiling fits, or SKIP. The old "Not fixable by SL adjustment alone" sentence is gone —
    it was the specific thing that was wrong.
  - `_reject(...)` call now passes `fixable=True` — the existing one-retry-in-the-same-
    thread loop in dexter.py (ANCHOR: "One retry in the same thread — same pattern as the
    geometry review," ~line 9844) fires on ANY `fixable=True` reject already, no dexter.py
    change needed. Verified by reading that loop (read-only this phase): confirmed it fires
    on the boolean flag generically, and confirmed `_g_fix_msg` includes the full
    `reject_reason` verbatim — Chev will see the exact minimum-stop number in his retry
    prompt, not a paraphrase.

DELIBERATELY NOT TOUCHED: the fill-time re-check copy of this same cost math, in dexter.py's
monitor loop (ANCHOR: "Cost gate fails at fill price") — cancel-at-fill stays non-retry by
design, a trade already filled doesn't get a do-over on its stop placement. NOTE FOR A
FUTURE SESSION, found incidentally during this phase's read-only verification, NOT fixed
here (out of scope): that fill-time re-check references `risk_gauntlet.MAX_COST_R` as a
flat, non-profile module-level dict — no such flat dict currently exists in risk_gauntlet.py
(only `_NORMAL["MAX_COST_R"]` / `_EXPLORATION["MAX_COST_R"]` inside the profile dicts). This
looks like a latent `AttributeError` waiting to happen at fill-check time, silently caught
by that block's own surrounding `except Exception`. Worth a dedicated look later — explicitly
not this phase's problem, one-phase-one-change-set.

VERIFICATION DONE: risk_gauntlet.py self-test suite stayed at 25 cases (test 5, the existing
cost-gate case, was upgraded in place rather than adding a new one — it now asserts
`fixable is True` and that the reject message contains the real minimum stop percentage,
computed from that test's own inputs via `FEE_SIDE`/`SLIPPAGE_SIDE`/`_NORMAL["MAX_COST_R"]`,
not hardcoded). All 25 green. Worked example, computed directly against the live module, not
from memory: crypto / day / exploration profile → cost_rt=0.1400%, MAX_COST_R=0.40 →
minimum stop = 0.3500%. `python -m py_compile risk_gauntlet.py` clean (dexter.py untouched
this phase, no compile check needed on it).

## EXECUTABLE GEOMETRY BLOCK — PHASE 3 (2026-07-06 15:12 — RESTART + CHEV PROMPT RE-PASTE)
================================================================================

*** THIS PHASE EDITS "Chev Prompt" — RE-PASTE INTO OPEN WEBUI REQUIRED. SAYING IT AGAIN: ***
*** editing the file on disk changes NOTHING until its content is manually pasted into ***
*** Open WebUI's model system prompt. Do not skip this step. ***

WHY THIS EXISTS: directly out of the INVALIDATION-LEVEL BOTTLENECK investigation — Chev was
being coached "your SL must clear at least 1x ATR from entry," which on a fast timeframe can
be a third of what the cost gate (Phase 2) actually demands. He was following one rule
straight into a wall built by a different rule he'd never been shown. ~60% of his skips cite
"no clear invalidation" — partly because the survivable band was never handed to him as
numbers, only as vibes. This turns the invalidation question into arithmetic he can check
himself, before writing a word.

THE CHANGE — dexter.py (`ask_chev_to_judge` and a new helper), Chev Prompt (one section):
  - New pure helper `_build_executable_geometry_block(asset_type, atr, price,
    exploration_mode)` (dexter.py, right before `ask_chev_to_judge`). For each of
    scalp/day/swing, computes: cost_rt (imported from risk_gauntlet's own FEE_SIDE/
    SLIPPAGE_SIDE/FUNDING_EST_SWING — never duplicated), the cost-floor minimum stop, the
    ATR-floor minimum stop (as a % of price), takes whichever is LARGER as the effective
    minimum (labeled which one won), the enforced net R:R floor
    (`risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile(...)["MIN_NET_RR"]`), and the minimum TP distance
    that R:R implies at that effective stop. Closes with: if no real structural level
    exists at or beyond the minimum SL distance for any trade_type, that's a valid, number-
    citable SKIP.
  - Inserted into `ask_chev_to_judge`'s escalation message directly above "TOOLS AVAILABLE,"
    titled "EXECUTABLE GEOMETRY — hard limits the Risk Gauntlet will enforce on any POST."
  - Fixed the two coaching lines that were actively contradicting this: "Your SL must clear
    at least 1x ATR" now says it must clear BOTH the ATR floor AND the cost floor from the
    block, whichever is larger. "For forex, minimum 20 pips. For stocks, minimum 0.5%." now
    also names crypto explicitly, pointing at the block instead of leaving it unstated.
  - Chev Prompt (Dexter-escalation section, right after the existing SKIP-conditions
    paragraph): 4 new lines — the block's numbers are hard limits, never propose a tighter
    SL, check invalidation candidates against the band before writing POST or SKIP, and any
    "too tight"/"too far" claim must cite the block's actual numbers. Section not otherwise
    restructured.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. The new helper's source was
extracted and exec'd standalone (NEVER imported dexter.py) against stub inputs covering all

case (atr=200, price=100,000 — a 0.2% ATR, deliberately low enough to force the cost floor
to win) that the rendered numbers match the phase spec's own worked values exactly:
  scalp: min SL 0.40% (cost floor) | min R:R 1.30:1 | min TP 0.84%

Also confirmed the ATR-floor branch engages correctly on a higher-volatility stub (atr=800
on the same price) — all three trade_types correctly switched to "(ATR floor)" and larger
numbers, proving the max()-of-two-floors logic actually branches both ways, not just one.

## TIMEFRAME FLOOR: STOP ESCALATING CRYPTO 5m — PHASE 4 (2026-07-06, RESTART REQUIRED)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: crypto 5m scalps almost never clear the cost gate (Phase 2) at a realistic
5m ATR stop — round-trip cost (fee + slippage) eats too large a share of the achievable R:R
at that stop distance for the timeframe to leave any room. Unlike every other fix this
session, this isn't a stale-data problem or a coaching gap that loosening or better
information can fix — the 5m chart itself doesn't contain enough room between "a stop tight
enough to be structurally honest" and "a stop wide enough to keep cost-per-R sane." Rather
than let Chev keep discovering this the hard way (get escalated, do the math, SKIP or get
cost-gated), the setup now never reaches him at all — but it still gets scanned and still
gets an Examiner shadow label, so if the data ever argues otherwise the floor can be revisited
with real evidence, not a guess.

DISCOVERY (done before any edit, per this phase's own STOP-CHECK requirement):
  (a) Setup timeframe is decided per-asset-type by `SCAN_TFS_CRYPTO = ["5m","15m","30m","1h",
      "4h"]` / `SCAN_TFS_FOREX = ["15m","30m","1h","4h"]` (dexter.py ~line 1600-1601) — stock
      shares the same list as forex (dexter.py ~line 9494: `tfs = SCAN_TFS_CRYPTO if
      item["type"]=="crypto" else SCAN_TFS_FOREX`), so neither forex nor stock scans 5m today.
      `TF_SECONDS` (~line 1588) gives each TF's ordering in seconds — used for the floor
      comparison instead of a hardcoded rank list.
  (b) The escalation decision sits at the END of a strictly sequential pre-gate chain, all in
      the main scan loop (dexter.py, per-result loop starting ~line 9509): confluence-score
      gate (no shadow label if it fails) → circuit breaker → Chev rate-limit → Chev health →
      escalation cooldown → forex event block → CHOPPY regime filter → the explicitly-named
      "TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE" block (TRADEABILITY score / STRUCT / DISTANCE / CONFLICT) → only
      then `ask_chev_to_judge(...)`. The new TF floor was added as the FIRST check inside the
      TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE block (before its threshold sub-checks), since that block's own
      stated purpose — "only escalate setups Chev is actually allowed to approve" — is exactly
      the category a hard TF floor belongs to.
  (c) DISCREPANCY FOUND AND RECONCILED: this phase's own instructions assumed neighboring
      pre-gates log rejections to chev_decisions.jsonl as decision "GATE_REJECT". Reading the
      actual code (all of circuit breaker / cooldown / event block / choppy regime /
      TRADEABILITY / STRUCT / DISTANCE / CONFLICT) shows every one of them ONLY calls
      `labeller.record_setup(result, asset_type, "NOT_ESCALATED", chev_meta={"reason": ...})`
      — none of them touch chev_decisions.jsonl. Grepping for "GATE_REJECT" confirms it's a
      real decision code, but it's written via `_log_chev_decision` (dexter.py:1821) only from
      gates that run AFTER Chev has already replied (e.g. the post-response SCORE GATE at
      ~line 9683) — a different layer entirely. Resolution: the new TF floor follows the REAL,
      existing pre-escalation convention (console print + `labeller.record_setup(...,
      "NOT_ESCALATED", chev_meta={"reason": "tf_below_escalation_floor"})`), not the assumed
      one — matching its actual neighbors exactly, and not implying Chev was ever consulted
      when he wasn't.

THE CHANGE — dexter.py only, two spots:
  - New constant `ESCALATION_TF_FLOOR = {"crypto": "15m", "forex": "5m", "stock": "5m"}`,
    added right after `EXPLORATION_MAX_DIST_PCT` in the EXPLORATION_MODE config block (~line
    1503), with a comment explaining the cost-vs-room reasoning and that forex/stock are
    no-ops today (kept explicit for if a faster TF is ever added to their scan lists).
  - New check inserted as the first line of the TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE block (dexter.py, right
    after its own opening comment, before `_trade_thr, _trade_max_dist = _active_thresholds
    (asset_type)`): looks up `ESCALATION_TF_FLOOR.get(asset_type)`, and if both `primary_tf`
    and the floor TF are known keys in `TF_SECONDS` and `TF_SECONDS[primary_tf] <
    TF_SECONDS[floor_tf]`, prints a "TF FLOOR" line, calls `labeller.record_setup(...,
    "NOT_ESCALATED", chev_meta={"reason": "tf_below_escalation_floor"})`, and `continue`s.
    Unknown/unmapped timeframes or asset types fail OPEN (escalate as normal) — never
    silently block on missing data.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. The exact inserted predicate was
re-implemented standalone (NEVER imported dexter.py) and run against 8 cases: crypto 5m
(blocked), crypto 15m/30m/4h (not blocked — 15m sits exactly at its own floor), forex 15m and
stock 15m (not blocked — also proves today's no-op for asset types that don't scan 5m), an
unknown TF string ("2m") and an unmapped asset_type — both correctly fail OPEN rather than
silently blocking. All 8 passed. Confirmed the live code's actual TF_SECONDS/ESCALATION_TF_FLOOR
values and comparison logic match the standalone test byte-for-byte via direct Read of the
inserted block.

WHAT KEV SHOULD SEE AFTER: crypto 5m setups stop appearing as Chev escalations entirely (no
more Telegram alerts or chev_decisions.jsonl entries for 5m crypto), but they should still
show up in the Examiner's shadow-label data (`labeller`/PENDING records) tagged
NOT_ESCALATED with reason "tf_below_escalation_floor" — worth spot-checking after restart to
confirm the shadow pipeline really does keep seeing them.

## TIME-STOP FOR OPEN TRADES — PHASE 5 (2026-07-06, RESTART REQUIRED, HIGHEST-RISK PHASE)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: `expiry_at` (2h scalp / 6h day / 48h swing, TRADE_TYPE_EXPIRY_HOURS,
dexter.py:1418) is computed once at proposal time and, before this phase, was ONLY ever
re-checked while a trade was still PENDING (to cancel an order that never filled). Once a
trade went OPEN, that same expiry_at just sat on the trade dict, unused forever — a "6-hour
day trade" that never hit SL or TP could squat open for days. Five July 1-3 positions were
doing exactly that, occupying all 3 day-trade concurrency slots (CONCURRENCY_CAP, risk
gauntlet gate 14) — 7 valid new setups died at that gate because of them. Trader logic: a
day trade that hasn't resolved in a day is a different trade nobody chose; either re-choose
it consciously (convert to swing) or free the capital and the slot.

SURVEY (done before any edit, per this phase's own hard stop-check):
  (a) OPEN branch / close-booking / close_type values: monitor function is
      `check_and_update_open_trades(worksheet, dashboard_ws, asset_types_to_check)`
      (dexter.py:8682). The OPEN branch runs from `is_long = trade["direction"]=="long"`
      through `still_open.append(trade)` / `open_trades = still_open`. There is no single
      shared "booking function" for a full close — the pattern (compute exit price/pnl/
      outcome/close_type -> update balance -> `worksheet.update(values=[[exit_price,
      exit_pnl,outcome,exit_pnl]], range_name=f"K{row}:N{row}")` -> build trade_copy with
      close_type set -> `threading.Thread(target=_do_postmortem, args=(trade_copy, outcome,
      pnl, exit_price), daemon=True).start()` -> `continue`) is duplicated inline at 4 sites
      (immediate-exit-at-fill, spot-fallback SL/TP, candle-true SL/TP, swing-management
      CHEV_CLOSE). `_do_postmortem` (dexter.py:2390) is the real shared piece — journal
      write, forensics, Chev post-mortem call, `honest_sim.record_close_R`. All close_type
      values in use before this phase: MANUAL, SIP_HIT, TP_HIT, SL_HIT, PARTIAL_25,
      PARTIAL_1R, CHEV_CLOSE, UNKNOWN. "Latest candle close price, same source as SL/TP":
      `honest_sim.get_exit_candles()` returns closed candles as {"t","o","h","l","c"} — used
      `exit_candles[-1]["c"]` when available, falling back to the live tick `price` when the
      candle fetch failed this cycle (same fallback convention the SL/TP path already uses).
  (b) Existing checkpoint machinery: the milestone HOLD/TAKE25/TAKE50/TRAIL_SL checkpoint is
      `_ask_chev_partial_tp` (dexter.py:7560) — builds a message (playbook + custom block +
      `_build_management_brief`), calls `_call_chev(...)`, and EXECUTES the decision itself
      inside the function on a background thread (never fully closes the trade, so no race
      with `still_open`). The swing 0.5R checkpoint, `ask_chev_manage_trade` (dexter.py:7685,
      renumbered ~7742 after this phase's insert above it), only builds+sends+returns the
      reply — the CALLER (inline in the main loop) parses CLOSE/TRAIL_SL and executes it,
      synchronously, because a full close has to mutate `still_open`/balance/sheet in the
      same place that owns them. Since time-stop can also fully close a trade, the new
      checkpoint (`_ask_chev_time_stop`) is modeled on `ask_chev_manage_trade`'s pattern, not
      `_ask_chev_partial_tp`'s — synchronous call, caller parses and executes.
  (c) close_type tolerance: `trade_forensics.py:144` only special-cases `close_type ==
      "SL_HIT"` (adds wick-vs-close / "would TP have hit later" diagnostic fields) — every
      other value, TIME_EXIT included, falls through untouched. `labeller.py` has ZERO
      references to close_type anywhere — fully agnostic. Both confirmed safe before adding
      TIME_EXIT.
  EXTRA FINDING, not anticipated by the phase spec, changed the plan: `load_state_from_sheet`
  (dexter.py:8134) only read `expiry_at` from the sheet (`row[16]`) INSIDE the
  `if status_clean == "PENDING":` branch. A trade that is already OPEN when Dexter restarts
  and reloads from the sheet got NO `expiry_at` in memory at all — since the column is
  written once at proposal time and never rewritten at fill, the value sitting in row[16] for
  an OPEN trade is still the correct original expiry, it just was never being read for that
  status. Left as-is, this would have made the entire phase inert for exactly the stale July
  1-3 positions it exists to catch. Fixed as part of this phase (same field, same column,
  same convention, just extended to both statuses) rather than treated as a separate issue.

THE CHANGE — dexter.py only:
  - `load_state_from_sheet`: moved the `expiry_at` read out of the PENDING-only branch so
    both PENDING and OPEN trades load it from `row[16]` on restart.
  - New helper `_ask_chev_time_stop(trade, current_price, hours_open, hours_allowed,
    price_r)` (dexter.py, right after `_ask_chev_partial_tp`) — builds the checkpoint message
    (playbook + `_build_management_brief` + a block stating symbol, trade_type, hours open
    vs hours allowed, current unrealized R, and both options CLOSE_NOW / CONVERT_TO_SWING
    verbatim), calls `_call_chev(..., timeout=90)`, returns the raw reply. Does not execute
    anything itself.
  - New block in the OPEN branch (dexter.py, right after SIP-transition detection, before the
    Chev milestone partial-TP section) — "── TIME-STOP CHECKPOINT ──": fires at most once per
    expiry event, guarded by `trade["time_stop_checkpoint_sent"]` (set to True BEFORE calling
    Chev, so a slow reply can't double-fire on a re-entry). Decision: if `trade["trade_type"]
    != "swing"` AND the reply starts with "CONVERT_TO_SWING" -> mutate ONLY `trade_type`
    ("swing"), `expiry_at` (now + 48h), and set `time_extended = True`; reset the checkpoint
    flag to False (a NEW expiry event, so it's allowed to fire exactly once more if the
    now-swing trade also times out) and write the two changed cells to the sheet
    (`update_cell(row, 16, "swing")`, `update_cell(row, 17, new_expiry)` — same column
    mapping convention as the existing TRAIL_SL cell writes). ANY other outcome — no reply,
    invalid reply, or the trade already being a swing (whether original or already-converted;
    same check, `trade_type == "swing"`, handles both) — force-closes through the exact same
    inline pattern every other exit above it uses, with `close_type = "TIME_EXIT"`.
  - SL/TP/PARTIAL/PENDING logic, `last_exit_check_ts`, the 1R house-partial, and SIP logic are
    completely untouched — this phase only adds a new block and reads one existing field
    earlier than before.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. The exact decision predicate
(expiry gate -> checkpoint fires? -> convert-or-close) was re-implemented standalone (NEVER
imported dexter.py) and run against: (a) fresh OPEN day trade well inside its window ->
checkpoint does not fire, dict unchanged; (b) expired day trade -> checkpoint fires; (c)
reply CONVERT_TO_SWING on a non-swing trade -> ONLY trade_type/expiry_at/time_extended/
checkpoint-flag change, all unrelated fields (entry/sl/tp/symbol/opened_at) provably
untouched; (d) an already-swing trade (time_extended=True) expiring again, even if Chev
replies CONVERT_TO_SWING once more -> forced CLOSE with close_type TIME_EXIT, proving the
once-per-trade cap actually holds; (e) an invalid/garbage reply and a None reply on an
eligible trade -> both CLOSE. Plus a guard case: a trade with `time_stop_checkpoint_sent`
already True does not fire again. All 15 assertions passed. Confirmed the live code's actual
conditionals (expiry comparison, guard-flag set-before-call ordering, the `trade_type !=
"swing"` eligibility check, the reply-matching) match the standalone test 1:1 via direct Read
of the inserted block.

*** WARN KEV, PROMINENTLY: on the first restart after this phase, the 3-5 stale July 1-3
positions will ALL trigger time-stop checkpoints within the first monitoring cycles. That is
the intended behavior this whole phase was built for, not a malfunction — expect several
CLOSE_NOW/CONVERT_TO_SWING Telegram-visible decisions and journal entries with close_type
TIME_EXIT (or a trade_type flip to swing) shortly after restart. ***

================================================================================
## HALLUCINATION GUARDS (TEMPLATE LEAK + FAR-PRICE SANITY) — PHASE 6
## (2026-07-06, RESTART + RE-PASTE REQUIRED)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: an audit of 58 real Chev posts found 2 cases where the TRADE: numbers could
not possibly belong to the live chart — an XRP proposal priced at literally the Chev Prompt's
own format example (entry=123.45, the exact number from the TRADE: line's illustrative
example), and a BTC short at 29,450 (a training-era price memory) against a live price of
62,711.95. Rare (~3% of posts) but each one poisons every downstream calculation (position
sizing, R:R, the risk gauntlet's math) and produces gibberish errors like "22175% consumed."
Two independent causes, two independent fixes — a leaky prompt example, and no Dexter-side
sanity check on the numbers Chev actually sends back.

THE CHANGE, PART (a) — "Chev Prompt", TRADE: format line:
  Previously the format line was a single fully-concrete example: `TRADE: direction=long,
  entry=123.45, sl=120.00, tp=130.00, ...` — a plausible-looking real price that an LLM can
  echo back verbatim under load, exactly what happened with the XRP case. Restructured so the
  ACTUAL format line Chev is told to follow uses named placeholders (`entry=<real entry price
  from THIS brief>`, `sl=<real structural invalidation price>`, etc. for every field) with an
  explicit instruction that every number must come from THIS setup's live data and never be
  copied from any example in the prompt. A separate, clearly-labelled "FAKE NUMBERS — format
  only" example is kept directly below it for field-layout learning, using deliberately
  absurd values (entry=999999.99 etc.) that don't resemble any real price for any watchlist
  asset (crypto tops out under ~100k, forex pairs sit under ~2, stocks are two/three digits)
  — so even if it leaked through verbatim, it would be caught by part (b) below, not silently
  accepted.
  *** THIS EDITS "Chev Prompt" — RE-PASTE INTO OPEN WEBUI REQUIRED. Editing the file on disk
  changes NOTHING until its content is manually pasted into Open WebUI's model system prompt.
  Do not skip this step. ***

THE CHANGE, PART (b) — dexter.py, new plausibility check:
  - New constants (next to `TRADE_TYPE_EXPIRY_HOURS`): `HALLUCINATION_MAX_ENTRY_DIST = 0.03`,
    `HALLUCINATION_MAX_SLTP_DIST = 0.15`. 3% for entry is deliberately generous — the
    DISTANCE pre-gate already caps a legitimate pending entry at 1.5% (exploration) from the
    confluence zone, so 3% sits well beyond any valid MODE-B pending and only catches numbers
    that plainly don't belong to this asset right now.
  - New block in the main escalation loop (ANCHOR: right after `_trade_originally_parsed =
    bool(parsed and parsed.get("trade"))`, before the SCORE GATE) — runs BEFORE every other
    post-parse gate, including GEOMETRY REVIEW, so nothing downstream does real ATR-ratio or
    R:R math on numbers that were never real. Compares `parsed["trade"]`'s entry/sl/tp against
    `result["current_price"]`: entry beyond `HALLUCINATION_MAX_ENTRY_DIST`, or sl/tp beyond
    `HALLUCINATION_MAX_SLTP_DIST`, collects a specific issue string per field ("entry <e> is
    <x>% from live <p>"). Fails OPEN if `current_price` is missing (never blocks on absent
    data, same convention as every other gate this phase touched or read this session).
  - If any issue fires: reuses the SAME same-thread retry mechanism as the POST:/SKIP:
    format reminder (append the assistant's reply + a correction message to `_chev_messages`,
    call `_call_chev` again on the same thread) — quotes Chev's exact numbers against the live
    price and asks for a corrected full TRADE: line or a SKIP. If the corrected reply still
    fails the same checks (or has no trade and isn't a SKIP either), logs `decision="REJECT"`
    with `reason="HALLUCINATED_LEVELS: <issue(s)>"` via the existing `_log_chev_decision`, and
    `continue`s — stopping all further processing of that escalation, matching the letter of
    the phase spec. If Chev's revision passes, or he switches to SKIP on the retry, processing
    continues normally with the corrected/updated `parsed`.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean. The exact issue-collection
predicate (the part before the Chev retry/logging side effects) was re-implemented standalone
(NEVER imported dexter.py) and run against 8 cases: the real BTC case (entry 29450 @ live
62711.95 -> caught), the real XRP case (entry 123.45, the exact prompt-leak number, @ a
realistic live XRP price -> caught), a legitimate pending entry 0.8% away -> passes, sl 20%
away (entry/tp fine) -> caught on the sl leg specifically without falsely flagging entry, tp
20% away -> caught, a missing current_price -> fails open with no issues (matches the live
`if _h_cur:` guard), and an entry sitting exactly AT the 3% floor -> not flagged (confirms the
comparison is strict greater-than, not >=). All 8 passed. Confirmed the live code's actual
predicate matches the standalone test 1:1 via direct Read of the inserted block.

================================================================================
## EXAMINER COUNTERFACTUAL REPORT (READ-ONLY, FIREWALLED) — PHASE 7 (2026-07-06)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: every gate decision in this system is currently justified by theory (costs,
EV, structure). This is the empirical audit of those decisions — it converts every future
"should we loosen X?" argument from opinion into a number, and it's the honest scorecard for
what exploration mode's data-buying is actually worth reading back.

THE FIREWALL (the reason this got its own phase instead of just being a labeller.py report
function): shadow "wins" must never leak into the real win-rate pool `compute_tag_win_rates`
reads — that would silently lower George's required R:R and admit worse trades. Hard rules
enforced in `counterfactual_report.py`: writes exactly one file, `counterfactual_report.txt`,
nothing else, ever; never imported by dexter.py/risk_gauntlet.py/labeller.py/honest_sim.py;
registers no scheduler/thread/Flask route; every number is labelled "shadow win rate," never
bare "win rate"; the output file opens with a fixed CAVEATS block (verbatim, see the script)
warning these numbers must never be merged into chev_journal.json or any tag win-rate calc.

DISCOVERY FINDINGS (done before any code, per the phase's hard stop-check):
  (a) labels_closed.jsonl schema (labeller.py record_setup/`_process_active`, read end to
      end): outcome field is `label` — `1`/`-1`/`0` (numeric: profit barrier, loss barrier,
      time-expiry drift) or the strings `"NO_FILL"`/`"VOID"`. `realized_R` is GROSS (exactly
      +-1.0 for barrier hits, drift-based for label 0) — `cost_R` is a SEPARATE field stored
      on the record at creation time (`_compute_cost_R()`), never netted into `realized_R`.
      Net R = `realized_R - cost_R`, matching labeller's own report functions' convention
      exactly (no double-application of costs).
  (b) LOAD-BEARING FINDING — how gate-killed POSTs appear in labels_closed.jsonl: THEY DON'T.
      Distinct `chev_decision` values actually present: NOT_ESCALATED (2497), SKIP (710),
      POST (3) — no "REJECT" value exists at all. Traced why: `labeller.record_setup(...,
      "POST", ...)` (dexter.py, confirmed anchor ~line 10306) fires ONLY inside the branch
      where a trade actually got locked (survived SCORE/STRUCT/MTF TAX/HALLUCINATION/
      GEOMETRY REVIEW/`risk_gauntlet.run_gauntlet()`) — the neighboring `else:` branch (a
      POST Chev proposed that a gate then killed, comment: "POST rejected upstream... not
      logged as a new trade") calls NOTHING on the Examiner. So a downstream gate-kill never
      gets a shadow barrier-walk — there is no shadow win rate/net R possible for COST_GATE,
      MTF_TAX, STRUCT_GATE, SCORE_GATE (GATE_REJECT), GEOMETRY, HALLUCINATED_LEVELS, etc.,
      full stop, not a data-cleaning gap. Real chev_decisions.jsonl REJECT reasons were text-
      classified during discovery: COST_GATE 38, PRICE_DRIFT 15, CONCURRENCY 12, HEAT_CAP 2,
      DATA_QUALITY 1 (that last one IS the pre-Phase-6 entry=123.45 hallucination case,
      caught retroactively as further evidence the old bug was real).
  (c) tf/trade_type are clean, present fields on every closed record — no join needed there.
      SKIP records' own `chev_reason` (Chev's one-line SKIP text) already carries enough
      signal to classify invalidation vs R:R vs other directly (verified against all 710 real
      SKIP records: 239 invalidation, 105 R:R, 366 other) — same for NOT_ESCALATED records,
      whose `chev_reason` IS the exact pre-gate name (below_trade_threshold, cooldown,
      struct_pregate, choppy_regime, tf_below_escalation_floor, conflicting_signals,
      event_block, below_threshold). Per the phase's own escape hatch ("if discovery shows
      labels already distinguish these, prefer the labels' own field and skip the matching"),
      NO cross-file (symbol/tf/timestamp) matching was implemented anywhere — every SKIP and
      NOT_ESCALATED bucket is populated straight from labels_closed.jsonl/labels_open.jsonl.

THE SCRIPT — `counterfactual_report.py` (new file, ~400 lines, zero project imports —
plain json/os/sys/datetime only; labeller.py was verified safe to import — proper
`__main__` guard, no module-level side effects beyond a `threading.Lock()` object and plain
constants — but wasn't needed since `cost_R` is already stored on every record):
  - `BASELINE_TS = "2026-07-06 04:26:00"` at the top of the file, clearly editable.
  - Buckets, each with real shadow stats (setups, resolved/coverage%, NO_FILL/VOID counts,
    fill rate, shadow win rate, avg net R, total net R, top 3 winners/losers by symbol/tf/
    date): SKIP - invalidation / SKIP - R:R / SKIP - other; one NOT_ESCALATED bucket per real
    pre-gate reason string found in the data; POST - all (reality anchor, thin sample — only
    3-4 records, since the Examiner's POST hook is this selective by design, noted loudly in
    the report itself).
  - Downstream gate-kills (COST_GATE, MTF_TAX, CONCURRENCY, PRICE_DRIFT, DATA_QUALITY,
    STRUCT_GATE, SCORE_GATE, GEOMETRY, HALLUCINATED_LEVELS, NET_RR, HEAT_CAP, CORR_CAP,
    LIQUIDATION): COUNTS ONLY from chev_decisions.jsonl, printed as "n/a shadow win rate/net
    R — no Examiner record" — never zero, never blank, never guessed.
  - Cross-bucket summary table ranking every bucket WITH real shadow R by total net R
    forfeited (downstream gate-kills correctly excluded — they have no R to rank).
  - Still-open/unresolved records (labels_open.jsonl) are counted toward `n_setups` and
    `coverage_pct` per bucket but NEVER given a guessed outcome — hard rule, enforced in
    `bucket_stats()` by construction (only `labels_closed.jsonl` rows ever populate label/R).

FIRST REAL RUN (2026-07-06, BASELINE_TS default): 845 of 3210 closed records and 230 of 244
open records fall at/after baseline; 382 of 2629 decisions. Selected numbers from the actual
output (full detail in counterfactual_report.txt, regenerated every run):
  SKIP - invalidation:  n=76 filled, shadow win rate 64.5%, total net R -16.70R
  SKIP - R:R:           n=29 filled, shadow win rate 69.0%, total net R  -6.04R
  SKIP - other:         n=60 filled, shadow win rate 58.3%, total net R -27.58R
  NOT_ESCALATED-below_trade_threshold: n=377 filled, win rate 61.3%, total net R -76.02R
  NOT_ESCALATED-cooldown:              n=76 filled,  win rate 57.9%, total net R -30.68R
  POST - all (reality anchor, n=3):    win rate 100%, total net R +2.45R
  Downstream gate-kills (counts only): COST_GATE 11, MTF_TAX 9, CONCURRENCY 6, PRICE_DRIFT 3,
  DATA_QUALITY 1, GEOMETRY 1.
  EVERY no-trade bucket in this window shows negative total shadow net R — i.e. across the
  board, in this specific window, the gates and Chev's skips would have cost more than they
  saved, at the Examiner's optimistic cost model. Read this with the CAVEATS at the top of
  the report firmly in mind (no checkpoint management, no partials, no concurrency limits
  modelled) before treating it as an argument to loosen anything — it's a first data point,
  not a verdict, and the sample skews toward 5m/15m scalp-ish reasons (below_trade_threshold
  alone is 377 of the filled total) which may not generalize to day/swing behavior.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile counterfactual_report.py` clean. `--selftest` mode
builds synthetic fixture records entirely in memory (never touches the real files) covering:
a SKIP-invalidation bucket with one hand-computed win and one loss (avg net R and total net R
asserted exactly), a SKIP-R:R label=0 drift outcome (net R asserted exactly, confirmed a
label=0 counts toward win rate as a non-win), a NOT_ESCALATED-cooldown bucket with one
NO_FILL (excluded from win rate) + one win + one still-open unresolved record (coverage %
asserted exactly), a NOT_ESCALATED-choppy_regime VOID-only bucket (shadow win rate asserts
None, not zero), a pre-baseline record proven filtered out of every bucket, and downstream
gate-kill counts classified and baseline-filtered correctly (a pre-baseline REJECT excluded).
19 assertions, all passed. Then run once against the real files — output reads coherently,
spot-checked the summary table's ranking and a few top winner/loser rows by eye.

FIREWALL CONFIRMATION: `grep -n "open(" counterfactual_report.py` shows exactly two calls —
`open(path, "r", ...)` inside the shared loader (used identically for all three read-only
input files) and `open(OUTPUT_FILE, "w", ...)` where `OUTPUT_FILE` is hardcoded to
`counterfactual_report.txt`. No other write/append call anywhere in the file. No project
file was modified this phase except handoff.txt — dexter.py, risk_gauntlet.py, labeller.py,
and "Chev Prompt" are all untouched.

OPTIONAL SUB-STEP 7B was skipped in PHASE 7 itself, per its own default scope. It has since
been implemented as its own phase — see BACKEND COUNTERFACTUAL ENDPOINT (PHASE 7B-1) below.

================================================================================
## BACKEND COUNTERFACTUAL ENDPOINT (PHASE 7B-1, 2026-07-06, RESTART REQUIRED)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: PHASE 7's counterfactual_report.py only ever produced a .txt file Kev had
to be at his desk to read. This is the backend half of putting the same numbers on the
phone — a read-only JSON endpoint, following the house pattern every other Strategy
Dashboard panel already uses (`_apiFetch('/api/strategy/...')`). No frontend work this
phase (that's 7B-2/3/4) — this is purely "can the phone GET the data," verified with
curl/browser, not yet wired into webapp/monitor.html.

DISCOVERY (done before any edit, per this phase's hard stop-check):
  (a) counterfactual_report.py (read in full) already had a `__main__` guard and its
      helper functions (`bucket_stats`, `_group_closed_open`, the classifiers) were already
      pure and side-effect-free at import time — BUT there was no single function
      returning the bucketing as a plain dict; `build_report()` interleaved computation
      directly into text-line assembly. Per the phase's own fallback instruction, the
      FIRST change was adding `build_counterfactual(baseline_ts=None, labels_closed_file=
      None, labels_open_file=None, decisions_file=None) -> dict` as the new shared,
      side-effect-free source of truth, then rewriting `build_report()` to render its text
      FROM that dict (via a new `_fmt_stat_block_from_bucket()` adapter) instead of
      computing independently — this is the "single source of truth" the phase's WHY
      calls for: the .txt and the JSON endpoint can now never quietly disagree.
  (b) Strategy route convention confirmed at `api_strategy_performance` (dexter.py ~line
      455): `@flask_app.route("/api/strategy/...")`, plain `def api_strategy_x():`,
      `flask_request.args.get(...)` for query params, `return jsonify({...})`. New route
      placed directly after it, before `api_strategy_heatmap`, matching this exactly.
  (c) Import safety confirmed two ways: (1) read confirms counterfactual_report.py's only
      module-level code is constant assignments and function/def statements — no threads,
      no loops, no network calls, no file I/O outside function bodies; (2) empirically
      timed a standalone `import counterfactual_report` (0.04s, zero side effects, then
      called `build_counterfactual()` successfully) before ever adding the import to
      dexter.py. `import counterfactual_report` added next to the other project imports
      (dexter.py, alongside `import risk_gauntlet` / `import honest_sim`).

THE CHANGE:
  - counterfactual_report.py: new `build_counterfactual(...)` (pure, read-only, no writes —
    loads the three source files, buckets SKIP/NOT_ESCALATED/downstream-gate-kills exactly
    as PHASE 7 did, then adds:
      • `verdict_split` per bucket — `{right, wrong, pending}`. A resolved, barrier-filled
        record is "right" if its shadow net R <= 0 (the skip/gate correctly dodged a
        loser) or "wrong" if net R > 0 (real edge was forfeited). For SKIP/NOT_ESCALATED
        buckets, "pending" = still-open (labels_open.jsonl) + NO_FILL + VOID — none of
        which have a verdict yet. For downstream gate-kill buckets (no Examiner record
        exists at all), ALL setups are folded into "pending" too, but this means something
        different there — "no shadow data will ever exist," not "will resolve later" —
        documented inline in the code so a future reader doesn't conflate the two.
      • `headline: {dodged_r, forfeited_r}` — dodged_r = sum of |net R| over every "right"
        verdict across ALL SKIP+NOT_ESCALATED buckets combined (total shadow loss
        magnitude correctly avoided); forfeited_r = sum of net R over every "wrong" verdict
        (total shadow gain magnitude missed). Cross-checked against PHASE 7's own bucket
        totals: forfeited_r - dodged_r ≈ the sum of every bucket's total_net_R, confirming
        internal consistency with the original report.
      • `coverage: {total, resolved}` — scoped to the SKIP+NOT_ESCALATED shadow-trackable
        universe only (summed n_setups / n_closed) — downstream gate-kills are deliberately
        excluded since "coverage" implies resolvability, and theirs never will.
      • `shadow_tags` / `shadow_combos` — per-individual-tag and per-full-combination
        shadow stats (n, resolved, shadow_wr, total_r), aggregated over SKIP+NOT_ESCALATED
        records only, using Dexter's own `features` token list (present on every record
        regardless of decision type) — NEVER `chev_tags`, which discovery confirmed is only
        ever populated on POST records (the SKIP/NOT_ESCALATED `record_setup` call sites
        never pass a "tags" key at all). Entirely independent of, and never merged with,
        `compute_tag_win_rates`'s real-trade leaderboard (DO-NOT-TOUCH respected).
      • `resolved_items` — flat, most-recent-first, per-record list with
        `{ts, symbol, tf, decision, bucket_key, shadow_r, verdict}`, capped at
        `RESOLVED_ITEMS_CAP = 300` so neither the .txt nor a phone ever has to receive an
        unbounded, ever-growing list. The .txt shows its 15 most recent as a compact "raw
        log" preview; the full (capped) list goes out over the JSON endpoint.
  - `build_report()` rewritten to call `build_counterfactual()` and render every existing
    section (SKIP/NOT_ESCALATED/POST/downstream-gate-kill/summary) from its returned dict,
    plus three brand-new .txt sections: SHADOW TAG LEADERBOARD, SHADOW COMBO LEADERBOARD,
    and RESOLVED ITEMS — RAW LOG.
  - dexter.py: `import counterfactual_report` (next to the other project imports). New
    route `GET /api/strategy/counterfactual` (right after `api_strategy_performance`):
    module-level cache `{ts, payload}` + `COUNTERFACTUAL_CACHE_SECS = 300`; recomputes only
    when the cache is empty or older than that; `?force=1` bypasses the cache but is itself
    rate-limited via `_counterfactual_last_force_ts` to once per 30 seconds (a refresh-
    spamming client can't defeat the cache's whole purpose). Response strips
    `build_counterfactual()`'s "_"-prefixed internal fields (raw winner/loser record dicts,
    used only by the .txt renderer) down to exactly the public schema: generated_at,
    baseline_ts, cache_age_secs, coverage, headline, buckets (key/label/kind/n/resolved/
    shadow_wr/avg_r/total_r/verdict_split only), shadow_tags, shadow_combos, resolved_items.
    GET-only; no mutation; no Chev/journal/Sheets/Firebase access anywhere in the route.

VERIFICATION DONE: `python -m py_compile counterfactual_report.py dexter.py` clean.
`python -X utf8 counterfactual_report.py --selftest` — 34 assertions (the original 20 from
PHASE 7, all still passing unchanged, plus 14 new ones covering `build_counterfactual()`'s
top-level keys, verdict_split on a mixed right/wrong/pending bucket, a downstream gate-kill
bucket's resolved=0/shadow_wr=None shape, hand-computed headline dodged_r/forfeited_r,
coverage totals, shadow_tags/shadow_combos aggregation, resolved_items shape, and a final
check that `build_report()`'s text output and `build_counterfactual()`'s dict never
disagree on the same fixtures) — all passed. Then run once against the real files (851
closed / 243 open / 389 decisions in-window) — output reads coherently; cross-checked
headline math (forfeited_r - dodged_r ≈ -202R) against PHASE 7's own per-bucket totals
(-200R) as an independent sanity check. Route logic (cache hit/miss, force bypass, force
rate-limiting, cache expiry) re-implemented standalone (NEVER imported dexter.py) and run
against 6 scenarios — all passed, matching the live inserted predicate exactly.

Import-safety re-confirmed empirically: `import counterfactual_report` timed at ~0.04s with
zero observable side effects before it was ever added to dexter.py.
