## INVALIDATION-LEVEL BOTTLENECK — OPEN INVESTIGATION (2026-07-06 09:01, no code changed)
================================================================================

WHAT PROMPTED THIS: a few hours after the NET_RR staleness fix (04:26 baseline), Kev asked
Claude to check the logs again — Chev was still rejecting nearly everything, and Kev hadn't
seen anything post to Telegram. Confirmed Dexter is online, 5 open positions, all from
July 1-3, nothing new. Pulled the last ~4 hours of chev_decisions.jsonl (129 entries,
2026-07-06 03:51-07:50) and found two things, one good, one new:

THE GOOD NEWS — NET_RR FIX CONFIRMED WORKING: NET_RR's share of skip reasons dropped from
35% (7 of 20, in the window checked before the fix) to 6% (8 of 129) in this window, and
the required ratios it's now citing (2.83, 2.97, 3.07) match the NEW post-fix numbers from
the fix itself, not the old inflated 3.07-3.85 range. The rolling-window + shrinkage fix is
live and doing what it was built to do.

THE NEW FINDING — A DIFFERENT GATE IS NOW DOMINANT: 77 of 129 skips (60%) — up from ~25%
in the pre-fix window — now cite an invalidation-placement problem, with a consistent
bimodal shape: the nearest real structural level is either TOO CLOSE (0.3-0.6% away —
normal noise would stop it out) or TOO FAR (2%+ away — breaks the risk/reward math), with
almost nothing landing in the comfortable middle. Real examples: TRXUSDT 0.57% away (too
tight), AAVEUSDT 0.5% and separately 0.3% away (too tight), ZECUSDT and BTCUSDT both 2.1%
away on their nearest swing (too far). All SKIP decisions (Chev's own judgment), not a
Dexter-side gate — confirmed by checking `decision` on every one of the 77.

DETECTION-SIDE INVESTIGATION (dexter.py) — LIKELY NOT A BUG:
  - Raw swing detection (`find_swings`, dexter.py:2832) is reasonably fine-grained: 3-candle
    window, only a 0.3% retracement needed to confirm a swing, checked within an 8-bar
    window. Dense, but mostly clustered close to current price (recent noise).
  - "Validated" SR levels (the ones Chev's told to trust) require multiple confirmed
    touches: MIN_TOUCHES_PER_TF = {"15m": 5, "30m": 3, "1h": 2, "4h": 2} (dexter.py:1575) —
    deliberately sparse, especially on faster timeframes, specifically so noise doesn't get
    mistaken for real structure.
  - CONCLUSION: the gap between "unvalidated noise right next to price" and "the next
    actually-validated level" is a natural consequence of a conservative, multi-touch
    validation bar meeting normal price behavior — not obviously a coarse-detection bug.
    Also likely still connected to the SAME root theme as the NET_RR fix: required R:R is
    still 2.0-3.0:1 for day trades even post-fix, so even a legitimately-placed medium-
    distance stop often still needs a fairly distant target to clear that bar. Not
    confirmed as fully separate from the NET_RR story — may be the same underlying tightness
    showing up in a different gate.

OPEN QUESTION RAISED BY KEV, NOT YET RESOLVED: does DEMANDING more specificity in Chev's
reasoning (the reasoning-specificity fix, ~04:26) itself make him MORE cautious/skip-prone?
The concern, worth taking seriously: defending a SKIP only requires citing ONE specific
broken thing; defending a POST requires MULTIPLE mandatory fields to all check out at once
(4H STRUCTURE, INVALIDATION, ENTRY BASIS, REASONING all separately required) — an LLM asked
to be rigorous can be structurally biased toward whichever answer is easier to justify
convincingly, and "I found one flaw" is less work than "everything specific lines up."
Mitigating factor already in place: the number-citation rule was applied SYMMETRICALLY (both
POST's REASONING and SKIP's WHAT WAS MISSING must cite a real number) — not skip-only. But
the deeper structural asymmetry (more mandatory fields on POST than SKIP) still exists and
wasn't addressed. Could not be tested cleanly from this session's data — too many other
changes landed in the same few hours to isolate the effect. HOW TO TEST IT LATER: once the
NET_RR and invalidation issues are no longer the dominant blockers, watch whether the raw
skip rate holds steady or keeps climbing — if setups are genuinely improving but Chev keeps
finding new specific reasons to decline at the same rate, that's the signal this is real.
Possible fix if confirmed: an explicit counter-instruction that a well-specified reason to
skip is not inherently more rigorous than a well-specified reason to take the trade.

NEXT STEPS (per Kev, 2026-07-06 09:01): no changes made this round on purpose — Kev is
giving the system more runway before touching anything else. Come back to this section
after a few more hours of logs accumulate and re-check: (1) has the invalidation-related
skip share moved from ~60%, (2) has the raw skip rate itself changed at all, (3) any new
dominant pattern that wasn't visible in this smaller sample.

## DERIVATIVES LAYER (derivs.py, added 2026-07-04)
================================================================================

C:\ChevTools\derivs.py — Binance USDT-M perpetual futures context: funding rate + open
interest trend, for crypto symbols only. 5-minute per-symbol cache shared by the scanner
and the brief builder (one network round-trip per symbol per 5 min, not per caller).

get_derivs(symbol) → {"funding_rate", "open_interest", "oi_chg_6h_pct", "oi_chg_24h_pct"}
or None on any fetch failure (cached either way for the TTL).

classify_derivs(funding_rate, oi_chg_6h_pct, price_chg_6h_pct) — PURE, unit-tested
function, no network. Funding is read as a CONTRARIAN signal (crowded side pays to stay
in — fuel for a squeeze against them). OI × price is a participation matrix: price+OI
both up = bullish confirmation (real participation); price up + OI down = bearish
divergence (weak rally); price down + OI down = bullish divergence (short covering);
price down + OI up = bearish confirmation. See CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM above for the
point values. Self-test: `python -X utf8 derivs.py` → 12/12 passing.

Wired into scan_pair_tf (crypto only) — contributes to total_score and to the
TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE's conflict-gate bull/bear split via reason-string keywords
("bullish"/"bearish") so _directional_split() classifies it correctly. Also upgraded the
Futures block in Chev's market brief — now shows 6h/24h OI trend and a how-to-read line,
not just a bare funding/OI snapshot. The old _fetch_binance_futures_data() function is
left defined but orphaned (deprecated, same convention as _sim_trading_cost) — do not
delete it, do not resurrect it.

================================================================================
## TRADE FORENSICS (trade_forensics.py, added 2026-07-04)
================================================================================

C:\ChevTools\trade_forensics.py — post-trade path attribution. Pure functions, no
network, no state — same pattern as derivs.py. Self-test: `python -X utf8
trade_forensics.py` → 19/19 passing.

compute_forensics(trade, candles) → dict with EXACTLY these keys: r_dist, mae_r, mfe_r,
bars_held, exit_type_detail, stopped_then_ran, rsi_entry, rsi_exit.
  - r_dist/mae_r/mfe_r require trade["sl_original"] (added at trade creation, see below);
    None for all three if it's missing rather than guessing.
  - exit_type_detail ('wick' vs 'close') and stopped_then_ran (did price reach the
    ORIGINAL tp before re-touching sl_original) are SL-exit-only; stopped_then_ran uses
    the same pessimistic same-candle tie-break as labeller.py (both touched same candle
    → loss wins → False).
  - rsi_entry/rsi_exit are None unless at least 20 candles precede the entry index in the
    supplied candle list (real warm-up, not a garbage Wilder's-RSI value).
  - Internally locates the actual exit candle by walking forward from entry looking for
    the first SL/TP touch — NOT by assuming "last candle in the list", since callers may
    append post-exit candles for the stopped_then_ran check.

Wired into dexter.py:
  1. Trade creation (single call site, right after log_new_trade() in the main escalation
     loop): new_trade["sl_original"]/["tp_original"] stamped alongside the existing
     original_sl/original_tp fields (different field names, deliberately additive —
     original_sl/original_tp already meant something else to honest_sim).
  2. _do_postmortem (fires on every full close): fetches candles via
     _fetch_candles_for_labeller (reused, no new fetch path) at a timeframe keyed by
     trade_type — scalp→5m, day→15m, swing→1h — with a 30-bar buffer before opened_at for
     RSI warm-up. Result stored on the journal entry under the key "forensics". Wrapped so
     any failure logs one line and never blocks the close/journal path.
  3. _run_learning_session: once ≥10 closed entries for an asset type carry a forensics
     dict, a "TRADE PATH FORENSICS (n=X)" block is appended to the learning input (NOT a
     new playbook section) with exactly 5 aggregates: % SL losses classified 'wick', %
     SL losses where stopped_then_ran, median MFE of losers, median MAE of winners,
     average bars held wins vs losses. Below 10 samples: nothing appended.

================================================================================
## DEXTER SCAN STRINGS — EXACT FORMATS (important for REASON_MAP)
================================================================================

These are the verbatim strings dexter's scan_pair_tf() puts in result["reasons"].
The Examiner's normalize_reasons() maps these to canonical tokens. Knowing the
exact format prevents substring pollution (e.g. "EMA55 support" → ema55, not sr).

  SR:        "Resistance(3x,3pt)"  "Support(2x,2pt)"   format: {Label}({N}x,{pts}pt)
             Resistance = sr_multi if N>=3, sr_single if N<=2. Same for Support.
  Fib:       "Fib 61.8% (golden pocket) (2pt)"  "Fib 50% (2pt)"  "Fib 38.2%"
  GP:        "★ GOLDEN POCKET"
             "★★ GP×SR DEADLY COMBO (×1.15 quality bonus applied)"  → gp_sr_combo
  GP watch:  "[WATCH — approaching GP] GP zone [...]..."  → gp_approach (not scored)
  RSI div:   "Regular Bearish Divergence (str=1.5pt)"  "Hidden Bullish (str=1.0pt)"
             "Hidden Bearish (str=1.0pt)"  "Regular Bullish Divergence (str=1.0pt)"
  Forming:   "[WATCH — not yet confirmed] FORMING bullish divergence (RSI gap Xpt, Y bars, str=Zpt)"
             → rsi_div_forming (NEVER maps to rsi_div — separate stat bucket)
  EMA:       "EMA55 support (2.0pt)"  "EMA21 resistance (1.0pt)"  "EMA13 support (0.5pt)"
             format: "{ema_label} {side} ({weight}pt)"
  EMA cross: "EMA crossover bullish_cross 2c ago"  → ema_cross
  BB:        "BB upper BURST (%B=1.12, 12.0% of band outside, 2pt)"  → bb_burst
             "BB lower BURST (%B=-0.05, ...)"                         → bb_burst
             "BB near upper (%B=0.88, top 15% of band, 0.5pt)"       → bb_near
             "BB near lower (%B=0.12, ...)"                           → bb_near
             "BB mid support (%B=0.50, 1pt)"                          → bb_mid
             "BB mid resistance (%B=0.50, 1pt)"                       → bb_mid
             "BB squeeze (width 1.2%, context, 0pt)"                  → bb_squeeze (0pt since 2026-07-04 — see CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM)
  VP:        "VP POC 4h (0.15% away ≤0.40% prox, 3pt)"               → vp_poc
             "VP VAH 1h (...)"  → vp_vah     "VP VAL 4h (...)"  → vp_val
             Unconfirmed-anchor variant (half points): "VP POC 4h (0.12% away ≤0.40%
             prox, unconfirmed-anchor, 1.5pt)" — same vp_poc/vah/val token, note is inline.
  RSI level: "RSI OVERBOUGHT (82.3, 0.5pt)"  → rsi_ob
             "RSI OVERSOLD (18.1, 0.5pt)"    → rsi_os
             "RSI crossed 50 up 2 bar(s) ago"  → rsi_50_cross (context, 0pt)
  Sweep:     "Sweep:buy_side (3pt)"  "Sweep:sell_side (3pt)"  → sweep
  Pattern:   "ascending_triangle (bullish, conf=0.75) BREAKOUT+vol"  → pattern_breakout_vol
             "head_and_shoulders (bearish, conf=0.65) BREAKOUT"      → pattern_breakout
             "bull_flag (bullish, conf=0.55)"                        → pattern_high_conf or mid_conf
  Derivs (crypto only, added 2026-07-04, from derivs.py — see DERIVATIVES LAYER section):
             "Funding extreme +0.0812% — crowded longs, bearish squeeze risk (3pt)"
                                                                       → funding_extreme
             "OI divergence — price +2.1% on OI -3.4% — weak rally, bearish (1.5pt)"
                                                                       → oi_divergence
             "OI confirmation — price +2.1% with OI +3.0% — bullish participation (1pt)"
                                                                       → oi_confirm

Ordering rule in normalize_reasons(): S/R detected by regex (^(Resistance|Support)\(\d+x,),
patterns detected by "conf=" substring. All other strings matched against REASON_MAP_ORDERED
list, longest/most-specific pattern first. EMA55/21/13 entries appear before any generic
"support"/"resistance" substring would match, preventing cross-contamination.

================================================================================
## VISUAL ANCHORS (drawn on chart when trade is clicked)
================================================================================

If Chev tags sr or sr_Xtf  → adds sr_level=<price> to TRADE: line
If Chev tags fib or fib_Xtf → adds fib_high=<price>, fib_low=<price>
If Chev tags vp             → adds vp_start=<YYYY-MM-DD>
If Chev tags rsi or rsi_Xtf → pill click now triggers live Dexter scan (see below)
If Chev tags ms or ms_Xtf  → no anchor needed, chart auto-overlays higher TF candles

      the actual point of the tab)

  Does NOT modify any data cells. Skip Log tab is skipped gracefully (with a
  message) if it doesn't exist yet — restart Dexter once first to auto-create it.

## STRATEGY DASHBOARD (webapp/index.html, added 2026-07-05)
================================================================================

WHY THIS EXISTS: Kev and Alejandro kept confusing themselves trying to understand "is
Chev/Dexter actually working" from raw log files and the static ALEJANDRO_GUIDE.html
(a well-made but PURELY EXPLANATORY walkthrough of the architecture — it teaches the
concept, it was never meant to show live activity). The chart webapp's existing job is
verifying tool accuracy (are the SR/Fib/VP overlays correct) — a different job entirely.
Nothing showed live strategy activity in a legible way; that gap is what this fills.

WHERE IT LIVES: a full-screen overlay (`#strategyOverlay`), not a cramped side-panel tab —
the existing right-side "intel panel" (Trades/Engine/Arsenal/Chat/Radar tabs) didn't have
the real estate for an equity curve, a heatmap, and a live feed at once. Opens via the new
🔥 fire-icon button in the top bar (`#strategyBtn`, next to the search box), same
open/close/backdrop-click/Escape pattern as the existing Ctrl+K command palette
(`#cmdPaletteOverlay` — copied the pattern deliberately for consistency).

FIVE TABS, in order:
  Overview      — scorecard strip (win rate, profit factor, expectancy, total closed, net
                  P&L), a live equity curve (lightweight-charts area series, same library
                  the main chart already uses), and a day-of-week x hour-of-day (UTC) setup
                  volume heatmap over the last 14 days. Also a quiet-system alert banner
                  that triggers automatically if there's been no POST in 12+ hours — so
                  Kev finds out from the dashboard, not by asking Claude to check.
  Chev's Thoughts — the live feed. Filterable pills (All/Posted/Skipped/Gate-Rejects).
                  Each card shows a Chev-branded emoji (webapp/emoji/*.png — fire.png for
                  POST, lets-see.png for SKIP, wrench.png for mechanical gate/gauntlet
                  rejects, oh-no.png for format errors) and his actual reasoning TEXT, not
                  raw JSON. SKIP cards get a red left border + a 15%-opacity red wash
                  bleeding in from the edge (`.stratFeedCard.isSkip`); POST cards the same
                  treatment in green; gate/gauntlet rejects in orange — the visual language
                  Kev asked for specifically.
  Why It Skips  — the funnel (not-escalated-by-pre-gate reasons, from the Examiner's shadow
                  log which sees setups even before Chev does → escalated → POST/SKIP/
                  reject breakdown → actually opened) and a sorted reason-frequency bar
                  chart, both over the last 24h.
  Performance   — win rate by grade, the confluence TAG leaderboard (real win rates, red-
                  to-gold-to-green), the confluence COMBINATION leaderboard (new, dimmed
                  below n=5 — see compute_combo_win_rates above), and the Planned R:R
                  distribution (Dexter's real cost-adjusted formula — see
                  compute_planned_rr above, NOT a realized-outcome approximation).
  Raw Log       — a plain searchable table over the same feed data, for the rare moment a
                  card isn't enough and the exact logged line is needed.

THE MODE BADGE IS A LIVE CONTROL, NOT JUST A DISPLAY: click it and (after a confirm()
dialog describing exactly what changes) it POSTs to /api/strategy/toggle_exploration,
flipping EXPLORATION_MODE in the running dexter.py process immediately — no restart. This
was Kev's "wouldn't it be cool" idea, built as asked. Deliberately scoped narrow: it only
flips WHICH of the two already-reviewed profiles (_NORMAL/_EXPLORATION in risk_gauntlet.py)
is active — there is no way over HTTP to edit the actual numbers inside those profiles.
Kev explicitly wants that separate, bigger feature — an editable-parameter UI — locked
behind a password ("BeijingCocktail69!") before it's ever built, specifically BECAUSE the
confluence/risk numbers are calibrated from real statistical data and he doesn't want them
changed casually. NOT BUILT YET, by design — flagged here as a known, deliberately-deferred
next step, not an oversight.

DATA SOURCES — all read-only except the toggle above, nothing here touches trading logic:
  chev_decisions.jsonl              — the live feed + raw log + funnel's decision breakdown
  chev_journal.json                 — scorecard, equity curve, R:R distribution, grade/tag/
                                       combo win rates (via risk_gauntlet's compute_* fns)
  labeller.OPEN_FILE / CLOSED_FILE  — funnel's NOT_ESCALATED reasons (only source that sees
                                       setups Dexter rejected before Chev ever judged them)
                                       + the heatmap's dow/hour_utc stamps
  risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile()— mode badge's live numbers

DELIBERATELY NOT A GOOGLE SHEET: considered and rejected. The raw data already exists
locally in the files above; a Sheet would add a slow round-trip for a live-updating
dashboard with no real benefit over reading files Dexter already writes. Sheets remain
useful as a human-browsable export (which already exists for closed trades) — just not as
this dashboard's live source.

KNOWN GAPS, honestly, since this is a first baseline meant to be iterated on:
  - Grade-accuracy panel will look sparse — `setup_grade` is blank on most historical closed
    trades, a real data gap, not a rendering bug.
  - Combo leaderboard has almost no trustworthy samples yet (same gap as tag-combination EV
    — see RISK GAUNTLET section) — visible and dimmed, not hidden, on purpose.
  - Planned R:R defaults trade_type to "day" when computing cost for closed trades, since
    chev_journal.json doesn't store trade_type on close — see compute_planned_rr above.
  - No password-protected parameter editor yet — deliberately deferred, see above.

================================================================================
## RSI DIVERGENCE — FULL ARCHITECTURE (important — many bugs fixed here)
================================================================================

TWO types of divergence Dexter detects:

1. CONFIRMED DIVERGENCE — past, already happened
   Functions: _ca_detect_rsi_divergence(df), detect_rsi_divergence(df),
              _detect_hidden_divergence(df)
   These find TWO confirmed swing pivots where price and RSI disagreed.
   Output includes: ts_t1, price_t1, rsi_t1, ts_t2, price_t2, rsi_t2, bias, tf
   The website draws solid green/red trendlines connecting the two pivots.

2. FORMING DIVERGENCE — live, predictive
   Functions: _detect_forming_divergence(df)
   Finds one CONFIRMED pivot + CURRENT mini-extreme as second point.
   Output includes: forming=True, ts_t1, price_t1, rsi_t1, ts_t2, price_t2, rsi_t2, bias
   Displayed as dashed amber trendlines. Projection extends 4 bars ahead at same slope.
   IMPORTANT: forming divergence is tagged "[WATCH — not yet confirmed]" in result["reasons"]
   and maps to token rsi_div_forming in the Examiner. Never mixed with confirmed rsi_div stats.

PREVIOUS DEAD APPROACHES (don't retry these):
  - conf.RSI_DIV_T1 / conf.RSI_DIV_T2: fields Chev was supposed to fill. Dead path.
  - Using the RSI validation guard to confirm direction: too aggressive, kills drawings.
    Guard only affects RSI panel line, never the price trendline.

================================================================================
## HOW DEXTER CALLS CHEV (key function: ask_chev_to_judge)
================================================================================

Located at ~line 3590 in dexter.py. Called when scan_pair_tf() detects 3+ confluences.

The message sent to Chev includes (in order):
1.  Chev's asset-specific playbook (chev_playbook_crypto/forex/stocks.txt)
2.  Recent relevant journal entries (last 3 same asset type + last 2 any type)
3.  Current open/pending positions (full list with entry/SL/TP/R:R) + correlation note
4.  Confluence re-entry pattern warning (A+C check — same level + same tags failed
    recently fires "PATTERN ALERT" or soft note; 2-hour window, last 30 losses)
5.  Full market brief (primary TF full candle dump + rich summaries for other TFs):
      - 4H MACRO TREND CONTEXT block — near the top, before Fib:
        "STRONG UPTREND / UPTREND / RANGING / DOWNTREND / STRONG DOWNTREND"
        Shows: net % move over ~3 days, HH/HL or LH/LL count, volume profile note,
        and a trend implication warning
      - Price snapshot (price, VWAP, EMA20, RSI, ATR, volume, BB)
      - Fibonacci levels
      - S/R zones (validated across 15m/30m/1h/4h, touch count shown)
      - Volume Profile (4H + 1H, anchor-based)
      - Previous day H/L/C
      - ADR for forex/stocks (with "x% of daily range already used" warning)
      - Forming + confirmed RSI divergence
      - BOS/CHoCH structural event
      - Zone dwell analysis (prior rejection count at confluence level)
      - MACD summary
6.  Session context (PEAK/GOOD/LOW) + economic calendar warnings
7.  Dexter's detected confluence zone + reasons + distance from level
8.  Direction hint (structural context: "near support/resistance — read the structure")
9.  Market regime (4H ADX + EMA regime label)
10. COUNTER-TREND ALERT — fires when confluence is near resistance in an uptrend or
    near support in a downtrend. 5-point checklist (score ≥ 1.5× the normal per-asset
    threshold — computed live, no longer a hardcoded "13" — confirmed divergence,
    4H BOS/CHoCH, structural SL, scalp only). "If you cannot articulate points 2-3 → SKIP"
11. RSI forming divergence block (if detected)
12. Engine survey (market state + geometry + auction hypothesis)
13. TOOLS AVAILABLE — explicit instructions to call before deciding
14. Full trading rules (SL placement, R:R, pending orders, SIP, scoring table)
15. ABSOLUTE RULES (SL direction, structural SL only — the flat "R:R ≥ 2.0" line that used
    to be here is gone; both R:R checks downstream are now EV/profile-based, not fixed)

If Chev's reply doesn't start with POST:/SKIP:, Dexter retries once with reminder. Two
SEPARATE gates fire after that, in order — GEOMETRY REVIEW (below), then RISK GAUNTLET
(its own section right after). Balance guard: cap only fires if balance > 0.

================================================================================
## GEOMETRY REVIEW (dexter.py, ~line 9304 — runs AFTER Chev posts, BEFORE risk_gauntlet)
================================================================================

An earlier, simpler sanity pass on Chev's actual entry/SL/TP numbers — separate from
risk_gauntlet.py entirely (different function, different file, was even using different
hardcoded numbers until 2026-07-05 — see below). Think of it as a spell-check before the
real grammar check: catches obviously broken geometry fast, in the same reply Chev just
gave, before the heavier gauntlet math runs.

Three checks, all computed from Chev's own proposed entry/sl/tp/position_size_usd:

1. ATR SL check — SL distance is compared against ATR_FLOOR[trade_type] × current ATR
   (from the active profile — see below). Two zones, not just pass/fail:
     RED zone (< 50% of the minimum): hard reject, goes into the retry message.
     YELLOW zone (50-100% of the minimum): logged as "SL WARN" but allowed through —
     a warning, not a block. Only red-zone failures trigger the retry.
2. R:R minimum check — Chev's TP/SL ratio must clear the flat MIN_NET_RR floor for this
   trade_type (from the active profile). This is the FLAT floor only, not the EV/tag-based
   one — this check runs before the gauntlet, so it doesn't have tag-win-rate context yet.
   If it fails, the message suggests a specific TP price that WOULD clear the ratio and
   asks Chev to check whether a real structural level sits near it.
3. Position size cap — implied margin (position_size_usd ÷ leverage) can't exceed the
   grade's max risk_pct by more than 25% tolerance. Catches Chev requesting an oversized
   position before it ever reaches the gauntlet's own (more precise) sizing math.

If ANY check fails, all the issues are batched into ONE retry message in the same
conversation thread (same pattern as the gauntlet's own retry) — Chev gets one chance to
revise the TRADE: line or reply SKIP:. No second retry after that; whatever comes back is
final for this escalation.

WHY THIS EXISTS AS A SEPARATE STEP FROM RISK GAUNTLET: it's cheap and catches the most
common, obvious mistakes (SL way too tight, TP way too close) in the same breath as
parsing Chev's reply — no need to run the full 14-gate deterministic engine (sizing,
leverage derivation, liquidation math, portfolio heat, correlation) just to tell Chev "your
TP is too close, try again." It's a fast pre-filter, not a duplicate of the real gate.

THE BUG THIS USED TO HAVE (found + fixed 2026-07-05): until this date, this check used its
OWN hardcoded numbers — a flat `_min_rr = 2.0` for every grade and trade_type, and its own
ATR multiplier table `{"scalp":1.0, "day":1.5, "swing":2.5}` — completely disconnected from
risk_gauntlet.py's numbers (which were already different: day floor 1.2× not 1.5×, swing
1.5× not 2.5×) AND from EXPLORATION_MODE. This was a real, previously undocumented FOURTH
source of the flat "2.0:1 R:R" belief Chev kept citing in his own reasoning all session —
even after the gauntlet itself became EV-aware, this earlier check was still handing Chev
a flat 2.0 in every retry message. Fixed by adding `risk_gauntlet.get_active_profile(
exploration_mode)` (a small public accessor into the same _NORMAL/_EXPLORATION dicts the
gauntlet uses) and having this check read `ATR_FLOOR`/`MIN_NET_RR` from that instead of its
own copies. One source of truth now, shared by both checks, both linked to the same
EXPLORATION_MODE flag.

================================================================================
## RISK GAUNTLET (risk_gauntlet.py)
================================================================================

C:\ChevTools\risk_gauntlet.py — Pre-trade risk validation + deterministic sizing,
21/21 tests passing. THIS SECTION WAS PREVIOUSLY STALE (described only 5 simple gates
from an early version) — rewritten 2026-07-05 against the actual current source, which
has grown to 14 sequential gates. Trust this version over any earlier summary.

Called by Dexter immediately after Chev posts a TRADE: line (main escalation loop, and
again on the fill-time re-check — see FILL-TIME PENDING RE-VALIDATION below). Chev's
requested risk_pct/leverage/position_size_usd are a REQUEST, not the final word — leverage
in particular is always DERIVED from margin budget and safety caps, never simply what
Chev asked for.

Gates, in order:
  1. Equity floor — no new trades when equity (free cash + all reserved margin,
     deliberately excluding unrealized PnL) is below MIN_EQUITY ($100).
  2. Side sanity — SL/TP must be on the structurally correct side of entry for the
     stated direction. Malformed trades rejected outright (SL_WRONG_SIDE/TP_WRONG_SIDE).
  3. ATR data quality — ATR/price must fall in ATR_SANITY_BAND (0.005%–10%). Outside
     that band the underlying candle data is untrustworthy; refuses to trade on it
     rather than patching around it (DATA_QUALITY).
  4. Stale price guard — if live price has already consumed > STALE_PRICE_FRAC (50%) of
     the entry→SL distance while Chev deliberated, the R:R he judged no longer exists
     (STALE_PRICE). Calibrated for Chev's ~6-minute deliberation window — see FILL-TIME
     PENDING RE-VALIDATION below for why this alone isn't enough once a trade can sit
     PENDING for hours.
  5. ATR floor — SL distance must be ≥ ATR_FLOOR[trade_type] × ATR. NORMAL: scalp=1.0,
     day=1.2, swing=1.5. EXPLORATION: scalp=0.6, day=0.7, swing=1.0 — see EXPLORATION_MODE
     LINKAGE below. Fixable: Chev can widen SL or reclassify trade_type on one retry.
  6. Risk clamp by grade — Chev's risk_pct is clamped into RISK_BANDS by setup grade:
     B=0.5–1.0%, A=1.0–1.75%, A+=1.75–2.5%. NOT mode-dependent — same in both profiles.
  7. Cost model — round-trip cost expressed in R-multiples must stay under
     MAX_COST_R[trade_type] — a stop too tight lets fees eat the trade alive (COST_GATE).
     NORMAL: scalp=0.20, day=0.25, swing=0.30. EXPLORATION: scalp=0.35, day=0.40, swing=0.45.
  8. Net R:R — EV-AWARE as of 2026-07-05 (see NET_RR: EV-BASED REDESIGN below), not a flat
     floor. Fixable via TP/SL revision (NET_RR).
  9. Size — notional = risk_usd ÷ stop_pct.
  10. Leverage derivation — leverage is a CONSEQUENCE, never Chev's choice: derived from
      margin budget (MAX_MARGIN_PCT=10% of equity per trade) and capped by
      LEV_CAPS (crypto 10x scalp/day, 5x swing; forex/stock 5x scalp/day, 2x swing).
      If the cap is hit, notional is scaled down to stay within the margin budget.
  11. Liquidation gate — stop_pct must stay under LIQ_SAFETY (50%) ÷ leverage; leverage
      is stepped down automatically first, only rejects (LIQUIDATION) if no leverage in
      range resolves it.
  12. Portfolio heat cap — sum of risk_pct across ALL open+pending trades must not
      exceed MAX_TOTAL_HEAT. NORMAL=8.0, EXPLORATION=25.0 (superseded 2026-07-05 — see
      EXPLORATION_MODE LINKAGE below; this used to be a manual override you had to
      remember to revert, now it flips automatically with the mode). Only ever gates NEW
      proposals — never retroactively re-checks trades already open when it changed (HEAT_CAP).
  13. Correlation cap — max same-direction positions in the correlated crypto set
      (_CRYPTO_CORR_SYMBOLS). NORMAL=2, EXPLORATION=3 (CORR_CAP).
  14. Concurrency cap — max open/pending per trade_type at once. NORMAL: scalp=1, day=2,
      swing=2. EXPLORATION: scalp=2, day=3, swing=3 (CONCURRENCY).

NET_RR: EV-BASED REDESIGN (2026-07-05):
Kev built Risk Gauntlet specifically to avoid hardcoded R:R rules ("that's amateur") — but
gate 8 (NET_RR) originally WAS exactly that: a flat MIN_NET_RR[trade_type] floor
(scalp=2.0, day=1.8, swing=2.5), rejected regardless of setup quality. This was found the
same session Chev independently cited "Required R:R of at least 2.0:1" as his own SKIP
reasoning on an AVAXUSDT/30m setup — not something anywhere in Chev Prompt tells him;
almost certainly Chev generalizing from a prior in-thread RISK GAUNTLET REJECT (NET_RR)
retry-bounce message (see below — that message is the one place a gauntlet reject reason
is ever shown to Chev) onto a fresh, unrelated symbol.

Root cause: a flat R:R floor can't be correct for both a setup type that wins 60% of the
time and one that wins 15% of the time. Fixed by making the requirement win-rate-aware:

  - compute_tag_win_rates(closed_trades) — new pure function (no I/O, no dexter.py
    imports, same purity constraint as the rest of this module). Takes the list from
    _load_journal() (chev_journal.json), returns {tag: {n, wins, win_rate}} per individual
    confluence tag. Strips the literal " manual-close" suffix some entries have appended
    directly onto the tags string (not a real tag) before splitting on commas.
  - run_gauntlet() gained a tag_stats=None parameter. For each tag on the trade with
    >= MIN_SAMPLES_FOR_EV (10) closed WIN/LOSS samples, look up its win rate. Among those,
    take the WEAKEST (lowest win rate) — same "weakest link, not average" principle
    already in Chev's own prompt — and require:
        required_rr = max(breakeven_rr * EV_SAFETY_MARGIN, ABS_MIN_RR[trade_type])
        breakeven_rr = (1 - win_rate) / win_rate
    EV_SAFETY_MARGIN = 1.15 (15% cushion above pure breakeven — win-rate estimates from a
    finite sample are noisy). ABS_MIN_RR (scalp/day=1.1, swing=1.3) is a floor under the
    floor — a small/noisy sample reading a very high win rate still can't approve a
    near-1:1 trade.
  - FALLBACK: if no tag on the trade has >= 10 samples yet, falls straight back to the
    original flat MIN_NET_RR[trade_type] — unchanged behavior. Early on, and for any new
    or rare tag, this is what actually fires. The EV path only activates where real data
    already supports it, tag by tag, not as an all-or-nothing switch.
  - dexter.py wires this by computing tag_stats = risk_gauntlet.compute_tag_win_rates(
    _load_journal()) fresh at both the initial and the one-retry run_gauntlet() call sites
    (main escalation loop, ~line 9390 and ~9412). Recomputed from the small local journal
    file each time rather than cached — the file is tiny (73 closed trades as of
    2026-07-05), parsing it is microseconds, not worth a cache layer yet.

Sanity-checked against the actual 73-trade journal on 2026-07-05 (day trade_type):
  cp          n=11  win_rate= 9.1%  -> requires 11.50:1  (was flat 1.8 — way too lenient)
  ema_21/13   n=13  win_rate=23.1%  -> requires  3.83:1
  sr_4h       n=33  win_rate=27.3%  -> requires  3.07:1
  fib_1h      n=34  win_rate=29.4%  -> requires  2.76:1
  dv          n=53  win_rate=34.0%  -> requires  2.24:1
  rsi/ema_55  n=13-18 win_rate~38-39% -> requires ~1.8:1 (close to old flat floor)
  sr/ema      n=26/14 win_rate~42-43% -> requires ~1.5-1.6:1
  ema_1h      n=11  win_rate=45.5%  -> requires  1.38:1  (was flat 1.8 — too strict)
Confirms the core problem the redesign fixes: the old flat 1.8 was simultaneously too
lenient for your worst-performing tag (cp) and too strict for your best (ema_1h).

Only individual-tag granularity has enough samples yet — exact multi-tag COMBINATION win
rates are almost all n=1-2 (one exception: "sr,fib,rsi" at n=12). single-tag weakest-link
remains the gate's real EV mechanism for this reason. UPDATE (2026-07-05, later same day):
this is now TRACKED, just not yet GATED on — `compute_combo_win_rates(closed_trades,
min_tags=2)` (added next to compute_tag_win_rates) computes the same win_rate/n stats keyed
on the full sorted tag combination instead of one tag at a time, and is surfaced on the
Strategy dashboard's Performance tab (dimmed below n=5 in the UI) so the data is visible
and growing rather than invisible until "someday it's ready." Revisit folding this into the
NET_RR gate itself once real combinations accumulate enough samples — not done yet,
deliberately, same reasoning as always: don't gate on statistics you don't trust yet.

risk_gauntlet.py self-test grew from 13 to 17 cases covering this: EV allowing a pass below
the old flat floor on a strong tag, EV rejecting above the old flat floor on a weak tag,
weakest-link selection across a mixed strong+weak tag trade, and confirming the thin-sample
fallback still behaves exactly like the pre-redesign flat gate.

EXPLORATION_MODE LINKAGE (2026-07-05, later same day): Kev's own concern — "we have a lot
of moving parts... otherwise I will have to spend most of my time figuring out why it's not
working" — after the earlier MAX_TOTAL_HEAT 8→25 change was a one-off MANUAL edit with a
"remember to revert before real money" comment. That's exactly the kind of scattered,
easy-to-forget knob Kev wanted eliminated. Fixed by restructuring every SETUP-QUALITY
constant (not account-safety constants — see below) into two named profiles, `_NORMAL` and
`_EXPLORATION`, sitting together at the top of risk_gauntlet.py:

  ATR_FLOOR:         NORMAL {scalp:1.0, day:1.2, swing:1.5}  | EXPLORATION {0.6, 0.7, 1.0}
  MAX_COST_R:        NORMAL {scalp:0.20, day:0.25, swing:0.30} | EXPLORATION {0.35, 0.40, 0.45}
  MIN_NET_RR (flat): NORMAL {scalp:2.0, day:1.8, swing:2.5}  | EXPLORATION {1.3, 1.2, 1.6}
  ABS_MIN_RR:        NORMAL {scalp:1.1, day:1.1, swing:1.3}  | EXPLORATION {0.8, 0.8, 1.0}
  MAX_TOTAL_HEAT:    NORMAL 8.0                              | EXPLORATION 25.0
  MAX_CORR_SAME_DIR: NORMAL 2                                | EXPLORATION 3
  CONCURRENCY_CAP:   NORMAL {scalp:1, day:2, swing:2}        | EXPLORATION {2, 3, 3}

`run_gauntlet()` gained an `exploration_mode=False` parameter; at the top of the function
`prof = _EXPLORATION if exploration_mode else _NORMAL`, and every gate above reads its
threshold from `prof[...]` instead of a bare module constant. dexter.py passes
`exploration_mode=EXPLORATION_MODE` at both call sites (initial + the one retry) — so the
SAME flag that already loosens Chev's own subjective judgment gates (maturity/participation/
direction-score, in the escalation message) now ALSO drives the deterministic math gates.
Turn EXPLORATION_MODE off for real money and the whole risk posture reverts in one place —
no more hunting through the file for which constants were manually loosened and forgotten.

Explicitly NOT mode-dependent — account-survival math stays identical regardless of mode,
paper or real: equity floor, side sanity, data quality, stale price, RISK_BANDS, LEV_CAPS,
MAX_MARGIN_PCT, liquidation safety, MIN_SAMPLES_FOR_EV, EV_SAFETY_MARGIN. The reasoning:
setup QUALITY can reasonably flex for faster data collection on a paper account; account
SURVIVAL math (can this position blow up the account) should never flex regardless of intent.

Why this got built: Kev's diagnostic session on 2026-07-05 (Sunday) found Dexter had gone
~3 days without a single POST clearing the gauntlet, mostly because of ATR floor / cost
gate / R:R rejections concentrated during a genuinely quiet, BB-squeeze-heavy weekend
market (18 of 36 escalations checked flagged a squeeze) — EXPLORATION_MODE was already on,
but it wasn't touching the actual bottleneck (the math gates), so turning it on hadn't
helped. This linkage is the direct fix: the SAME toggle Kev already uses now reaches the
part of the pipeline that was actually blocking trades.

risk_gauntlet.py self-test grew from 17 to 21 cases — added a matched pair proving the
toggle itself works: same trade, same portfolio, exploration_mode is the only thing that
differs, and the verdict flips (ATR_FLOOR REJECT → PASS; HEAT_CAP REJECT → PASS).

compute_planned_rr(entry, sl, tp, asset_type, trade_type="day") — added 2026-07-05, same
day as the Strategy dashboard build. Pulls gate 8's exact cost-adjusted net R:R formula out
standalone so anything reporting on CLOSED trades shows Dexter's REAL planned R:R at entry
time, not an approximation. Backstory: the Strategy dashboard's first version derived R
from `pnl ÷ (stop_pct × position_size_usd)` — a legitimate but DIFFERENT number (realized
outcome R-multiple, not what Dexter computed when judging the trade) — Kev caught that this
wasn't "how Dexter does it" and was right to. This function is the fix; the dashboard's
"Planned R:R Distribution" panel uses it now. Caveat worth knowing: chev_journal.json does
not store trade_type on closed entries, so this defaults to "day" — only affects the
funding-cost term for crypto swings, a small effect, but the default is a guess where the
real trade_type wasn't logged. Validated against all 73 real closed trades: range 0.13:1 to
7.63:1 — a believable spread, unlike the old approximation.

Cost constants (shared with honest_sim.py and labeller's cost_R — must stay in sync):
  Fee (per side):      crypto=0.05%  forex=0.015%  stock=0.02%
  Slippage (per side): crypto=0.02%  forex=0.01%   stock=0.02%
  Overnight funding (swing only): 0.06% per side

R multipliers (must match labeller.py R_MULT):
  scalp=1.0×ATR  day=1.2×ATR  swing=1.5×ATR

FILL-TIME PENDING RE-VALIDATION (added 2026-07-05):
run_gauntlet() only ever ran ONCE, at proposal time — built while a pending-order idea
(see TRIGGER-PENDING SETUPS below — drafted, then shelved same session, so it never went
live) was still on the table, since it would have meant trades legitimately sitting
PENDING for hours (up to TRADE_TYPE_EXPIRY_HOURS: 2h scalp / 6h day / 48h swing) instead
of minutes. Kept regardless of that idea's status — pending orders already exist in the
live system (e.g. any limit-style entry Chev proposes away from current price) and the
old stale-price guard (calibrated for a ~6-minute window) was never enough for those by
itself. A second,
narrower re-check now runs at the moment a PENDING order actually fills, inside
check_and_update_open_trades, before status flips to OPEN:
  - Fresh ATR floor: refetches current candles for the trade's own primary_tf (now
    stored on the trade dict, and round-trips correctly through the sheet's metadata
    JSON column on restart) and re-verifies SL distance still clears ATR_FLOOR × the
    FRESH ATR — catches volatility collapsing or spiking since Chev's proposal.
  - Fresh cost/R:R: recomputed using the ACTUAL fill price (which can differ from the
    quoted entry on a gap fill), not the originally quoted one — catches a gap fill
    silently eating most of the R:R.
  - Regime drift: logged only, NOT auto-cancelled — whether a regime flip should kill
    an otherwise-valid pending order was judged too big a call to make unilaterally.
    KNOWN GAP: regime_at_proposal does NOT survive a Dexter restart for a trade still
    PENDING at that point (only primary_tf does) — the drift check just silently no-ops
    for those restart-surviving trades. Safe (non-blocking check), just incomplete.
  - If either hard check fails, the fill is CANCELLED (sheet row marked EXPIRED, reason
    logged) rather than opened blind against stale conditions.

================================================================================
## THE EXAMINER (labeller.py)
================================================================================

C:\ChevTools\labeller.py — Triple-barrier labelling + meta-labelling. 26/26 tests passing.

Purpose: Build a shadow trading record for EVERY setup Dexter encounters (POST, SKIP,
NOT_ESCALATED, REJECT), label each outcome objectively, and measure whether Chev's
judgment adds alpha above the raw Dexter score.

--- SHADOW RECORD LIFECYCLE ---

Stage 1: PENDING — created when Dexter encounters a setup.
  - entry_ref = result["price"] (the confluence zone), NOT current_price.
    Using current_price would collapse the two-stage design (immediate touch).
  - expiry_ts = now + EXPIRY_HOURS[trade_type] from setup time.
  - Waits for price to touch the zone (touch_band = max(0.1%, 0.25×ATR)).
  - If price never touches by expiry → label = NO_FILL (closed as untraded).

Stage 2: ACTIVE — armed when zone is touched.
  - active_expiry_ts = touched_ts + EXPIRY_HOURS[trade_type] from touch time.
  - session_at_touch and regime_at_touch stamped at transition.
  - Barriers armed: upper (profit), lower (loss), upper_2r (+2R target).
  - Long:  upper = entry+1R  lower = entry-1R  upper_2r = entry+2R
  - Short: upper = entry-1R  lower = entry+1R  upper_2r = entry-2R

Labels:
  +1     — profit barrier hit before loss barrier
  -1     — loss barrier hit (or same-candle pessimistic rule fires)
   0     — active_expiry reached without barrier; realized_R = drift (close−entry)/r_dist
  NO_FILL — PENDING expired without touch (never activated)
  VOID    — ACTIVE expiry passed 7+ days ago with no candle data covering the window.
             Honest: we refuse to invent a label when data is unavailable.

Pessimistic same-candle rule: if BOTH barriers hit in the same candle → label=-1.
Rationale: worst-case assumption; eliminates fill-order ambiguity.

hit_2r flag (post-resolution trailing walk):
  Definition: "did price touch +2R before returning to the loss barrier AFTER profit exit?"
  After label=+1 resolves, walk subsequent candles (strictly after profit exit candle):
    - +2R reached before loss barrier → hit_2r=True
    - Loss barrier reached before +2R → hit_2r=False
    - Same candle: both 2R and loss → loss wins, hit_2r=False (pessimism)
    - active_expiry or no subsequent candles → hit_2r=False
  bars_held is frozen at the profit exit candle (trailing walk is post-resolution only).

EXPIRY_HOURS (wall-clock, not bars):
  scalp=2h  day=6h  swing=48h

Deduplication:
  record_setup() skips if an unresolved PENDING record for the same symbol+tf already
  has entry_ref within 0.5×ATR. Prevents 2-minute rescan loop from flooding the shadow
  book with near-identical records for the same persistent zone.

--- DIRECTION SOURCE ---

direction_src = "chev"  — direction came from Chev's TRADE: line (POST decision).
direction_src = "proxy" — direction inferred from zone position:
    result["price"] (zone) < result["current_price"] → zone below price → support → long
    result["price"] > result["current_price"]        → zone above price → resistance → short
    At-level (within 0.05%): regime tiebreak (TRENDING_UP → long, TRENDING_DOWN → short).

CRITICAL: chev and proxy stats are NEVER mixed in any report. Separate buckets always.
This enforces statistical integrity: chev direction reflects Chev's active judgment;
proxy direction reflects a structural baseline. Mixing the two poisons both.

--- DEXTER HOOKS (10 edits applied to dexter.py) ---

1. import labeller  (top of file)
2. _fetch_candles_for_labeller()  — wrapper that converts fetch_candles() output
   to the [{t, o, h, l, c}] format labeller expects; detects asset_type from symbol suffix.
3. labeller.start_resolver_daemon(_fetch_candles_for_labeller) at startup (interval=900s).

Four NOT_ESCALATED hooks (each stamps chev_reason with the block cause):
4. cooldown block    → labeller.record_setup(result, asset_type, "NOT_ESCALATED", {"reason":"cooldown"})
5. event block       → chev_reason="event_block"
6. choppy regime     → chev_reason="choppy_regime"
7. below threshold   → chev_reason="below_threshold"

8. SKIP hook — fires after _log_chev_decision("SKIP"):
   labeller.record_setup(result, asset_type, "SKIP", {"reason": parsed["skip_reason"]})

9. POST hook — fires after _log_chev_decision("POST"):
   labeller.record_setup(result, asset_type, "POST", chev_meta={
       "direction": parsed["direction"], "entry": parsed["entry"],
       "tags": parsed["tags"], "reason": parsed["reasoning"],
       "trade_type": parsed["trade_type"]
   })

10. Syntax check: passed.

--- EFFECTIVE N (overlap weighting) ---

When multiple records share asset_type + direction with overlapping ACTIVE windows,
they are statistically non-independent (same market move affects all of them).
Effective N = sum(1/k) where k = count of overlapping co-directional records.
All report stats use eff_N, not raw_N. This prevents spurious high confidence from
correlated trades made during the same trending move.

--- REPORT FUNCTIONS ---

chev_scoreboard()   — POST vs SKIP expectancy stratified by Dexter score band.
                      Bands: [10-12], [12-14], [14+]. Wilson 95% CI on all win rates.
                      Net expectancy = realized_R - cost_R (round-trip trading cost).

tag_lift_report()   — Per-feature-token lift stats.
                      lift = P(win|token) / P(win overall, base rate).
                      Temporal discovery split: discovery_ts = first epoch where token
                      SIMULTANEOUSLY meets eff_N ≥ 30 AND lift > 1.0 (using running
                      base rate at that point — no lookahead). Persisted in
                      labels_discovery.json once set, never revised.
                      Post-discovery actionable = eff_N ≥ 30 AND CI_lo > post-discovery base rate.

weight_suggestions()  — For tokens with eff_N ≥ 50: INCREASE / DECREASE / KEEP.
                        INCREASE: lift > 1.5 AND CI_lo > base_rate.
                        DECREASE: lift < 0.8.

skip_reason_audit()   — Groups closed records by chev_decision:chev_reason.
                        Shows win rate + Wilson CI + avg_R per gate cause.
                        If NOT_ESCALATED cooldown setups outperform POST → gate is hurting.

fill_rate_report()    — fill_rate = filled / (filled + NO_FILL). VOID excluded from both.

full_report()         — Writes all the above to label_report.txt.

--- CONFIG ---

R_MULT = {scalp:1.0, day:1.2, swing:1.5}    — matches risk_gauntlet.py ATR floors
EXPIRY_HOURS = {scalp:2, day:6, swing:48}
MIN_N_EFF = 30   (discovery threshold; tag lift only shown above this)
MIN_N_WEIGHT = 50  (weight suggestion floor)
Score bands: [10-12], [12-14], [14+]

--- SELF-TEST (26 cases, all must pass) ---

Run: python -X utf8 labeller.py

Tests cover: PENDING expiry→NO_FILL, PENDING→touch→win, loss barrier, pessimistic
same-candle, time expiry→label=0, SHORT barriers (both directions), hit_2r trailing
walk (profit+2R on subsequent candle, loss before 2R), at-level activation,
session_at_touch=PEAK, Wilson CI, PENDING→ACTIVE→expire→label=0 (NOT NO_FILL),
VOID timeout (8+ days past), EMA55 reason → ema55 not sr, forming div → rsi_div_forming,
SR multi/single, profit candle 1 + 2R candle 5 (no loss) → hit_2r=True, profit candle 1
+ loss candle 4 (before 2R) → hit_2r=False.

## CRITICAL RULES (never violate)
================================================================================

- No vision/screenshot chart reading ever. All data from real API calls.
- Chev's tools must actually be CALLED, never narrated or faked.
- No code changes without Kev explicitly asking for them.
- SL for LONG must be numerically below entry. SL for SHORT above entry.
  Dexter hard-rejects SIP-direction violations.
- Risk: 0.5–3% of balance per trade.
- Leverage caps: crypto scalp/day=10x swing=5x. Forex/stock scalp/day=5x swing=2x.
- Dexter is the execution layer. Chev recommends only. Never give Chev order-placement
  tools (no Alpaca/Binance trade execution tools in Open WebUI).
- Always use localhost:8080 (Dexter's Flask). Never 5500 (VS Code Live Server).
- google_credentials.json must stay at C:\ChevTools\ (not in subfolders, never GitHub).
  Share only via WhatsApp/email directly.
- labeller.py direction_src "chev" and "proxy" must NEVER be mixed in any statistic.
- EXPLORATION_MODE (dexter.py) is a deliberate TEMPORARY state, currently True. Don't
  "clean it up" or remove the exploration constants/helper without checking with Kev —
  the phase ends by flipping the boolean, not by deleting the machinery.
- Editing the "Chev Prompt" text file does NOT change Chev's behavior by itself — it
  must be manually pasted into Open WebUI's model system prompt editor every time.
- SUPERSEDED (2026-07-05, later same day): risk_gauntlet.py's setup-quality constants
  (ATR floor, cost gate, R:R, heat cap, correlation cap, concurrency cap) are no longer
  single hardcoded numbers you have to remember to revert — they're two named profiles,
  `_NORMAL` and `_EXPLORATION`, selected automatically by `exploration_mode=EXPLORATION_MODE`
  passed into every run_gauntlet() call. Turning EXPLORATION_MODE off (the one flag,
  same one mentioned above) reverts MAX_TOTAL_HEAT to 8.0 AND everything else in the same
  motion — no more separate manual reminder needed for this specific constant. See
  EXPLORATION_MODE LINKAGE under RISK GAUNTLET above for the full before/after table.
