   Key decisions made and finalised:
   - Two-file JSONL: labels_open.jsonl (open) + labels_closed.jsonl (resolved, append-only)
   - Two-stage PENDING → ACTIVE shadow records
   - threading.Lock on all I/O
   - All timestamps timezone-aware UTC, compared as epoch seconds
   - VOID for unresolvable windows (never estimated) — honest over optimistic
   - config_ver string on every record (future schema migration support)
   - direction_src split: "chev" vs "proxy" — NEVER mixed in statistics
   - NO_FILL only for PENDING records; ACTIVE + expired = label=0 with drift
   - Pessimistic same-candle rule: both barriers same candle → label=-1
   - hit_2r = trailing walk AFTER profit exit, not same-candle check
   - REASON_MAP built against actual dexter scan strings, ordered longest-first
   - Discovery fires on lift criterion (eff_N≥30 AND lift>1.0), not sample size alone
   - Discovery timestamp frozen in labels_discovery.json — never revised
   - Actionable = post-discovery CI lower bound > post-discovery base rate (not 0.50)

================================================================================
## THE HONEST SIMULATOR (honest_sim.py) — ALL 4 STEPS DONE (2026-07-05)
================================================================================

C:\ChevTools\honest_sim.py — candle-true exit simulation, real trading costs, and a
daily circuit breaker. Self-test: 25/25 passing (`python -X utf8 honest_sim.py`).

PURPOSE: today's paper-trade exits are checked against ~2-minute spot polls, which
(a) misses wicks that pierce SL and recover between polls, (b) checks TP before SL when
both were touched (optimistic ambiguity), (c) fills exactly at TP/SL even through gaps,
and (d) — before this build — left one close path (_startup_sl_audit) charging zero fees.
This makes the shadow book (labeller.py, which already grades pessimistically) a fairer
referee than the real trade log, corrupting POST-vs-SKIP comparisons.

CORRECTION TO PRIOR HANDOFF: this build's research found the "MILESTONE PARTIAL TP +
CHEV JUDGMENT" feature (previously listed above as "designed but not built") was ALREADY
LIVE in dexter.py — _ask_chev_partial_tp() and _execute_partial_close() implement exactly
that HOLD/TAKE25/TAKE50/TRAIL_SL flow at trade-type thresholds (scalp=0.7R, day=1.0R,
swing=1.5R). Also already live before this build: cost deduction on most close paths via
_sim_trading_cost(), and r_multiple already computed/journaled in _do_postmortem. The
honest_sim project's real net-new work is narrower than first scoped: candle-true wick/gap
detection for forex+stock (crypto already had a cruder version via _detect_sl_tp_hit),
candle-true PENDING fills for ALL asset types (previously spot-only everywhere), and the
circuit breaker (fully new).

--- STEP 1: honest_sim.py module (done) ---

Public functions: get_exit_candles, check_exit, check_pending_fill, apply_costs,
record_close_R, breaker_status. Config mirrors risk_gauntlet.FEE_SIDE/SLIPPAGE_SIDE/
FUNDING_EST_SWING (imported directly, not duplicated).

THE RULEBOOK (check_exit, applied per-candle in order — this is law, not a heuristic):
  R1 gap-through-SL: candle open already at/beyond SL → exit at OPEN (worse than SL).
  R2 SL touch: checked BEFORE any profit logic — ambiguous candle (both SL+TP touched)
      always resolves SL_HIT (house pessimism).
  R3 partial at 1R: fires once, only if not already partial_done/sip_active and
      orig_tp_rr > 1.05. Same-candle ordering: partial first, then TP if also touched.
  R4 gap-through-TP: open already at/beyond TP → exit at TP exactly (never better).
  R5 TP touch.
  R6 nothing touched → next candle.

check_exit has a THREE-STATE return (all callers must branch on
`result is not None and result["exit_price"] is not None`, never bare dict truthiness,
since a partial-only result is a truthy dict with exit_price/close_type = None):
  None                                    → nothing happened
  {exit_price: None, close_type: None, partial: {...}}  → 1R partial fired, still open
  {exit_price: float, close_type: str, partial: dict|None}  → trade exited

check_pending_fill: STOP-style orders (breakout, chasing the trigger direction) fill at
the candle OPEN if it already gapped past entry (worse than quoted); LIMIT-style orders
(pullback, against the trigger direction) always fill at exactly entry, never better,
even on a favorable gap. The remainder of that same fill candle is then run through
check_exit using its REAL open (not the fill price) — a fill candle can gap you straight
through your stop in the same bar, and that must surface as an exit at the real gap price.

get_exit_candles: returns None on genuine fetch failure (caller falls back to spot logic)
vs [] on a successful fetch with nothing new yet (normal, most cycles — NOT a fallback
trigger). Crypto uses a small dynamic candle count (1m, no scanner equivalent to share a
cache with). Forex/stock request a FIXED 500 candles matching the main scanner's own 15m
fetch depth (tf_fetch_limits in dexter.py) specifically so whichever of the two callers
runs first this cycle populates fetch_candles()'s 60s cache for the other — this only
works because the request SIZE matches; a dynamically-sized request (what was tried first)
almost never matches the scanner's size and would just add a second network call.

--- STEP 2: dexter.py wiring (done) ---

Anchor A: `import honest_sim` added.
New helper _honest_sim_last_check_ts(trade): reads trade["last_exit_check_ts"], else
parses trade["opened_at"] (the reliable UTC string field — see KNOWN BUGS re: open_ts
vs opened_at), else falls back to now-300s. Legacy trades from before this deploy get
bootstrapped automatically, no backfill needed.

Anchor C (PENDING, check_and_update_open_trades): candle fetch failure → byte-identical
spot fallback. Otherwise honest_sim.check_pending_fill decides the fill. Fill price is
now written back into trade["entry"] AND sheet column C (can legitimately differ from the
quoted entry on a stop-style gap fill). If the fill candle also produced an immediate
SL/TP hit, the trade opens and closes in the same cycle.

Anchor B (OPEN, same function): fetch failure → the ENTIRE original spot block (TP/SL
check + legacy 1R auto-partial) runs completely unchanged, still calling
_sim_trading_cost — that swap is Step 3's job, not Step 2's. Otherwise honest_sim.check_exit
decides; a partial executes at the exact 1R price via apply_costs(fraction=0.5) and writes
the same-shaped PARTIAL_1R journal entry as before; a real exit still computes cost via
_sim_trading_cost for now (same reason). The legacy partial block gained one guard clause
(`exit_candles is None and ...`) so it only fires in the fallback branch. Milestones, SIP
transition/ratchet, swing trailing, BOS alerts: untouched, still spot-price-driven, still
unconditional.

Jane (jane_*, check_and_update_jane_trades): zero edits, confirmed untouched — deliberate
control arm on the old rules.

--- STEP 3: cost-call-site replacement (done 2026-07-05) ---

Every remaining _sim_trading_cost() call site replaced with honest_sim.apply_costs():
api_close_trade (force-close endpoint), _execute_partial_close (Chev's TAKE25/TAKE50 and
the new HOLDING-verdict mechanical partial), the spot-fallback and candle-true branches
of the main TP/SL/SIP close, the legacy 1R partial fallback, and CHEV_CLOSE (swing trail
management). _startup_sl_audit — the one real gap found, previously charging ZERO cost on
an offline-SL-breach close — now deducts cost too. `grep _sim_trading_cost dexter.py`
shows only the function definition itself, zero call sites (left defined, orphaned,
deprecated — same convention as _fetch_binance_futures_data).

Found and fixed along the way: partial-close PnL was being accumulated under TWO
different field names depending on which code path fired — trade["partial_pnl"]
(_execute_partial_close, legacy swing fallback) vs trade["partial_net_pnl"] (the two
candle-true partial paths). Neither was ever read back anywhere else in the codebase
(pure write-only fields), so unifying to partial_net_pnl everywhere was a safe, no-op-
for-existing-readers cleanup — necessary because Step 3's record_close_R wiring needs
ONE canonical accumulator to sum partials into the final close's net_pnl.

honest_sim.record_close_R() is centralized inside _do_postmortem — NOT duplicated at
every close site — since every full-close path already threads through it via
`threading.Thread(target=_do_postmortem, ...)`. Computes
`round(pnl + trade.get("partial_net_pnl", 0.0), 2)` as the total realized R for the
circuit breaker. The one path that never calls _do_postmortem — api_close_trade (the
synchronous force-close Flask endpoint) — gets its own explicit record_close_R call.

--- STEP 4: circuit breaker gate (done 2026-07-05) ---

Wired into the main escalation loop, checked first thing inside
`if result and result["count"] >= min_conf:` — before the rate-limit/Chev-health check,
before cooldown. Calls honest_sim.breaker_status(); if halted (today's accumulated
realized R ≤ DAILY_R_HALT = -3.0), shadow-logs labeller NOT_ESCALATED/circuit_breaker and
sends ONE Telegram alert per halted UTC day (module-level `_breaker_alert_sent_date`
guards this — not one alert per scan cycle). A new UTC day auto-clears the halt. Open
trades are completely untouched — the breaker only blocks NEW escalations, never
existing position management.

================================================================================
## LEVEL-HEALTH TRADE MANAGEMENT (dexter.py, replaces the old R-distance milestone, 2026-07-05)
================================================================================

Resolved a real design flaw: the OLD milestone trigger (Chev's partial-TP ask AND the
house 1R auto-partial) fired purely on how far price had travelled (1R), which tells you
nothing about whether the trade is about to stall or punch through. Two trades sitting
at exactly 1R can be in completely opposite situations. Worse, the two mechanisms could
collide on the same cycle for day trades (both keyed to ~1.0R) with nobody having decided
what should happen when they did.

THE FIX — key the management decision off the actual STRENGTH of the level ahead of the
trade, not the distance behind it:

  _score_level_health(symbol, asset_type, tf, level_price, level_kind, df=None)
    Reuses _validate_anchor() — originally built to validate ENTRY anchors (confirmed/
    active/confidence) — against a synthetic anchor built from the level's own price.
    Returns verdict HOLDING (confirmed, confidence≥60, still active) / WEAKENING
    (active but not confirmed, or confidence<60) / BROKEN (anchor["active"] is False).

  _check_level_proximity(trade, current_price)
    Finds the nearest qualifying level within 1.5% ahead of the trade — either the TP
    itself, or a validated SR zone between entry and TP (via _get_levels_for_management,
    below) — and returns its health verdict.

  _get_levels_for_management(symbol, asset_type, tf)
    Fetches all 4 SR timeframes (mirrors scan_pair_tf's own SR block), NOT just the
    trade's single primary_tf — deliberate deviation from a simpler single-TF design,
    because _ca_build_validated_levels() requires multi-TF-confirmed touch data to
    return anything at all; a single-TF version would have silently always returned
    empty SR zones.

Wired into monitor_open_trades, replacing the old milestone-ask block entirely:
  BROKEN     → SL moved to breakeven, trade left to run. No profit taken.
  WEAKENING  → asks Chev, now with the level verdict included in his prompt (0pt visible
               context — see below). His HOLD/TAKE25/TAKE50/TRAIL_SL reply decides.
  HOLDING    → mechanical 50% close (_execute_partial_close) + SL trailed to breakeven.

_ask_chev_partial_tp() gained three new optional kwargs (level_verdict, level_label,
level_price) — when present, a "LEVEL HEALTH CONTEXT" block is inserted into his prompt
explaining what HOLDING/WEAKENING/BROKEN mean, so he's never asked to judge a setup
without knowing why Dexter is asking now.

================================================================================
## FAST INTRADAY STRUCTURAL ANCHORS (dexter.py + labeller.py, added 2026-07-05)
================================================================================

PROBLEM: the struct pre-gate/STRUCT_REJECT (see CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM below) only
recognized multi-touch SR zones and Volume Profile as "structural anchor" — both need
real historical touch volume to validate. On thin/quiet sessions (weekends, overnight),
almost nothing clears sr_score≥2 or vp_score≥2 even when perfectly reasonable intraday
reference points exist. Investigated in a Phase 1 (research-only) pass before any code
was touched — see that investigation for why VWAP and round numbers were explicitly
scoped OUT of this build (VWAP as currently computed is a non-session-reset cumulative
average, not a true session VWAP — would need re-anchoring work first; round numbers
risk making the gate a near no-op if not tightly bounded per asset scale).

Two new anchors added instead — prior-day H/L (already had a dedicated function,
_get_previous_day_hl, just never wired into scan_pair_tf) and opening range (built from
scratch):

  _get_session_context() — refactored to also return session_start_ts: the UTC start of
  the most recently opened currently-active main session (Asian/London/NY). When London
  and NY overlap (13:00–16:00 UTC), NY's later start wins — it's the fresher open.
  Returns None during the dead zone (21:00–00:00 UTC) — single source of truth for
  session boundaries; opening-range logic never re-derives them independently.

  _get_opening_range(df, session_start_ts, num_candles) — first num_candles candles of
  df at/after session_start_ts → {"or_high", "or_low"}. Returns None cleanly (no
  exception, no stale range) if no session is active or the fetched window doesn't
  reach back far enough. num_candles is chosen per primary_tf at the call site
  (_or_candles_by_tf: 5m=12, 15m=4, 30m=2, 1h=1, 4h=1) to approximate ~1 hour after open.

Both wired into scan_pair_tf, right where SR/Fib candidates are gathered for
dist_from_level: each qualifying anchor (within the same 1.5% band used everywhere else
in the pre-gate) is folded into the SAME candidate list that feeds dist_from_level/
nearest_level — deliberately NOT a new vp_score-style distance exemption, since that
would repeat the exact special-case pattern already identified as a wart. A new boolean
result["fast_anchor_pass"] is the only field the gates read. Score treatment: UNLOCK-ONLY
— never touches sr_score/vp_score/total_score/result["count"] (a fast anchor pass widens
what counts as "structural" for the gate; it does not inflate the score every OTHER gate,
including the counter-trend tax, reads). Visible to Chev as a 0pt context reason string
("PDH proximity (0.34% away, 0pt, context)", same pattern as BB squeeze) so he's never
looking at a setup that scored via EMA/Fib/RSI alone with no visible structural mention.

Both the pre-gate (`_sr_pre < 2 and _vp_pre < 2 and not result.get("fast_anchor_pass")`)
and the post-Chev STRUCT_REJECT gate got the IDENTICAL widened condition in the same
change — the two gates read the same sr_score/vp_score fields and must never drift apart
(this is exactly the kind of gate inconsistency the TF_MIN_CONFLUENCE fix below exists to
prevent).

labeller.py REASON_MAP_ORDERED gained 4 new tokens: fast_anchor_pdh, fast_anchor_pdl,
fast_anchor_or_high, fast_anchor_or_low — tested directly against normalize_reasons(),
no collisions with existing patterns.

PDH/PDL DAY-CACHE (added same session, found via a Twelve-Data-budget question): the new
_get_previous_day_hl() call inside scan_pair_tf was hitting fetch_candles' shared 60s
cache, but that TTL is far shorter than the ~24h this value actually needs — every scan
of a symbol (5m crypto scans every 5 min, forex/stock 15m scans every 15 min) was a fresh
cache MISS, meaning up to ~288 unnecessary "1d" fetch attempts/symbol/day for crypto and
roughly 1,000–2,000/day combined for forex+stock (which fall back to Twelve Data, not
free like Binance, if yfinance fails). Fixed with a dedicated _pdhl_cache keyed on
(symbol, asset_type), storing (utc_date_str, result), same per-symbol-cache pattern as
derivs.py — refetches only when the UTC date rolls over. Failures are NOT cached, so a
transient error retries next scan instead of silently blocking that symbol all day.

LIVE VERIFICATION (same-day restart, before the PDH/PDL cache fix landed): confirmed via
labels_open.jsonl that 33+ setups with sr_score=0/vp_score=0 (would have died at
struct_pregate under the old gate) correctly passed on a fast-anchor reason instead, with
zero of them rejected by struct_pregate. Of those, 12 reached Chev; his SKIP reasons were
specific (confirmation timing, invalidation, R:R math) not generic "no structure"
dismissals — an early, positive signal the visibility design is working, though sample
size is small and no POST had happened on this population yet as of that check.

================================================================================
## TRIGGER-PENDING SETUPS — TRIED, REVERTED, KEPT IN RESERVE (2026-07-05)
================================================================================

STATUS: written, then explicitly reverted by Kev the same day, before ever being pasted
into Open WebUI. Documented here as a deliberate idea to have "in the arsenal" — not a
live feature, not a TODO, just a designed-and-shelved option worth remembering if the
current approach (see below) doesn't work out.

DIAGNOSIS (still valid — this part didn't change): pasted terminal logs showed Chev
skipping nearly every escalation. Quantified later against chev_decisions.jsonl over a
4.5-hour window: 93 decisions, 0 POSTs, 72% of all SKIPs citing some form of "lacks
confirmation" ("lacks clear confirmation at the current price level", "insufficient
confirmation candle", "RSI divergence is forming but not yet confirmed", etc.) — one
instruction, not many different objections. Every playbook in "Chev Prompt" said
"Entry: only when TRIGGER fires — not on approach, not on touch." Lowering Dexter's
score threshold did nothing because this isn't at the score/confluence layer at all —
it's a separate, score-independent layer of Chev's own reasoning. Root cause: Dexter
escalates proactively (right as price reaches a zone) while the old rulebook demanded
evidence that could only exist AFTER that moment — a timing mismatch, not a tuning
problem.

THE SHELVED FIX: not to loosen TRIGGER discipline, but to give Chev the third option a
real discretionary trader already has — resting a pending order at the level, instead of
choosing between "enter now" (violates the TRIGGER rule) or "skip forever" (throws away a
setup that just hasn't confirmed yet). The plumbing for this needs ZERO code changes and
still exists, untouched, right now: dexter.py's log_new_trade computes
`entry_trigger_above = entry > current_price_at_creation` automatically — this has been
in the codebase since the very first commit (confirmed via `git log -S`). If Chev's
TRADE: entry price differs from current price, Dexter silently creates a pending order
that only fills once price actually reaches it, bounded automatically by
TRADE_TYPE_EXPIRY_HOURS (2h scalp / 6h day / 48h swing) — no new expiry logic needed if
this is ever revisited. A "TRIGGER-PENDING SETUPS" paragraph teaching Chev this was
option was written and added to "Chev Prompt," then removed the same day (see below)
before it was ever pasted into Open WebUI — so it was never actually tested live.

WHY IT WAS REVERTED, NOT JUST LEFT UNTESTED: Kev's call was to go further, not more
cautious. His view: even a well-explained third option doesn't help if Chev's own
instinct is fundamentally too conservative to ever reach for it — better to test removing
the TRIGGER/candle-confirmation requirement itself first (see the ABSOLUTE RULES / Who
You Are / all three playbooks rewrite, same session) and see if that alone fixes the
near-zero POST rate, rather than layering a workaround on a rule he considers wrong in
the first place. That rewrite is what's actually live now (pending Kev's copy-paste).

IF THIS COMES BACK: watch whether removing the TRIGGER requirement outright over-corrects
— i.e. Chev starts entering on first touch/wick without anything holding first, and entry
quality visibly drops. If so, this shelved pending-order idea is the natural middle
ground: reintroduce SOME confirmation discipline via playbook entry criteria, but pair it
with this mechanism so a not-yet-confirmed setup becomes a resting order instead of a
discarded one. Zero code changes needed to bring it back — it's a "Chev Prompt"-only
addition, and RISK GAUNTLET's FILL-TIME PENDING RE-VALIDATION (built the same session,
still live in dexter.py) already exists to make pending orders that sit for hours safe
regardless of whether this specific prompt paragraph ever comes back.

================================================================================
## THE ACTUAL ROOT CAUSE — HARDCODED CONFIRMATION FIELD IN DEXTER'S OWN MESSAGE
## BUILDER, NOT "CHEV PROMPT" (found + fixed 2026-07-05, hours after the above)
================================================================================

THE REWRITE ABOVE DID NOT WORK. Kev confirmed the rewritten "Chev Prompt" was in fact
pasted into Open WebUI (pasted its live content back verbatim — matched the file exactly).
Despite that, Chev kept citing confirmation-candle language at almost the same rate as
before. Quantified against chev_decisions.jsonl, bucketed hourly: the "lacks confirmation"
share of SKIPs was 42-85% in every hour AFTER the prompt edit (04:33 on 07-05), no better
than the hours before it — and the last POST in the entire log was 2026-07-03 17:00, a
44-hour drought, not the 8 hours Kev first described. The "Chev Prompt" fix, while a
correct and worthwhile cleanup on its own terms, was treating the wrong document.

THE REAL MECHANISM — two separate things, both independent of "Chev Prompt" entirely:

1. dexter.py's escalation MESSAGE BUILDER (the function that constructs the actual text
   sent to Chev for every escalation, ~line 6575 on) hardcoded a MANDATORY confirmation
   requirement that no system-prompt edit could ever touch:
     - Output format required a `CONFIRMATION:` field on every POST, described as "what
       the current candle at the entry level looks like right now."
     - "Dexter will not log the trade without all required fields" — i.e. structurally
       mandatory, not optional guidance.
     - An explicit hard rule: "Do NOT enter just because confluence exists — require
       price action confirmation: a bullish candle close ABOVE the level (for longs), or
       bearish close BELOW (for shorts). Touching a level is not confirmation. A candle
       close through it is."
     - The SKIP menu offered "CONFIRMATION candle" as a ready-made, expected reason.
   A second, near-duplicate message template (a Bollinger-Band-specific escalation path,
   ~line 6700 on) had the identical `CONFIRMATION:` field requirement.
   FIX: `CONFIRMATION:` renamed to `ENTRY BASIS:` in both templates — "the confluence/
   structure already in place that makes this the moment to act," explicitly NOT a candle
   requirement. The hard rule was replaced with the opposite instruction: "Confluence and
   structure ARE the entry basis — once they support the trade, act. Do NOT wait for an
   additional candle to close or a rejection wick to print before entering." The existing
   MODE A (market entry) / MODE B (pending order) choice was KEPT as-is in spirit — that
   mechanism was always legitimately about whether price has reached the zone yet (a real
   distance question), not about candle patterns — but its wording was cleaned of
   "confirms"/"confirmation candle" framing too. `parse_chev_reply()` updated to parse the
   new `ENTRY BASIS:` label (falls back to also accepting the old `CONFIRMATION:` label so
   an in-flight thread that hasn't picked up the new wording yet doesn't lose the field);
   internal storage key stays `"confirmation"` unchanged so the Sheet/journal schema and
   `_do_postmortem`/checkpoint-recall display code didn't need touching, just relabeling.

2. A SEPARATE self-reinforcing feedback loop: `_run_learning_session()` (runs
   automatically every 10 closed trades, all 3 asset types, background thread) asks Chev
   to analyze its own recent losing trades and explicitly write bullet points under the
   heading "SETUPS NEEDING EXTRA CONFIRMATION," with a literal example: "wait for one
   rejection candle close before entering." That output gets saved into
   chev_playbook_{crypto,forex,stocks}.txt / chev_playbook.txt, and `_load_playbook()`
   PREPENDS THE ENTIRE FILE to literally every escalation message Dexter ever sends
   (`context_prefix += "=== YOUR TRADING PLAYBOOK ===\n{playbook_text}"`), regardless of
   what "Chev Prompt" says. Even without that exact heading present at any given moment
   (it only appends when ≥3 recent losses exist that cycle), the base playbook content
   generated by the main rewrite step was independently saturated with "confirmatory
   signals," "confirms directional bias," "trend confirmation" phrasing throughout every
   section — Chev's own default trading-theory bias surfacing when asked open-ended
   questions like "what separates a high-conviction entry from a marginal one."
   FIX: the loss-pattern prompt's heading changed to "STRUCTURAL RISK FACTORS," its
   candle-close example replaced with a structural/confluence-based one, and a hard rule
   added banning "wait for a confirmation candle" recommendations outright. The main
   playbook-rewrite prompt gained the same hard rule. The win/loss-comparison prompt's
   "confirmed" example reworded to "3+ prior touches" to stop modeling the phrasing. The
   FOUR EXISTING playbook files were hand-edited (not regenerated) to swap "confirmatory/
   confirmed/confirms" wording for "aligned/supported" wherever it implied a timing gate,
   including the most direct offender in the legacy chev_playbook.txt Jane's-patterns
   section: "her approach tends to outperform when she waits for additional confirmatory
   price action" → reworded to require more confluence, explicitly NOT waiting on candles.

ALSO FIXED IN "Chev Prompt" ITSELF (missed in the earlier rewrite): the BB NEAR BAND
reading ("Wait. Do not jump in at the first touch. The signal strengthens on a candle
close rejection.") and the VP POC reading's "A candle close through the POC..." framing —
both previously left in deliberately as "legitimate technical nuance," but Kev's renewed,
explicit instruction ("anywhere there is a rule that says Chev needs confirmation... I
want it completely wiped") overrides that earlier judgment call. Both reworded to drop the
candle-close requirement while keeping the underlying technical concept (near-band
proximity, POC break-and-retest) as descriptive data, not a gate.

WHAT WAS DELIBERATELY LEFT ALONE (per Kev's own explicit carve-out — "not the confluence
threshold, not the tools and indicators he has"): `_validate_anchor()`'s internal
confirmation logic (retrospective candle-based validation of whether a detected swing
anchor is real — a pure internal analysis function, never surfaced to Chev as an entry
rule), the `cp` (candle pattern) confluence tag itself, `detect_candlestick_patterns`
output text (e.g. "Inverted Hammer — watch for bullish follow-through confirmation" — a
descriptive tool output, one signal among many, not an entry gate), the zone-dwell
"Context note" (already explicitly says "these are data points, not hard gates... calls
for patience, not a skip"), the repeat-mistake `PATTERN ALERT` warning (demands more
CONFLUENCE on a repeated losing setup — a legitimate risk check, not a candle wait), and
the BB-squeeze / RSI-divergence-quality language (waiting for a squeeze's burst direction
or distinguishing confirmed-vs-forming divergence are real information gaps, not
psychological hesitation).

NOT YET VERIFIED: whether Chev actually starts POSTing now. This requires live
observation after the edits are in effect (no code-side toggle needed — the message
builder change is live in dexter.py immediately, no Open WebUI paste required this time,
since the fix lives in the message DEXTER constructs, not in Chev's system prompt). Watch
chev_decisions.jsonl for POST activity and for the "lacks confirmation" SKIP-reason share
to actually drop, the same way it was quantified above — don't just assume the fix worked.

ROUND 2 (same day, minutes later): Kev pointed out the SKIP reasons weren't only citing
candles — plenty were generic: "The setup lacks clear confirmation at the current price
level," "The setup lacks clear confirmation and is too early," with no candle, RSI, or SR
mentioned at all. Confirmed `ask_chev_to_judge` sends a fresh, stateless single-message
list per escalation (`messages = [{"role": "user", "content": context_prefix + msg}]`,
dexter.py ~line 6739) — no persistent conversation history across escalations, so this
generic phrasing is NOT few-shot mimicry from past turns bleeding through; it's the
model's own default hedging bias resurfacing now that the explicit trigger phrase is gone,
plus a few remaining stray "confirms/confirmed" word choices in the BB section of the
same message (NEAR BAND, MID LINE, SQUEEZE sub-sections — reworded to "supports/aligns").
Since removing trigger phrases alone clearly wasn't sufficient, added a direct, positive
counter-rule to the escalation message itself, right after the MODE A/B section:
"BANNED SKIP LANGUAGE: 'lacks confirmation,' 'needs confirmation,' ... too early,' or any
variant that doesn't name a concrete, checkable factor" — forces WHAT WAS MISSING to name
one of: a specific tool that returned nothing, a specific contradicting 4H fact, a
specific R:R/ATR-floor number, or a specific unplaceable invalidation level. If none of
those apply, the rule states plainly the setup doesn't qualify for a SKIP at all.
Everything RSI/Fib/SR/scoring-related was left untouched per Kev's explicit instruction —
only vague, non-specific hedging language was targeted.

================================================================================
## MISLEADING LOG MESSAGE FIX — "TRADE: line missing/invalid" (dexter.py, 2026-07-05)
================================================================================

Four separate gates — SCORE GATE, STRUCT GATE, MTF TAX, GEOMETRY REJECT — can each null
parsed["trade"] after Chev's reply parsed successfully, and none of them `continue`; all
four fell through to one generic line: "Chev posted but TRADE: line missing/invalid."
That message is only true for a genuinely malformed reply — it was flatly wrong for these
four cases, where the TRADE: line parsed fine and a specific, already-printed gate
rejected it. Looked like two separate problems in the logs (e.g. "MTF TAX rejected: ..."
immediately followed by "TRADE line missing/invalid") when it was one clean rejection.

Fixed by capturing `_trade_originally_parsed = bool(parsed and parsed.get("trade"))`
right after the initial parse, before any gate runs. The final branch now checks this
flag: genuinely-never-parsed keeps the original message; had-a-trade-but-rejected-
upstream now prints "POST rejected upstream (see gate message above) — not logged as a
new trade." No trading behavior changed (cooldown/decision-logging were already correct)
— purely a log-accuracy fix, but a meaningful one given how much diagnosis this session
depended on reading these exact lines correctly.

## WHAT WAS BUILT — THIS SESSION (2026-07-04, continued — escalation pipeline overhaul)
================================================================================

Context: the scoring recalibration (previous session) made the normal threshold so tight
that Dexter escalated hundreds of setups over 10 hours and Chev posted ZERO trades. This
whole run of work fixed the escalation pipeline itself, then built the infrastructure to
run a data-collection phase safely, then closed 6 more bugs found by re-reading the
scoring code end to end.

1. TRADEABILITY PRE-GATE (new, runs before Chev is ever asked) — see CONFLUENCE SCORING
   SYSTEM section above for full detail: trade threshold, struct pre-gate, distance gate
   (now VP-aware), directional conflict gate (_directional_split). All four shadow-logged
   under distinct NOT_ESCALATED reasons.

2. THREE INCONSISTENT THRESHOLD LITERALS UNIFIED — min_score in ask_chev_to_judge,
   min_score in the post-Chev hard score gate, and the raw CONFLUENCE_THRESHOLD_* checks
   all used to compute the threshold slightly differently (one was even missing the
   stock branch entirely, silently falling into the crypto=10 bucket). All three now
   route through _active_thresholds()/the same CONFLUENCE_THRESHOLD_STOCK constant.

3. CHEV'S SCORING RUBRIC REPLACED — Chev's system prompt used to hand him a stale,
   differently-weighted scoring table and tell him to re-count points himself and SKIP if
   under threshold. Since Dexter's score is now authoritative and pre-gates already
   enforce it, the prompt now tells Chev the setup ALREADY PASSED the gate — his job is
   judgment (structure, trend, contradictions, timing), never re-arithmetic. Also added
   ENTRY MODES (confirmation vs pending-limit) so "price hasn't tagged the zone yet" no
   longer produces a bad SKIP — Chev now parks a PENDING order instead.

4. WEEKEND MARKET GATES — is_forex_market_open() added (forex closed Fri 22:00 UTC →
   Sun 22:00 UTC); is_ny_market_hours() now also excludes weekends. Both gate their
   respective scan loops so stocks/forex don't scan against stale closed-market candles.

5. SIX BUG FIXES found re-reading the scoring code (see CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM section
   for the mechanics of each): VP distance-gate false rejection when a setup already has
   a VP anchor; a second, older forming-divergence detector was silently occupying one of
   the two confirmed-divergence scoring slots (removed from the scoring path only — the
   display-only occurrence elsewhere is untouched); SR now scores only the nearer of
   R/S when both are in range; opposing divergences (bull vs bear) can no longer both
   score; BB squeeze demoted to 0pt context; the counter-trend "score ≥13" literal
   unified to the real computed 1.5× number, in both dexter.py's prompt AND all three
   playbook files. A seventh fix (VP respecting the auction anchor's own
   active/confirmed validation stamps) landed in the same pass — see CONFLUENCE SCORING
   SYSTEM section.

6. DERIVATIVES LAYER — derivs.py, see its own section above.

7. TRADE FORENSICS — trade_forensics.py, see its own section above.

8. CHEV_PROMPT ("Chev Prompt" file) OVERHAUL — 5 edits: stripped stale point-value
   annotations from the tag list (Dexter's score is authoritative, tags are for chart
   anchors/learning only); replaced the false "SL automatically moves to breakeven at 1R"
   claim with the real PARTIAL_1R / milestone-checkpoint / SIP mechanics; made the
   Bollinger BURST rule regime-conditional (fade logic only applies in RANGING/weak
   trend — in a CONFIRMED 4H trend price can "walk the band" and fading it is the
   low-probability counter-trend trade); established explicit precedence between
   Dexter's score (decides ELIGIBILITY, already decided) and the survey's letter grade
   (conviction/sizing only, never a veto, and a SKIP on grade alone is no longer valid);
   added an explicit "NO TOOL CALLS during Dexter escalations" rule (everything needed is
   already embedded in the escalation message — calling get_market_survey etc. mid-
   escalation just re-fetches data Chev already has and burns the response window).

9. EXPLORATION MODE — see its own section above. Currently ACTIVE.

10. PLAYBOOK TEXT CORRECTIONS + LEARNING-SESSION GUARDRAILS:
    - Removed a false-confidence "100% win rate" claim and all remaining Bollinger-
      squeeze-as-winner-ingredient mentions from chev_playbook_crypto.txt and the legacy
      chev_playbook.txt (squeeze is 0pt context now, not a confluence).
    - STATISTICAL HONESTY prompt block added to the learning-session generation prompt:
      every win-rate/performance claim must state its sample size; no absolute language
      ("always"/"never"/"100%"/"guaranteed") below n=20; patterns with <10 supporting
      trades must be labeled tentative; only tag codes actually present in the supplied
      journal data may be referenced.
    - _preserve_critical_section() added — the learning session FULLY OVERWRITES each
      playbook file on every rewrite, and its generation prompt never even asked the
      model to reproduce the TRENDING MARKET BEHAVIOUR — CRITICAL section (hand-written,
      must survive every rewrite). This was being silently dropped on every learning
      session. Now: after generation, before write, the existing file's CRITICAL section
      is extracted verbatim (works for both "### heading" and "**heading**" styles) and
      spliced back into the generated text, replacing whatever the model produced there
      (or inserting it if the model omitted it entirely, which it always was). Wrapped so
      a preservation bug logs one line and falls back to the generated text as-is —
      never blocks a learning session from completing.
    - Investigated (not changed): the legacy chev_playbook.txt is frozen but not dead —
      see FILE LOCATIONS section for detail.

VERIFICATION STATUS ACROSS ALL OF THE ABOVE: dexter.py compiles clean throughout every
step; labeller.py's 26/26 self-test re-run and re-passed after every dexter.py-adjacent
change (confirms REASON_MAP tokenization untouched); derivs.py 12/12; trade_forensics.py
19/19. Dexter was NOT restarted at any point during this work — Kev restarts it and
pastes the updated Chev Prompt into Open WebUI himself.

## ARCHITECTURE — DESIGNED BUT NOT YET BUILT
================================================================================

--- REGIME TRANSITION DETECTION ---

Store _prev_regimes = {} per symbol. After each _an_regime() call, compare.
Transition confirmed when ALL THREE hold for 2 consecutive scans:
  a. ADX rising (current ADX > ADX 3 candles ago)
  b. Price closes above range top (or below bottom for downtrend)
  c. Volume > 1.5× 20-period average

Pre-transition fast-scan: when ADX is 20-25 AND rising, scan at 2-minute intervals.
Output: pullback setup alert (NOT a chase signal).

## KNOWN BUGS / GOTCHAS
================================================================================

- client.session.timeout in gspread: NEVER add this. That version of gspread has no
  .session attribute on Client. Adding it causes AttributeError.

- Expo Node version: Node 24 breaks Expo config plugins. Always `nvm use 20` first.

- Dexter's /api/pending: always guard with `if worksheet is None: return jsonify([])`
  before any worksheet.get_all_values() call. Worksheet can be None when Sheets fails.

- Firebase SSE race: RSI div lines (_rsi_div flag) must NEVER be saved to Firebase/
  localStorage. _clearRsiDivOverlay() and _drawRsiDivVisual() must never call
  saveDrawings(). SSE listener must preserve live _rsi_div drawings on update.

- labeller.py: direction_src "chev" and "proxy" must NEVER be mixed in statistics.
  A setup where Chev's direction contradicts the zone proxy is NOT an error — it's
  Chev exercising judgment. Record both; compare separately.

- labeller.py entry_ref for non-POST: always result["price"] (the confluence zone).
  Never result["current_price"] — that would make every record immediately touch-activate.

- Two different "when opened" fields exist on a trade dict: opened_at (a plain UTC
  string, "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S", reliably stamped at creation for every real trade) and
  open_ts (an ISO-format field _sim_trading_cost() reads for crypto-swing funding math,
  but which is basically never populated for real trades — only ever set when loading
  old Jane rows from the sheet). Net effect: crypto swing funding cost has likely been
  silently computing as $0 this whole time. honest_sim keys off opened_at, not open_ts.
  Not fixed as part of the honest_sim build (out of scope) — flagging for whenever it is.

- "Chev Prompt" is the ACTUAL filename — no underscore, no file extension. Task briefs
  and prior conversation sometimes refer to it as "Chev_Prompt" or "chev_prompt.txt";
  those don't exist. Editing the real file changes nothing in Chev's behavior until the
  content is manually pasted into Open WebUI's model system prompt editor.

- _setup_grade()'s min_score must NEVER be routed through _active_thresholds() — it is
  the one deliberate exception to "every gate reads thresholds through the helper".
  Grading always uses the full normal per-asset threshold regardless of EXPLORATION_MODE,
  because the grade (and its suggested risk %) is the actual risk control during the
  exploration phase. If a future edit "fixes" this to be consistent with the other
  threshold call sites, it defeats the entire safety design of exploration mode.

- chev_playbook.txt (no asset suffix, legacy) is frozen but NOT dead: _run_learning_
  session is never called with asset_type=None anymore, so nothing rewrites this file —
  but the Firebase monitor snapshot push and _ask_chev_about_jane_trade() both still read
  it live. Don't assume "no writer" means "safe to delete."

- Duplicate dexter.py launches: happened TWICE this week (both times two processes
  started at the exact same second, confirmed via WMI process query, confirmed NOT
  Flask's reloader since use_reloader=False is hardcoded). There is zero code-level
  protection against this — no lock file, no port-bind check that would fail the second
  instance. Both times it was caught by noticing two processes in Task Manager/WMI, not
  by any in-app signal. Check for this explicitly before trusting escalation volume or
  Sheet data after any restart.

- regime_at_proposal (used by the fill-time pending re-validation's regime-drift log,
  see RISK GAUNTLET above) is NOT reconstructed when a trade is loaded from the Sheet on
  Dexter restart — only primary_tf is. A trade that was PENDING across a restart will
  silently skip the regime-drift log line (safe — it's a non-blocking check — just
  incomplete). Not fixed; low priority since the ATR-floor and cost/R:R re-checks (the
  two that actually block a bad fill) both use primary_tf, which DOES survive a restart.

- The old "TRADE: line missing/invalid" log line used to fire for FOUR different
  situations that have nothing to do with a missing TRADE line (SCORE GATE, STRUCT GATE,
  MTF TAX, and a failed GEOMETRY REJECT revision all nulled parsed["trade"] after a
  perfectly valid parse). Fixed 2026-07-05 — see its own section above. If you see this
  exact message in old logs predating that fix, it does NOT mean Chev's reply was
  malformed; check whichever gate message printed immediately before it instead.

================================================================================
*** VRAM OVERFLOW FIX — "THE SMALLER DESK" (chev-32b-learn + SHORTER
keep_alive) — 2026-07-09 — RESTART: YES (launcher.py build/check changed),
DEPLOY: N/A, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
CONTEXT: VRAM on the 24GB GPU was overflowing and forcing a CPU offload
(massive latency). Root cause: chev-chelios-clone (escalations) and
chev-chelios (learning/chat) BOTH ran the main chev-32b model at num_ctx
12288, which needs a ~3GB KV cache each. Because Dexter pings the clone
frequently, the clone's keep_alive timer never expired, so when a learning
session fired, BOTH KV caches were resident at once: 19GB shared weights +
3GB clone KV + 3GB learn KV = 25GB > 24GB → CPU offload.
KEY VRAM/KV-CACHE FINDINGS:
- Ollama only consumes VRAM while a model is actively loaded. After the
  keep_alive idle window expires, the model UNLOADS COMPLETELY (0 VRAM) —
  it is NOT a permanently reserved block.
- Both brains share the SAME qwen2.5:32b weights (19GB). When either brain
  loads, those weights are mapped once and shared; only the per-model KV
  cache is separate.
- Worst case (both brains resident simultaneously): 19GB weights + 3GB clone
  KV (12288) + 2GB learn KV (8192) = 24GB — fits the card exactly. With the
  shorter timer below, the overlap window is essentially eliminated.
MISCONCEPTION CORRECTED: the 5-minute clone keep_alive was assumed to be the
problem's cause in the sense of "permanently holding VRAM." The real issue is
that it never EXPIRED (frequent pings reset it), so the clone stayed resident
and overlapped the learning session. Fixing it is about SHORTENING the idle
window so the clone unloads before a learning session stacks on top.
THE SMALLER DESK — NEW MODEL chev-32b-learn: created ChevBrain-learn.modelfile
with num_ctx 8192 (KV cache ~2GB instead of ~3GB), num_gpu 99, num_thread 6,
FROM qwen2.5:32b. This is the dedicated learning/chat brain; the clone keeps
the full 12288 chev-32b. Because weights are shared, two brains cost 19GB +
the two smaller KV caches, not 38GB.
ACTION FOR KEV — OPEN WEBUI: change the model keep_alive to 2m (two minutes)
for both brains in Open WebUI (Admin → Models / settings). This lets the
clone unload after 2 minutes of Dexter idleness, so a learning session almost
never finds the clone still resident — no overlap, no CPU offload.
launcher.py CHANGES (verified with py_compile, exit 0):
1. New constants CHEV_BRAIN_LEARN_MODELFILE = r"C:\ChevTools\ChevBrain-learn.
   modelfile" and CHEV_BRAIN_LEARN_NAME = "chev-32b-learn".
2. _build_brain()._do_build() now runs `ollama create` for BOTH chev-32b
   (from ChevBrain.modelfile) AND chev-32b-learn (from ChevBrain-learn.
   modelfile) in one click; its success message tells Kev to point the clone
   at chev-32b and learning at chev-32b-learn, then restart Ollama.
3. _check_brain() now returns True ONLY when BOTH chev-32b and chev-32b-learn
   appear in `ollama list` — this is the function the UI status loop calls
   (self._check_brain() in _status_loop), so the status dot now verifies both
   models exist. The "Chev Brain" service-card description was updated to read
   "(chev-32b + chev-32b-learn)".
VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile launcher.py` exit 0. ChevBrain-learn.
modelfile written at C:\ChevTools\ChevBrain-learn.modelfile.
RESTART: YES — launcher.py's build and existence-check changed, so restart the
launcher to pick them up before clicking "Build Chev Brain." DEPLOY: N/A.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

================================================================================
*** FOLLOW-UP — THREE-HAT REVIEW OF "THE SMALLER DESK" (launcher.py +
dexter.py learning-prompt guard) — 2026-07-09 — RESTART: YES (launcher.py
+ dexter.py changed), DEPLOY: N/A, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
Triggered by a cross-discipline review (software engineer / data analyst /
day trader) of the VRAM fix above. Verdict per hat:
- SWE: code good (rated B, not "mid"). One real robustness bug fixed.
- DATA ANALYST: context distribution is CORRECT — clone keeps 12288 (escalation
  prompt ~9,730 tok in, ~2.5K headroom for the reply); learn drops to 8192
  (heaviest prompt ~3-5K tok in, generous headroom). Shared qwen2.5:32b weights
  mean no VRAM doubling. Both brains have room. One overflow risk guarded.
- DAY TRADER: learning loop is sound (evidence-based, sample-size honesty,
  conditions-not-outcomes). 8192 does not degrade lesson quality. No objection.
FIXES:
1. launcher.py _build_brain() — the original ran both `ollama create` calls in
   one try; if the SECOND failed, the first model was already built but
   _brain_built stayed False, so the next click REBUILT the already-built first
   model (~30s waste) and the failure message didn't name the missing brain.
   Also the already-built message only named chev-32b. New behavior: a
   _ollama_models() helper lists installed models; _do_build builds ONLY the
   missing brain(s) (skips ones already present), sets _brain_built/status True
   only when _check_brain() confirms BOTH exist, and otherwise reports "Build
   incomplete — one brain missing" so a re-click cleanly finishes the job.
   _check_brain() now reuses _ollama_models(). Message names both brains.
2. dexter.py _run_learning_session() _fmt_entry() — the Step-1 playbook-rewrite
   prompt (sent to the 8192-ctx chev-32b-learn brain) built entries_text from up
   to 20 trades with UNTRUNCATED `analysis`. If 20 post-mortems were each very
   long, the prompt could approach 8192 and Ollama would silently truncate the
   trade history, so Chev would learn from a partial record. Now caps each
   trade's `analysis` at 400 chars (same family of bound already used by the
   loss/compare prompts at 300/200). Output playbook is unchanged in structure.
VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile launcher.py dexter.py` exit 0.
RESTART: YES (both files changed). DEPLOY: N/A. RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

================================================================================
*** FOLLOW-UP — LIVE VERIFICATION OF "THE SMALLER DESK" (build + param proof
+ 32768 vram-default clarification) — 2026-07-09 — RESTART: YES (launcher.py
+ dexter.py changed earlier), DEPLOY: N/A, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
WHAT WORKED:
1. `ollama create chev-32b-learn -f C:\ChevTools\ChevBrain-learn.modelfile`
   succeeded (exit 0) — reused the already-local qwen2.5:32b layers, so NO
   19GB re-download. `ollama list` now shows BOTH chev-32b:latest and
   chev-32b-learn:latest (each 19GB, weights shared on disk).
2. `ollama show chev-32b-learn` confirms the Modelfile params took: num_ctx
   8192, num_gpu 99, num_thread 6. So the smaller desk is real, not just
   created.
3. `ChevBrain.modelfile` confirmed to still pin num_ctx 12288 for the clone —
   both brains explicitly pin their context, so Ollama's startup
   "vram-based default context" (default_num_ctx=32768 on the 24GB card)
   NEVER applies to either model. That 32768 is only Ollama's fallback for
   models with no num_ctx set; it is informational, not what these brains use.
4. launcher.py/dexter.py both py_compile clean (exit 0) from the earlier
   three-hat review fixes (build-only-missing-brains logic + the 400-char
   analysis cap on the playbook-rewrite prompt).
WHAT DID NOT WORK / NOT YET DONE (user-side, not code):
- The Open WebUI steps are NOT yet done: pointing chev-chelios-clone →
  chev-32b and chev-chelios → chev-32b-learn, and setting keep_alive=2m on
  both, then restarting Ollama. These are Kev's manual UI actions. Until done,
  the clone and learn connections still run the old routing and the 5-minute
  timer, so the VRAM overlap the fix targets is not yet eliminated in
  practice.
- CAVEAT surfaced: Open WebUI lets you set a per-model num_ctx that OVERRIDES
  the Modelfile. When wiring chev-32b-learn in Open WebUI, num_ctx must be
  left blank (inherits 8192) or set to 8192 — if someone typed 32768 there it
  would win and blow the KV budget. Same check for the clone at 12288.
WHAT IT SOLVES:
- The root VRAM-overflow cause: clone (chev-32b, 12288 → ~3GB KV) and learn
  (chev-32b, 12288 → ~3GB KV) both ran the SAME large context, so when Dexter
  kept the clone resident (frequent pings never let its keep_alive expire) and
  a learning session fired, both 3GB KV caches were live at once: 19GB weights
  + 3GB + 3GB = 25GB > 24GB → forced CPU offload + latency.
- New split: clone stays at 12288 (~3GB KV); learn moves to chev-32b-learn at
  8192 (~2GB KV). Worst case both resident simultaneously = 19GB shared weights
  + 3GB clone KV + 2GB learn KV = 24GB, fitting the card exactly. With the
  planned 2m keep_alive, the clone unloads after 2 min of idleness so overlap
  is rare → no offload, no latency.
- Corrected the misconception: VRAM is only held during an active load; after
  keep_alive expires the model unloads to 0 VRAM. The 5-min timer's real flaw
  was that it never EXPIRED (constant pings), not that it reserved space
  permanently.
HOW IT BENEFITS:
- Shared qwen2.5:32b weights mean two brains cost 19GB + the two smaller KV
  caches, not 38GB — the "smaller desk" is pure KV-cache savings with zero
  quality loss (the learn prompt fits 8192 comfortably; the day-trader review
  confirmed the learning loop stays evidence-based and conditions-not-outcomes).
- Dexter's flow is undisturbed: Open WebUI just calls the model names it's
  pointed at; the second brain loads in ~1-2s on first request after an unload.
- The launcher now builds only the missing brain on re-click and reports
  accurately, and the playbook-rewrite prompt can no longer silently truncate
  its 20-trade history at the 8192 boundary.
RESTART: YES (launcher.py + dexter.py changed earlier). DEPLOY: N/A.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.
NEXT (Kev, manual): in Open WebUI set clone→chev-32b / learn→chev-32b-learn,
set keep_alive=2m on both, leave num_ctx blank (inherits 8192/12288), restart
Ollama, then launch Dexter.

*** VP-ONLY ANCHOR DETECTION + MULTI-TIMEFRAME VP POPUP — 2026-07-11 —
RESTART: YES (dexter.py changed), DEPLOY: YES (webapp changed — push_dashboard.py),
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
CONTEXT: Kev flagged that the Arsenal Volume Profile tool was anchoring wrong —
screenshots showed it landing on a recent mid-range retest dip instead of the true
start of the current range, and separately, an entire OLD price distribution
(78-84) was getting merged into the CURRENT range's (76-79.5) value area after a
decisive, never-retested breakdown between them. Both traced to the same root
cause: VP shared `_detect_auction_anchor()` (the dual-pivot swing detector) with
Fib/SR/VWAP, which is tuned to find "the most recent clean swing" — correct for
Fib, wrong for VP, which needs "the full life of the CURRENT auction."
WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. dexter.py — new `_detect_vp_anchor()` (next to `_detect_auction_anchor`,
   Fib/SR/VWAP untouched). Walks ATR compression -> expansion transitions OLDEST
   to NEWEST (reverse of the existing ATR fallback), and for each candidate tests
   whether the value area (POC/VAH/VAL) from candidate-to-now still statistically
   matches the value area from just the recent window — noise-tolerant (ATR-scaled
   ​tolerance, so an ordinary wick/fakeout can't break the chain, per Kev's explicit
   requirement that the range doesn't have to be perfect). First (oldest) passing
   candidate wins, so VP gets the longest history still provably the same auction.
   SECOND GUARDRAIL (added after Kev caught a real case in his own chart): a
   candidate is now ALSO rejected if the older portion of its window never
   actually overlaps the current value area (a "did it ever come back" check,
   separate from the raw POC/VAH/VAL tolerance test) — this is what distinguishes
   an ordinary sharp move THAT HAPPENED INSIDE a persistent range (should merge)
   from a genuine, un-retraced regime change into a separate distribution (must
   NOT merge). Falls back to the farthest-fractal method if nothing passes.
2. Call sites switched to the new function (verified by reading each site, not
   guessed): /api/analysis/vp (now /api/analysis/vp_stack, see #3), the 4H/1H VP
   text block in _build_rich_market_brief, and the vp_score block in scan_pair_tf
   (Chev's real confluence-scoring gate) — per Kev's explicit choice to fix this
   EVERYWHERE VP is used, not just the chart, so Chev's reasoning and the chart
   always agree. Left untouched (confirmed general/Fib-specific): /api/analysis/
   anchor, Fib's own anchor call (comment there updated — it no longer claims to
   share VP's anchor), and two general "Active Auction Anchor" narrative blocks.
3. Multi-timeframe VP popup — mirrors the existing Fib stack exactly, since VP's
   anchor legitimately differs by timeframe and Kev was tired of changing the
   chart's TF and re-clicking VP to compare. New /api/analysis/vp_stack route
   (15m/1h/4h, same TFS-with-color convention as /api/analysis/fib_stack), new
   #ctpVpBody popup section with per-TF checkboxes, new _fetchAndDrawVpStack()
   replacing the old single-TF _fetchAndDrawVP() in chat.js (renamed the old one's
   naming collision away — rsi-canvas.js has its own unrelated _fetchAndDrawVP()
   for the Radar idea-pill trade overlay, kept on the restored single-TF
   /api/analysis/vp route, untouched).
4. Backend/frontend consistency — /api/analysis/vp[_stack] now also returns
   bin_edges/bin_volumes (previously computed and discarded); the frontend's
   drawing.js no longer recomputes its own histogram from currentCandles
   (computeVP() deleted) — the chart always renders exactly what Dexter computed,
   never a silently-different client-side approximation.
5. Anchor dragging — found and fixed a real gap: hitTest()'s generic-overlay
   exclusion was blocking a VP box's own anchor-drag hit case from ever being
   reached for Dexter-detected (tagged) boxes, so only manually hand-drawn VP-tool
   boxes were ever actually draggable. Fixed the exclusion to let tagged VP boxes
   through to their anchor-only hit test (drawing.js), while separately fixing
   _drawHoverX so tagged boxes still can't be deleted via the generic hover-X
   shortcut (only via the Arsenal button/checkboxes) — dragging an anchor now
   locally recomputes that box's histogram from currentCandles (the one place
   client-side recompute is intentional, since it's a deliberate user override of
   a specific range, not the auto-detected case).
6. Pair-switch reset + a real bug found mid-session: loadDrawings/_syncDrawings
   now strip _vp/_vp_stack-tagged drawings so VP never carries over to a new
   symbol. Found (via Kev's bug report) that the SAME filter, if also applied to
   the PERSISTENT Firebase SSE listener (_subscribeDrawings), wiped out a user's
   own just-added VP box moments after adding it — because saveDrawings() echoes
   back through that same listener. Fixed by only filtering the two one-shot
   load paths, not the live listener, which must trust its own echoes.
VERIFICATION: new test_vp_anchor.py (standalone, no dexter import, same
convention as test_risk_net.py) — 7 scenarios: screenshot-reproduction (anchor
lands at the true breakout, not the dip), noise tolerance (one wick doesn't move
it), multiple-compressions precedence (earliest wins), the regime-change rejection
(an old, abandoned high-price range must NOT merge into a new one after a
never-retraced breakdown), a matching case confirming an ordinary in-range dip
still merges correctly, fallback behavior, and the return-shape contract. ALL
PASS. `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean; `node --check` clean on all touched
JS. Manually walked the exact screenshot scenario that started this — anchor now
lands at the true breakout candle, not the retest dip.
BENEFIT: Volume Profile's POC/VAH/VAL now represent the actual current auction on
every timeframe, not a stale swing pivot borrowed from a tool built for a
different job; Chev's vp_score confluence points and the chart the user watches
are now provably the same numbers; two real interaction bugs (anchors that looked
draggable but weren't, VP vanishing on its own echo) are fixed; comparing
timeframes no longer requires manually re-clicking the tool per TF.
RESTART: YES. DEPLOY: YES (webapp/index.html, webapp/js/*, webapp/css/* all
changed — push_dashboard.py as usual). RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

*** SHADOW-TRADE DIAGNOSTICS: labeller.py COST_R FIX + WEIGHT LAB (CONFLUENCE TAG
WEIGHT PROPOSALS) — 2026-07-11 — RESTART: YES (dexter.py changed), DEPLOY: YES
(webapp changed), RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
CONTEXT: Kev asked to mine the accumulated shadow-trade data (labels_closed.jsonl,
~10k records) for real, actionable edge Dexter's own gates might be missing.
Running the existing counterfactual_report.py surfaced two real problems before
any tag-weighting work could be trusted: (1) the "POST" bucket (Chev's real
trades, re-simulated through the Examiner's shadow lens) showed impossibly large
losses (-4.21R, -3.63R) that turned out to be a cost-model artifact, not real
losses; (2) the raw per-tag leaderboard is fundamentally misleading for
near-ubiquitous tags (ema13/ema21/bb_squeeze appear on nearly every setup, so
their aggregate mostly just measures the whole population's base rate, not their
own marginal effect) — confirmed concretely when gp_sr_combo's raw leaderboard
total (+18.88R, looked like a missed edge) flipped to a significant NEGATIVE
marginal coefficient once fit simultaneously against every other tag.
WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. labeller.py — found and fixed a real formula bug in _compute_cost_R(): cost is
   round-trip fee/slippage divided by stop_pct, where stop_pct comes from a flat
   R_MULT x ATR box; on low-ATR%-relative-to-price instruments (forex swing
   especially) this produced cost_R of 2-3R+ — nonsensical, since risk_gauntlet.py
   hard-caps REAL trade cost at 0.20-0.45R and would never have approved a trade
   that expensive. Added COST_R_CAP = 0.50 and capped the function's return value.
   Historical labels_closed.jsonl records were NOT rewritten (old records keep
   their old values); counterfactual_report.py and weight_proposal.py both apply
   the same cap at READ time instead, so old data self-corrects without a rewrite.
   Verified: the three "largest losers" that looked like -4.21R/-3.63R/-3.46R all
   turned out to be the ordinary capped -1.0R shadow loss, inflated entirely by
   this formula — confirmed by pulling those exact records.
2. counterfactual_report.py — relabeled the misleading "POST — REALITY ANCHOR"
   section to "POST — SHADOW REPLAY (NOT real trade P&L)" with an explicit note
   that real fills/stops/P&L live in chev_journal.json and are NOT what this
   section shows (it's Chev's stated entry re-simulated through the SAME
   mean-reversion-zone-touch box SKIP/NOT_ESCALATED use, which is a structurally
   different, harder test for a real trade's actual entry/direction — confirmed
   by checking that POST's shadow win rate stays much worse than SKIP's even
   within matched asset/trade-type slices). Separately pulled REAL numbers
   directly from chev_journal.json (n=108 usable trades, computed R = pnl /
   (position_size_usd x |entry-sl|/entry), verified against a sample record's
   real pnl first): avg R = -0.12, total = -12.60R, win rate 38% — better than
   the shadow-POST number but still net negative; NOT the "everything's fine"
   result an earlier unverified claim asserted mid-session, which is why this got
   checked directly instead of taken on faith.
3. NEW weight_proposal.py — standalone, read-only, no dexter.py import. Answers
   "what is each confluence tag's MARGINAL contribution to net_R, holding every
   other tag and asset_type/trade_type constant" via Ridge regression (handles
   the heavy tag collinearity far better than plain OLS/groupby) with bootstrap
   95% confidence intervals. Excludes POST from the regression sample entirely
   (see #2 — structurally different population). THIS IS THE EXACT FEATURE
   FLAGGED AS A RISK AND DELIBERATELY NOT BUILT in the CONFLUENCE SCORING SYSTEM
   section above ("brainstorm item 6" — auto-tuning point values from real
   performance needs guardrails against a runaway feedback loop, the same shape
   as the playbook self-reinforcement bug). Built NOW with exactly the three
   guardrails that section specified: (a) MIN_N=30 AND a bootstrap CI that must
   not cross zero before a tag's effect is trusted at all; (b) proposals are
   sign-only, capped at +/-1 point per run regardless of how large the estimated
   effect looks; (c) the script only ever prints a proposal — it never applies
   anything itself. New test_vp_anchor.py-style self-test (`--selftest`, synthetic
   data only): a planted +0.4R tag must come out significant-positive, a
   planted-zero-effect tag must NOT be significant, a huge-effect n=5 tag must be
   dropped by MIN_N before it ever reaches the regression. ALL PASS.
4. NEW "Weight Lab" — turns the text report into an approve-by-hand UI, built in
   four gated phases (recon -> backend loader -> API routes -> frontend), each
   verified before the next began:
   - dexter.py: WEIGHT_OVERRIDES_FILE + _apply_weight_overrides(), called ONCE at
     startup only (deliberately NOT a per-cycle hot-reload like tunables.json — a
     weight change is a bigger behavioral commitment than a tunable). Sums deltas
     per tag, applies to CONFLUENCE_SCORES in place, with a HARD safety clamp
     independent of the UI's own +/-1 cap (defense in depth): a tag's final value
     can never leave [0, 2x its original value + 2]. Unknown tags are ignored
     (never added as a new key) with a logged warning; a malformed file applies
     nothing and startup continues normally. CONFLUENCE_SCORES itself was never
     hand-edited — only this runtime override mechanism was added.
   - New read-only GET /api/weight_proposal (300s cache, same pattern as
     /api/strategy/counterfactual): runs weight_proposal.py's regression
     in-process, gated by its own self-test (serves NO numbers if the checker
     itself is broken — verified by deliberately breaking a planted assertion,
     confirming the API-facing error names exactly which one failed, then
     restoring it), applies a FREEZE-WINDOW rule (only records after the most
     recent approved change are eligible once one exists; needs 200+ fresh
     records before proposing again), and includes an independent raw with/
     without-tag cross-check per proposed tag plus an "agree"/"conflict" flag
     against the regression's sign — a second, cheaper check on the checker.
   - New @require_key POST /api/weight_proposal/approve and /revert: validate
     |delta|==1, tag exists in CONFLUENCE_SCORES, tag was in the last-served
     SIGNIFICANT set (server-side, never client-trusted), no duplicate pending
     entry for the same tag; atomic writes (temp file + os.replace) to
     weight_overrides.json. New read-only GET /api/weight_overrides annotates
     each entry "active" (already applied this run) by comparing against a
     snapshot taken at startup.
   - New Engine-pane "⚖️ Weight Lab" section (webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js, new
     webapp/css/components/weight-lab.css): reuses the exact existing X-Chev-Key
     mechanism (_apiFetch already handles the key prompt/401-reprompt — no second
     auth flow invented), friendlyTag()/tag registry, and the existing toast
     system. Six states (loading/self-test-failed/frozen/pending-restart/
     proposals/nothing-significant); a loud pending-restart banner always shows
     above everything else; conflicting rows get a visible warning badge and a
     muted approve button; every card states plainly "Proposal only. Nothing
     changes until you approve AND restart Dexter."
VERIFICATION: could not use a Flask test client for the new routes (dexter.py
starts live threads at bare module import, no __main__ guard — the same reason
every test_*.py in this project reimplements logic standalone rather than
importing dexter). Instead: standalone reimplementations of every piece of new
logic (loader clamps/unknown-tag/malformed-file, approve/revert validation +
atomic writes, the self-test-gate capture mechanism against a deliberately broken
real assertion) verified against temp files and the real weight_proposal.py; a
full end-to-end chain test feeding a realistic multi-entry approve output
(including a negative-delta floor-clamp case) through the actual loader logic;
@require_key wiring confirmed correct by direct source read (its 401 behavior is
already proven in production by 6 pre-existing routes using the identical
decorator). `python -m py_compile dexter.py` clean; `node --check` clean.
BENEFIT: closes the loop this project's own history flagged as worth having but
too dangerous to build carelessly — real evidence about which confluence tags
carry genuine edge, with the exact guardrails already specified (minimum sample +
significance, hard per-run cap, human-approval-only) rather than a silent
auto-tuner. The cost_R fix stops a measurement artifact from ever again being
mistaken for a real trading result; the POST relabeling stops the exact
misreading that happened mid-session from happening again to someone reading the
report cold.
NEXT (Kev, manual): CURRENT_WEIGHTS in weight_proposal.py is deliberately an
empty placeholder — populating it (or approving via the Weight Lab UI, which
reads live CONFLUENCE_SCORES directly and needs no manual dict) is a TRANSLATION
job, not copy-paste: the labeller's tag vocabulary and CONFLUENCE_SCORES' keys are
different languages that mostly don't string-match (PHASE 16's own note above).
Only map/approve a tag where the underlying mechanic is certain; leave anything
ambiguous unmapped. Also: the current sample is one week of one market regime —
treat a first approval as a hypothesis, not a conviction, and prefer letting a
tag clear the evidence bar across more than one freeze-window before spending the
capped point. Deploy webapp changes via push_dashboard.py, restart Dexter, then
follow the manual checklist (open Engine pane -> confirm Weight Lab loads ->
approve one tag -> confirm the restart banner -> restart -> confirm /api/
tag_registry serves the new value and the banner clears).
RESTART: YES. DEPLOY: YES (webapp/index.html, webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js,
webapp/css/components/weight-lab.css — push_dashboard.py as usual).
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

*** LEARNING-SESSION MODEL ROUTING — DECIDED AGAINST A THIRD MODEL — 2026-07-12 —
RESTART: N/A (no code change beyond a revert), DEPLOY: N/A,
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO — BUT SEE "STANDING REQUIREMENT" BELOW ***
CONTEXT: an audit of Chev/Dexter/Clone communication (2026-07-11) found the
learning-session prompt (playbook rewrite + loss-pattern analysis + win/loss
comparison, all three calls inside _run_learning_session) was running on
chat-Chev (MODEL_ID = "chev-chelios"), whose system prompt alone already
overflows its own context window: "Chev Prompt" measures ~13.9k tokens (chars/4
heuristic) against a confirmed 12,288 num_ctx. Adding the learning prompt's own
worst-case size (~5.8-6.6k tokens, measured via a standalone synthetic
reproduction of _fmt_entry's 20-entry/400-char-cap worst case, no dexter import)
pushes the combined total to roughly 19.7k-20.5k tokens against 12,288 ctx —
guaranteed silent truncation on every learning-session call.
DECIDED AGAINST: a dedicated third Open WebUI model ("chev-learn", chev-32b-learn
base, minimal system prompt) was specced and briefly implemented
(LEARNING_MODEL_ID constant + model_id overrides at all three call sites) as the
fix. Kev rejected it on a two-LLM ceiling / project-partner constraint — the
system runs on exactly two Open WebUI models (chat-Chev and the Clone) by design,
and a third was not something Kev wanted to take on. The revert is clean: all
three calls are back to their prior no-model_id-argument form, the constant is
deleted, py_compile confirmed no reference to it remains anywhere in dexter.py.
DECISION ON RECORD: learning sessions stay on chat-Chev, permanently, by design
— not a temporary state waiting for a model that will get created later.
STANDING REQUIREMENT (this is the part that must survive): the chev-chelios
system prompt pasted into Open WebUI must stay at or under roughly 5k tokens.
This is not a style preference — it is the only thing standing between the
learning session and silent truncation, given the ~6.6k worst-case learning
prompt still has to share a 12,288-token window with whatever system prompt is
live. If "Chev Prompt" ever regrows past that budget (a new section added, an
old one un-trimmed), the learning session silently degrades again with no error,
the same way it already did once. The main-prompt trim (chev_prompt_proposed.txt,
built the same day as this audit, target ~250 lines / ~4k tokens) exists
specifically to create and hold this headroom — it is a load-bearing dependency
of the learning session's correctness now, not a cosmetic cleanup.
CODE STATE: dexter.py's checkpoint reroutes (all three checkpoint types now on
ESCALATION_MODEL_ID, "chev-chelios-clone") and the stock/stocks asset_type
normalization (_norm_asset_type, fixing _load_playbook's PLAYBOOK_PATHS lookup,
_run_learning_session's asset_journal filter, and the ADR gate) are UNCHANGED by
this revert — those were separate, correct fixes and stay in place.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO for this entry specifically — but the pending
chev_prompt_proposed.txt paste (once Phase 3 lands) is now upgraded from "planned
cleanup" to "the fix that keeps this decision safe."

*** TWO-TIER PLAYBOOK MEMORY (DURABLE LESSONS + RECURRENCE) — 2026-07-12 —
RESTART: YES (dexter.py changed), DEPLOY: NO,
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO. RE-PASTE CLONE PROMPT: YES (chev_escalation_prompt_v2.txt,
third and final Clone paste of this whole audit) ***
CONTEXT: closing move of the Chev/Dexter/Clone communication audit. Two real
gaps left in the learning system after everything else in this audit: (1) no
lesson Kev writes could ever survive a rewrite except the one hardcoded
TRENDING section, so there was no way to hand-curate a permanent rule the way
the Weight Lab lets Kev hand-approve a weight; (2) the learning session had no
memory of its OWN past output, so it could rediscover (or contradict) the same
finding every 10 trades with no way to tell a durable pattern from noise.
DESIGN: two-tier memory, mirroring the Weight Lab's propose/approve split.
FAST TIER: the existing auto-rewritten sections, now window-labeled (see
below). DURABLE TIER: a new "### DURABLE LESSONS (HUMAN-CURATED)" section per
playbook that the learning session can READ but can NEVER write — preserved
across every rewrite by the same mechanism that already protected TRENDING
MARKET BEHAVIOUR, generalized to support more than one such section. Promotion
into it is Kev's manual act ONLY, guided by machine-flagged "(recurring)"
markers — auto-promotion was explicitly out of scope and was never built.
WHAT CHANGED (dexter.py):
1. _PRESERVED_SECTION_ANCHORS — a module-level tuple of substring-AND anchor
   pairs (currently DURABLE LESSONS + HUMAN-CURATED, and TRENDING MARKET
   BEHAVIOUR + CRITICAL) replacing the old single-purpose hardcoded check. A
   third preserved section is now a one-line addition. _is_section_heading,
   _extract_section, _strip_preserved_sections, and _preserve_critical_section
   were all generalized to loop over this tuple — proven with a real playbook
   (chev_playbook_crypto.txt's actual TRENDING section spliced byte-identical
   through the new code) plus scratch tests for both-present, DURABLE-only-no-
   TRENDING, and the explicit byte-identical-survival requirement (23 checks
   total, all passing).
2. WINDOW LABELING: every fast-tier section must now open with "Window:
   <oldest ts> -> <newest ts>, n=<count>, regime: <trending/ranging/mixed>" --
   the dates and n are computed in Python from the actual trade batch, only
   the regime word is the model's own judgment. Lessons now say which week's
   weather, not just what the weather was.
3. RECURRENCE: the previous playbook (with BOTH preserved sections stripped --
   not just DURABLE LESSONS, TRENDING is equally human-authored teaching that
   must not be echoed back as a false "derived today" claim) is fed back into
   the prompt as a fenced, rules-bound reference block: re-derive every claim
   from today's data, mark a repeated finding "(recurring)", list anything
   recurring 2+ consecutive rewrites under a PROMOTION CANDIDATES subsection
   addressed to Kev. The model never promotes anything itself.
4. SMART TRUNCATION: the reference block is capped at 1200 chars, but NOT via
   a blind head-slice -- _build_reference_block_text does breadth-first round-
   robin (every section's bullet #1 before any section's #2), because playbook
   sections front-load their strongest claim and a head-slice would have given
   perfect recall of whichever section is written first and zero recall of the
   rest, biasing every "(recurring)" marker toward one section. Proven with a
   maxed-out synthetic playbook (all 9 sections, cap forced to exactly this
   edge) plus a direct contrast showing a naive head-slice of the same text
   would miss 5 of 9 sections.
5. TOKEN BUDGET: shrunk `recent` from asset_journal[-20:] to [-15:] to make
   room for the reference block. Worst-case combined prompt (system + this
   learning prompt) now clears 12,288 ctx with 148 tokens of real headroom
   under the pessimistic chars/3.5 estimate (1,665 under the optimistic
   chars/4). Two named pressure-release valves are in the code comment on
   _REFERENCE_BLOCK_CHAR_CAP if that margin is ever needed back: drop `recent`
   to 14 entries, or shave _fmt_entry's analysis cap from 400 to 350 chars --
   both cost less signal than shrinking the reference block itself, which is
   the piece doing the long-term-learning work.
6. OVERFIT GUARDS added to the prompt: the existing tentative(n<5) rule is
   unchanged; new lines forbid generalizing a pattern beyond the regime named
   in its own window line, and require a rule that contradicts a DURABLE
   LESSON to be flagged as a conflict for Kev rather than silently overridden.
7. LEGACY PLAYBOOK CONSUMERS fixed per caller: _ask_chev_about_jane_trade
   (symbol is in scope) now derives the asset class from Jane's symbol and
   reads the correct asset-specific playbook -- every verdict Chev has given
   on one of Jane's trades until now was judged against the stale, generic,
   pre-split chev_playbook.txt (last real update 2026-07-02), never the actual
   asset-specific file. This matters beyond Jane's trades alone: those
   verdicts feed the cross-analysis advisory-accuracy tracking. _push_to_
   firebase (no symbol/trade in scope, a pure account-wide dashboard snapshot)
   correctly keeps the generic file, with a dated comment explaining why.
8. CLONE PROMPT v2 (prompts/chev_escalation_prompt_v2.txt, 142 lines): adds an
   8-line VOLUME PROFILE RULES block after BOLLINGER BAND RULES -- closes the
   last flagged gap from this whole audit, where the Clone accepted vp_start
   tags without ever being told what POC/VAH/VAL mean. Byte-identical to
   chev_escalation_prompt_proposed.txt everywhere else, confirmed by diff.
OUT OF SCOPE, NEVER BUILT (on the record, not an oversight): auto-promotion to
the durable tier, shadow/simulated data appearing in any playbook, Weight Lab
changes, learning cadence changes. The TP-only checkpoint parser defect found
earlier in this audit is still open and still its own future task.
NEXT (Kev, manual): paste chev_escalation_prompt_v2.txt into the Clone in Open
WebUI (replaces the prompt pasted a few days prior). Restart Dexter -- this
arms the two-tier memory, the round-robin reference, window labels, the Jane
playbook fix, and everything else queued from this audit in one restart. Watch
the next learning trigger: each playbook's fast-tier sections should show the
new Window line; a rewrite or two later, expect the first "(recurring)"
markers and a PROMOTION CANDIDATES note. THE DISCIPLINE THAT MATTERS: don't
rush the first DURABLE LESSONS entry. Let candidates marinate across at least
two windows spanning different regimes (a claim that survived both a trending
week and a ranging week is worth more than five claims from the same regime).
When Kev writes one, write it dated, in his own words -- that section is the
only place in the system where a lesson can live forever, and the only hand
that can put one there is his.
RESTART: YES. DEPLOY: NO. RE-PASTE CLONE PROMPT: YES. RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.
